Tenant isolation is enforced by passing `user.tenant_id` into the service-layer SELECT (RLS catches a bug if the WHERE clause ever drifts). New service helper [`pending_ops.list_pending(session, tenant_id, *, status=None, operation=None, limit=100, offset=0) -> list[PendingBulkOperationModel]`](src/tagpulse/services/pending_bulk_operations.py) wraps the SELECT — pure-async, mirrors the existing `_load` / `create_pending` / `approve` / `reject` signatures so the module surface stays uniform. Tests: 5 route-layer cases in new [`tests/unit/test_bulk_operations_list.py`](tests/unit/test_bulk_operations_list.py) (no-filter default + service-kwarg forwarding, filter passthrough for `status` + `operation` + `limit` + `offset`, invalid-status 422, viewer-role 403, editor-role 200) using the established `FastAPI()` + `app.dependency_overrides[get_current_user, get_session]` + `monkeypatch.setattr(pending_ops, "list_pending", _stub)` pattern from `tests/unit/test_tag_reconciliation.py`. Plus 3 service-layer cases appended to [`tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py`](tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py) that compile the SQL statement via `literal_binds=True` and assert the WHERE / ORDER BY / LIMIT / OFFSET clauses match the contract — no Postgres dependency. `make check` clean: **1367 passed, 1 skipped** (+8 from Sprint 50 close-out's 1359), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. `openapi.json` regenerated (+1 path entry, no schema changes — `PendingBulkOperationResponse` already existed). The C3-era "list endpoint intentionally out of scope" sentence is removed from the route module docstring. **Downstream:** unblocks TagPulse-UI Phase F (admin pending-bulk-operations inbox at `/admin/pending-bulk-operations` per [docs/design/tag-registry-ui.md §7.2](docs/design/tag-registry-ui.md)). Files: `src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py`, `src/tagpulse/services/pending_bulk_operations.py`, `tests/unit/test_bulk_operations_list.py` (new), `tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py`, `openapi.json`.
- **Sprint 51 Phase A — Tag registry UI design doc.** New design doc [docs/design/tag-registry-ui.md](docs/design/tag-registry-ui.md) covering the UI surfaces that turn the Sprint 50 tag registry backend into operator-usable screens — anticipated in [ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md) §"Negative / costs" *("Two new admin workflows (CSV import, transfer) need UI before the registry is operator-usable. Backend can ship first; UI is a separate sprint")*. Covers information architecture (top-level `/tags` nav entry between Assets and Devices; sub-routes for list/detail, import wizard, bulk wizard, transfer flow, three reconciliation views; shared `/admin/pending-bulk-operations` inbox multiplexing all four pending-op kinds via the `pending_bulk_operations.operation` discriminator), per-phase component breakdown (B–F), and the cross-repo PR sequencing contract that pins the [TagPulse-UI](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI) OpenAPI client to the Sprint 50 release tag at sprint kickoff so mid-sprint TagPulse changes can't churn the generated TypeScript client out from under in-flight UI work. **Two design decisions resolved in this doc** (closing the roadmap entry's open items): (1) **`tag_known=NULL` UX policy** — never surface NULL in the `/tags` list (the list is over the `tags` table, which is registry rows, not over `tag_reads`); reads in the brief unclassified window appear nowhere by design, and the `unregistered-reading` reconciliation view filters them out too per Phase E's lag-induced-false-positive avoidance. (2) **Pending-approval inbox lives under `/admin/pending-bulk-operations`, not `/tags`** — it accepts four operation kinds today (`tags.import`, `tags.bulk_patch`, `tags.bulk_retire`, `tag.transfer`) and is designed for future Sprint 51+ device bulk ops to register as one-line additions to a `RENDERERS` dict, not a page rewrite. **Three backend gaps queued for Sprint 51b** (UI-only sprint by construction — backend stays frozen): `GET /tenant/config` should expose `tag_bulk_import_rate_limit` + `tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` so wizards can render accurate limits in step 1 rather than discovering them on submit failure; `GET /tags?import_request_id=<uuid>` filter for the import-success-pane deep link; `GET /tenants?role=admin_in` for the transfer-flow recipient typeahead (avoids the N+1 of `/tenants` + per-tenant role probes). None block UI work — workarounds documented per phase. **Sprint 50 backend remains the contract** for the duration of Sprint 51; any UI-surfaced gap escalates to Sprint 51b on this repo with a coordinated bump of the TagPulse-UI OpenAPI client pin in a single commit. Files: `docs/design/tag-registry-ui.md` (new), `docs/roadmap.md` (Sprint 51 entry).

### Fixed

- **Sprint 50 deploy hotfix — migration 045 reserved-batch-key backfill failed on asyncpg with `AmbiguousParameterError: inconsistent types deduced for parameter $1 (text versus character varying)`.** The dev deploy `tpdev-migrations` job failed at `upgrade 044 -> 045` because the backfill `INSERT … SELECT t.id, 'tag', :key, now(), now() FROM tenants t WHERE NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM labels l WHERE … AND lower(l.key) = lower(:key))` reuses the same `:key` bind in two positions with different inferred types — as a value for the `labels.key VARCHAR` column and inside `lower(:key)` (TEXT-returning). The psycopg2 path used by `make check` happily passes parameters server-side and the conflict never surfaces; asyncpg's `Connection.prepare()` rejects it. Fixed by attaching `.bindparams(sa.bindparam("key", value=key, type_=sa.Text()))` so the parameter type is declared explicitly and asyncpg has no deduction to do. No other Sprint 50 migration reuses a bind across heterogeneous typing sites. Files: `migrations/versions/045_tag_label_namespace.py`.
- **Sprint 50 post-ship audit — close two API-surface gaps in the tag registry ([ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Post-Phase-F audit pass on commit `d776b8a` surfaced two related gaps that the per-phase test suites did not catch because they were holes between modules rather than bugs inside one. **G-1 (reserved label-key namespace was not enforced).** Migration 045's docstring is explicit: *"the labels API rejects user-initiated CREATE / UPDATE / DELETE for any key matching the reserved namespace regardless of entity_type"* — but the labels route layer had no such guard. An admin could (a) `POST /labels {"key": "batch.foo", "entity_type": "asset"}` and succeed because the migration only seeded the reserved keys under `entity_type='tag'` (the labels catalog's per-entity-type uniqueness left the door open under every other entity_type), (b) `DELETE /labels/{id}` against the seeded `(tag, batch)` row and wipe their tenant's batch grouping wholesale, or (c) `PATCH /labels/{id}` against the seeded row and silently mutate the contract-level color. Closed by adding `RESERVED_LABEL_KEYS: frozenset[str]` + `is_reserved_label_key(key)` to [src/tagpulse/services/tags.py](src/tagpulse/services/tags.py) (single source of truth co-located with the ADR-028 helpers it sits next to) and a `_refuse_if_reserved(key)` route-layer guard in [src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py) fired from `create_label`, `update_label` (on the existing row's key — PATCH has no rename surface so the row's stored key is the only thing that can be tampered), and `delete_label` (on the loaded row before any deletion). Refusal is **403 Forbidden** with a JSON `detail` carrying `{"message": "...reserved by ADR 028...", "reserved_keys": [sorted-list]}` — 403 not 409 because the caller has the `admin`/`editor` role, the request is syntactically valid, and the row exists; they are just not permitted to mutate this specific reserved resource. Per-entity *association* endpoints (`POST /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels`) are deliberately NOT guarded: operators must be able to bind `batch=reel-008rT` values to tags via the seeded reserved row — that is the whole point of the reservation. **G-4 (POST /tags/{id}/labels returned 404 "Unknown entity kind").** The labels-route URL → DB `entity_type` mapping `_ENTITY_TYPE_FROM_URL` was never widened when migration 045 added `'tag'` to the labels.entity_type CHECK constraint — so the ADR 028 §"Batches: labels, not a table" flow (operator-facing comment in [src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py) line 225 explicitly says *"batch goes through `POST /tags/{id}/labels` (per ADR 028 OQ 5)"*) returned 404 end-to-end. The seeded `batch.*` rows existed in the catalog, the route accepted them as the body payload — but the URL segment `tags` had nowhere to dispatch. Closed by adding `"tags": "tag"` to the URL map. Both the GET/POST/DELETE per-entity endpoints now resolve correctly for tag-scoped labels. **Audit findings deliberately NOT remediated** — G-2 (no general programmatic tenant-create API exists; `scripts/smoke_setup.py` already seeds the four reserved rows on dev tenant provisioning — purely theoretical until a tenant-create endpoint lands) and G-3 (Phase G validation — registrar-worker integration test, reconciliation Prometheus gauges, live-PG bulk-import/two-person tests; **explicit non-goal** per [ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md) §"Phase G" and [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md) §Sprint 50). Tests: new [tests/unit/test_labels_reserved_keys.py](tests/unit/test_labels_reserved_keys.py) (16 cases across 6 test functions). `TestIsReservedLabelKey` (8 cases) pins the predicate — all four seeded keys reserved, six non-reserved keys (including `Batch` case-sensitive, `batch.foo` exact-match-not-prefix, empty string) pass. Route-layer tests (8 cases) wire `labels_route.router` into a fresh `FastAPI()` with `app.dependency_overrides[get_current_user]` / `[get_current_tenant]` / `[get_session]` and monkeypatch `TimescaleLabelRepository.{get,create,update,delete,find_by_key}` to async stubs that raise `AssertionError` if reached — so a passing test on a reserved key proves the repo was never touched. Parametrized over `entity_type ∈ {"tag", "asset"}` to nail the "regardless of entity_type" clause from migration 045. G-4 test asserts the 404 response payload now carries the label-lookup message (`"Label 'batch' not found for entity_type 'tag'"`) rather than the pre-fix `"Unknown entity kind"` — i.e. the request reaches the post-mapping codepath. `make check` clean: **1351 passed, 1 skipped** (+16 from Phase F's 1335), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. `openapi.json` regenerated — **zero drift** (signatures unchanged; the new 403 path is an error response not declared in `responses={}` so it doesn't surface in the spec — consistent with the existing 403 paths on every other admin-gated route). Files: `src/tagpulse/services/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_reserved_keys.py` (new).

### Added

- **Sprint 50 Phase E — Tag reconciliation reports ([ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 5](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Closes the operator-triage half of ADR 028 §Governance #5: "Scheduled job emitting per-tenant exception views — registered-but-never-read, unread-for-N-days, unregistered EPCs reading, bindings on retired tags." Phase E ships the **read-only HTTP surface** for those three exception views — viewer-role accessible, JSON or CSV — so operators can self-serve the reconciliation queries from their dashboards / spreadsheets / cron-driven ticketing pipelines today. The actual scheduled worker that emits these as per-tenant OTel gauges is **explicitly deferred to Phase G**: the service-layer functions are pure-async over `AsyncSession`, so wiring them to a `tag_reconciliation_worker` that periodically calls each view and records the row count to a gauge is a one-screen module that doesn't need to land alongside the API. New endpoint **`GET /v1/tenants/{slug}/tags/reconciliation/{view}`** accepts `view ∈ {registered-unread, unregistered-reading, bindings-on-retired}` (validated as a `Literal` so unknown views surface as 422 — operators get a real signal on typos instead of a confusing empty list), `?days=N` (1..365, default 30, bounded so an operator can't accidentally `?days=1000000` and force a full-table scan), `?limit=N` (1..1000, default 100 — wider than the 500-cap on other paginated routes because reconciliation operators routinely triage larger batches and the queries are all index-backed), `?offset=N` (>=0, default 0), and `?format=json|csv` (default JSON). `require_role("admin", "editor", "viewer")` — read-only by design, the lowest role tier with API access can pull these reports without operator escalation. CSV branch returns `PlainTextResponse(media_type="text/csv", Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="tags-{view}.csv")` with a fixed column order per view so operators can bind spreadsheet templates to the output without breakage on a future field addition; the `responses={200: {...}}` block declares both content-types in the OpenAPI schema so generated clients pick up both branches. New module [`src/tagpulse/services/tag_reconciliation.py`](src/tagpulse/services/tag_reconciliation.py) (~285 LOC) owns the three SQL queries and the CSV serializer; pure-async, takes only `(session, tenant_id, *, days, limit, offset)` (the `bindings-on-retired` view omits `days` because the underlying invariant is point-in-time, not time-windowed — a stock_items row bound to a retired tag is a defect regardless of when the tag was retired). **`registered-unread`** — operator question "what did I import last quarter that no reader has ever picked up?" — `SELECT * FROM tags WHERE tenant_id=:t AND status IN ('registered','active') AND (last_seen_at IS NULL OR last_seen_at < now() - days)` ordered by `last_seen_at ASC NULLS FIRST, epc_hex ASC` so the never-seen tags surface at the top of the spreadsheet (operators almost always want those before the "seen 90 days ago" tail); status filter includes `active` because the Phase D registrar may have flipped a tag to `active` on its first read months ago and then gone silent. **`unregistered-reading`** — "what EPCs are my readers picking up that aren't in my registry?" the inverse of the canonical ADR 028 governance loop — `SELECT tag_id, MAX(timestamp), COUNT(*) FROM tag_reads WHERE tenant_id=:t AND tag_known=FALSE AND timestamp >= cutoff GROUP BY tag_id ORDER BY MAX(timestamp) DESC` so the most-recently-active unregistered EPCs lead; uses `tag_known=FALSE` (the column Phase D's registrar populates) so the result is what the registrar has actively classified as "EPC not in tags table", not just "no row in tags" — which matters because reads with `tag_known IS NULL` are reads the registrar hasn't yet processed and showing them would surface lag-induced false positives. **`bindings-on-retired`** — "did anyone leave a stock_items row pointing at an EPC I retired?" the soft-asset-side invariant check — `SELECT stock_items.*, tags.* FROM stock_items JOIN tags ON (stock_items.tenant_id=tags.tenant_id AND stock_items.binding_value=tags.epc_hex) WHERE stock_items.tenant_id=:t AND stock_items.binding_kind='epc' AND stock_items.consumed_at IS NULL AND tags.status IN ('retired','defective','transferred_out') ORDER BY tags.updated_at DESC` — `consumed_at IS NULL` is the canonical "active binding" filter on `stock_items` (verified against the model — there is no `unbound_at` column on that table; the `unbound_at` pattern in earlier ADR drafts referred to a separate `asset_tag_bindings` table that was never materialised). Terminal status set is the same one Phase B / D use (`retired`, `defective`, `transferred_out` — `active` and `registered` are explicitly NOT terminal). Result rows are emitted as new Pydantic models in [`src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py): `RegisteredUnreadRow` (tag_id, epc_hex, status, source, first_seen_at, last_seen_at, created_at), `UnregisteredReadingRow` (tag_id, last_seen_at, read_count), `BindingOnRetiredRow` (stock_item_id, epc_hex, product_id, lot_id, stock_item_state, tag_id, tag_status, tag_updated_at). **CSV serializer** (`rows_to_csv(view, rows) -> str`) writes the header row **even on empty results** so spreadsheet consumers that introspect the column set don't break on a zero-row reconciliation pass; uses `csv.writer(buf, lineterminator="\n")` for deterministic Unix-newline output (matches every other text artifact this service emits); datetimes render as ISO 8601 via `str(value)` (`2026-05-23T12:30:45+00:00`); `None` values render as empty cells (not the string `"None"` — would alphabetize wrong in spreadsheet sorts). Header order is part of the CSV contract — adding a column to a row schema is OK, renaming or reordering existing columns is a breaking change for operator-bound spreadsheets. Tests: new [`tests/unit/test_tag_reconciliation.py`](tests/unit/test_tag_reconciliation.py) (12 cases across 2 test classes). `TestRowsToCsv` (5 cases) covers the pure CSV serializer — registered-unread header + row shape including the `,,,` empty-cell rendering for None timestamps, unregistered-reading header on empty result, bindings-on-retired header + row, ISO-8601 datetime rendering with the `read_count` integer cell, and the empty-input-still-emits-header property parametrized over all three views. The route-level tests (7 cases) wire the real `tags.router` into a fresh `FastAPI()` instance with `app.dependency_overrides[get_current_user] = _user` and `app.dependency_overrides[get_session] = _session` (sentinel yielding `object()` — never reaches SQLAlchemy because the three service-layer query functions are monkeypatched to async stubs) following the established `tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py` + `tests/unit/test_assets_route_category_ids.py` pattern. Coverage: registered-unread JSON dispatch verifies the captured `(tenant_id, days, limit, offset)` tuple matches the query string (proves the route forwards the query params unmangled); unregistered-reading CSV export asserts `content-type: text/csv`, `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename=tags-unregistered-reading.csv`, and the body header line; the critical **bindings-on-retired test asserts the route does NOT forward `?days=` to the service function** (the service signature omits the kwarg — would TypeError if the route forwarded it incorrectly); unknown view returns 422 (the Literal validator); `?days=0` returns 422 (the Query bound); `?format=xml` returns 422 (the regex pattern); viewer role permitted on the happy path. The service-layer SQL queries themselves are NOT unit-tested here — the integration suite covering live Postgres is the right home and ships in Phase G alongside the registrar-worker integration test from Phase D. `make check` clean: **1335 passed, 1 skipped** (+12 from Phase D's 1323), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. **Out of scope for Phase E** (deferred): scheduled `tag_reconciliation_worker` emitting per-tenant gauges `tagpulse_tag_reconciliation_{view}_count{tenant_id}` on a cron interval (Phase G — the pure-async service functions are designed for a future worker to call without modification); operator-facing runbook (Phase F — alongside the ADR 028 status flip Proposed → Completed and the gap 2.14 → Done in the design-doc reference matrix); a `?since=ISO8601` filter as an alternative to `?days=N` (YAGNI for now — operators have asked for day-window semantics, not point-in-time; can be added additively without breaking the days param). Files: `src/tagpulse/services/tag_reconciliation.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `tests/unit/test_tag_reconciliation.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 50 Phase D — Tag registrar worker + soft-asset gate ([ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md) §"Hot-path interaction" + §"Soft-asset interaction").** Closes the runtime side of the registry: the only writer of `tag_reads.tag_known` and of `tags.{first_seen_at,last_seen_at,status←active}`, plus the inventory auto-create gate that enforces ADR 028's "soft assets are created only for registered/active EPCs" invariant. **D1 + D2 (worker).** New module [`src/tagpulse/workers/tag_registrar_worker.py`](src/tagpulse/workers/tag_registrar_worker.py) (~330 LOC) drains `tag_reads WHERE tag_known IS NULL` in batches (default 500), classifies each read against the `tags` registry via a **pure** `classify_reads(reads, tags) → _Classification` function (DB-free, fully unit-testable), then bulk-updates the two `tag_known` partitions in one round-trip per truth value and flushes per-tag mutations through the SQLAlchemy unit-of-work. Classifier semantics: read EPC matches a tag with `status ∈ {registered, active}` → `tag_known=TRUE` + (if `status='registered'`) promote to `active` so the registrar is the sole owner of the `registered → active` edge (operator API explicitly excludes this transition per Phase B's `validate_status_transition`); read EPC missing from the registry, in a terminal status (`retired`/`defective`/`transferred_out`), or `epc IS NULL` → `tag_known=FALSE`; cross-tenant matching is impossible because `tags` is keyed on `(tenant_id, epc_hex)` and the fetcher joins per-tenant. `first_seen_at` is populated only when currently NULL (first-ever read wins); `last_seen_at` uses a no-rewind guard (max over batch per tag, only updates when strictly greater than stored value) so out-of-order batches can't move the cursor backward. The classifier emits per-tag `_TagUpdate` records with a no-op skip when nothing changed, which keeps the flush set minimal under steady-state load. **Loop design.** Drain-converge: `run_once()` returns the row count, the outer `_loop()` sleeps `interval_s` (default 1.0 s) only on partial batches (`< batch_size`), so a backlog drains at line rate and steady-state idles at one query per second. SLI target per roadmap risk lock: **p95 lag < 10 s** end-to-end from ingest commit to `tag_known` write. Two new OTel counters in [`src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py`](src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py): `tagpulse_tag_registrar_processed_total{tenant_id}` (reads classified, the denominator for SLI dashboards) and `tagpulse_tag_registrar_promoted_total{tenant_id}` (tags flipped `registered → active`, the headline activity signal — should rise on operator-driven imports and otherwise be near-zero). **D3 (soft-asset gate).** [`src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py`](src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py) `IngestionService.__init__` gains an optional `tag_repo: TimescaleTagRepository | None = None` parameter. In the inventory branch, **before** `_infer_lot_id(...)` is called (i.e. only on the rare first-ever-read-for-an-EPC path that would otherwise auto-create a `stock_items` row), the service looks up the EPC via `self._tag_repo.get_by_epc(tenant_id, normalize_epc_hex(epc))` and returns early if the tag is absent or in a terminal status, bumping a new `tagpulse_stock_item_auto_create_blocked_total{tenant_id}` counter. **Justification for the inline tag-table read in `IngestionService`** (which ADR 028 §"Hot-path interaction" otherwise forbids): the steady-state hot path is `tag_reads INSERT` + `stock_items SELECT` — the gate sits exclusively in the rare "no stock_items row yet" branch, so >99% of reads still touch zero rows in `tags`. The alternative (an eventually-consistent block via the registrar worker) would let unregistered EPCs auto-create soft assets and leave operators reconciling the orphans, which the ADR explicitly calls out as the worse failure mode. Wired into both factory call sites: [`src/tagpulse/api/dependencies.py`](src/tagpulse/api/dependencies.py) and [`src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py`](src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py) now pass `tag_repo=TimescaleTagRepository(session)` to `IngestionService(...)`. **ORM gap fix.** Migration 044 (Phase A) added `tag_reads.tag_known BOOLEAN NULL` to the DB but `TagReadModel` was never updated — caught when the worker module first referenced `TagReadModel.tag_known`. [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py) now declares `tag_known: Mapped[bool | None] = mapped_column(Boolean, nullable=True)` on `TagReadModel` (between `reader_antenna` and `created_at`); `Boolean` added to the SQLAlchemy import list. **App wiring.** [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) imports `TagRegistrarWorker`, adds a `tag_registrar_worker: TagRegistrarWorker | None = None` lifespan slot, instantiates it under `if settings.workers_inline:` after `dwell_worker.start()`, and stops it in the shutdown block. New settings keys in [`src/tagpulse/core/config.py`](src/tagpulse/core/config.py): `tag_registrar_interval_s: float = 1.0` and `tag_registrar_batch_size: int = 500` with docstrings noting the SLI target. **Tests** — new [`tests/unit/test_tag_registrar_worker.py`](tests/unit/test_tag_registrar_worker.py) (15 cases) covers constructor guards (zero batch size, non-positive interval), empty input, D1 classification (active TRUE, registered TRUE + promotion, terminal FALSE parametrized over `retired`/`defective`/`transferred_out`, missing tag FALSE, null EPC FALSE without tag lookup, cross-tenant isolation), and D2 semantics (first_seen_at only-set-when-null, last_seen_at no-rewind, batch-max-timestamp wins, mixed-batch partitioning across active + registered + retired + unknown + null in one classify call). All 15 pass in 1.3 s — the pure-classifier design means no DB fixture is needed for full semantic coverage. `make check` clean: **1323 passed, 1 skipped** (+15 from C5's 1308), `ruff check` and `mypy --strict` both clean. **Out of scope for Phase D** (deferred): integration test driving `run_once()` against a real Postgres (Phase G — fits cleanly alongside the C5 + Phase E reconciliation-report integration tests); dedicated unit test for the soft-asset gate (Phase G — the gate is exercised by the broader suite, explicit coverage lands with reconciliation reports); `tagpulse_tag_registrar_lag_seconds` histogram for the SLI dashboard (Phase G — current counters give numerator + denominator, the histogram is a polish item). **Sprint 50 Phase D closes ADR 028's two largest runtime concerns** — the hot-path-interaction question (the worker, not the ingest path, owns `tag_known` writes) and the soft-asset-interaction question (the inventory auto-create branch now enforces registry ownership). Remaining Sprint 50: Phase E (reconciliation reports), Phase F (docs + ADR status flip Proposed → Completed + gap 2.14 → Done), Phase G (validation). Files: `src/tagpulse/workers/tag_registrar_worker.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py`, `src/tagpulse/core/config.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/dependencies.py`, `src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py`, `tests/unit/test_tag_registrar_worker.py` (new).

- **Sprint 50 Phase C5 — Unified audit log for bulk operations ([ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 7](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Closes the last open clause in ADR 028's governance section: "Every bulk op writes one row to a single `audit_logs` table keyed on `(actor, action, batch, count, request_id)` so a single SQL grep reconstructs operator intent end-to-end without spelunking through `changes` JSONB on multiple action strings." Pre-C5, every C1–C4 bulk-op call site stuffed those discriminators into the existing `audit_logs.changes` JSONB blob — operator queries had to `WHERE changes->>'request_id' = '…'` per action string, which is opaque, untyped, unindexable, and inconsistent across the seven call sites C1–C4 introduced (each one chose its own JSON key names). C5 hoists the five governance discriminators into first-class nullable columns — `request_id UUID`, `batch TEXT`, `count INTEGER` with `CHECK (count IS NULL OR count >= 0)`, `pending_id UUID NULL FK pending_bulk_operations.id ON DELETE SET NULL`, `approved_by UUID NULL FK users.id ON DELETE SET NULL` — keeping the legacy `changes` blob populated in parallel for backward compatibility (dual-write; pre-C5 readers stay green). Two partial indexes on `(tenant_id, request_id) WHERE request_id IS NOT NULL` and `(tenant_id, batch) WHERE batch IS NOT NULL` make per-tenant request-id and batch-grep queries an O(log n) index scan instead of a JSONB sequential scan — the dominant operator-debug pattern post-C1/C2 has been "find every audit row that participated in request X" and "find every operation that touched batch B-001". **Migration [`migrations/versions/048_audit_log_bulk_op_unification.py`](migrations/versions/048_audit_log_bulk_op_unification.py)** adds the five columns + check + two partial indexes + ON DELETE SET NULL FKs (admin/pending churn must not wipe audit history — same rationale as the C3 `pending_bulk_operations.requested_by/decided_by` FK shape). The migration **also bumps `audit_logs.action` from `VARCHAR(20) → VARCHAR(40)`** via `op.alter_column` — initially deferred from C5 prep, then reversed when a grep of migration 012 confirmed the original 20-char limit and C1/C3/C4 actions like `tag.bulk_retire_requested` (25 chars), `tag.bulk_import_requested` (25), `tag.bulk_patch_requested` (24) overflow it; the legacy 10-char actions (`create`, `update`, `decommission`) remain forward-compatible. `downgrade()` reverses the alter_column, drops the FKs, indexes, check, and columns in symmetric order. **ORM** [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py): `AuditLogModel` extended with five `Mapped[…]` columns mirroring the migration; `action` widened to `String(40)`. **Helper API** [`src/tagpulse/core/audit.py`](src/tagpulse/core/audit.py): `AuditLogger.log()` signature gains five keyword-only params — `request_id: UUID | None = None`, `batch: str | None = None`, `count: int | None = None`, `pending_id: UUID | None = None`, `approved_by: UUID | None = None` — threaded into the `AuditLogModel` constructor; existing callers continue to work unchanged (every new kwarg defaults to None, so the legacy 6-arg call shape is forward-compatible — this is what made the 7 C1–C4 call-site updates a one-line-per-site change instead of a refactor). `list_logs()` filter API extended with `request_id: UUID | None = None` and `batch: str | None = None` kwargs (the two columns that have backing partial indexes — `count` and `pending_id`/`approved_by` aren't filterable yet because no operator workflow needs them as primary keys; can be added later when the `GET /admin/audit-logs` UI grows the surface). Dict serialization extended with five new keys (UUID-typed values stringified, `int`/`str` typed values pass through). **Call sites updated (7 across 2 files)**: [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py) — `tag.bulk_import_requested` (Section 7a, +`pending_id`+`count`), `_execute_tag_import` `tag.bulk_imported` (+`request_id`+`count`+`pending_id`+`approved_by`), `tag.bulk_{patch,retire}_requested` (+`pending_id`+`count`+`batch=scope_value if scope_kind == "label_batch" else None`), `_execute_bulk_mutation` `tag.bulk_{patched,retired}` (+`request_id`+`count`+`pending_id`+`approved_by`+`batch`), `tag_transfer.requested` (+`request_id`+`count`). [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py) — `{op}.approved` (+`pending_id`+`approved_by`+`count`+`request_id`), `{op}.rejected` (+`pending_id`+`count`). The `batch` extractor lives at the call site (not in `AuditLogger.log`) because the column is only meaningful when `scope_kind == "label_batch"` — extracting it inside the helper would require leaking scope-kind semantics into the audit-log primitive, which would block the upcoming non-tag bulk ops (Sprint 51+ device bulk ops will have a different scope vocabulary). **Admin endpoint** [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/admin_ops.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/admin_ops.py): `list_audit_logs` accepts two new `Query(default=None)` params — `request_id: UUID | None` and `batch: str | None` — threaded into the `AuditLogger.list_logs()` call so operators can grep the unified shape directly via `GET /admin/audit-logs?request_id=<uuid>` (every audit row from a single bulk op end-to-end: pending creation → approval → execution) or `?batch=B-001` (every operation that ever touched a specific label-batch). **Tests** — new [`tests/unit/test_audit_log_unified.py`](tests/unit/test_audit_log_unified.py) (8 cases across 3 test classes) covers the surface: `TestAuditLoggerLogSignature` (the five new kwargs are accepted and persist into the `AuditLogModel` constructor; defaults are None when omitted; legacy six-arg call shape still works unchanged), `TestListLogsSerialization` (the five new keys appear in the dict returned by `list_logs()`; UUID-typed values stringify; None values stay None), `TestListLogsFilters` (compiled SQL for `list_logs(request_id=X)` includes `audit_logs.request_id = …` with the hex form of the UUID literal, and `list_logs(batch=…)` includes `audit_logs.batch = …`). Uses the established `_FakeSession`/`_FakeResult` pattern from `test_pending_bulk_operations.py` for the filter assertions — compiles statements via SQLAlchemy's `literal_binds=True` against the postgres dialect; no Postgres dependency. `make check` clean: **1308 passed, 1 skipped** (+8 from C4's 1300), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. `openapi.json` regenerated (+37 lines for the two new query params on `/admin/audit-logs`). **Out of scope for C5** (deferred — bookkeeping, not blocking): one-time backfill of pre-C5 audit rows where `changes->>'request_id'` etc. is present (the dual-write makes this a pure cleanup pass that can land any sprint without breaking anything; current grep queries can union `WHERE request_id = X OR changes->>'request_id' = X::text` for the transition); admin UI for batch/request-id filtering on the audit-log surface (a Sprint 51 deliverable once the operator workflow patterns settle); usage-meter `audit_logs_written_total` counter labelled by `action` (deferred to the Sprint 50 governance-section close-out commit alongside the ADR 028 status flip Proposed → Completed). **Closes Sprint 50 Phase C end-to-end** — C1 (bulk CSV import), C2 (dry-run + confirmation tokens), C3 (two-person rule + `pending_bulk_operations`), C4 (scope-required filters on bulk PATCH/retire), C5 (unified audit log) collectively implement all 7 ADR 028 §Governance rules; remaining Sprint 50 work is Phase D (registrar worker) + Phase E (reconciliation reports) + Phase F (docs + ADR status flip + gap 2.14 → Done) + Phase G (validation). Files: `migrations/versions/048_audit_log_bulk_op_unification.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/core/audit.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/admin_ops.py`, `tests/unit/test_audit_log_unified.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 50 Phase C4 — Scope-required filters on bulk PATCH / bulk retire ([ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 3](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Closes the loop ADR 028 §Governance #3 left for C4: "Bulk `PATCH` and bulk retire **must** carry either `labels[batch]=<value>` or `epc_list[]` with `len ≤ 1000`. There is deliberately no 'PATCH all tags in tenant' surface." Two new endpoints, both wired through the C1 8 MiB / per-hour rate-limit substrate is *not* applied here — the 1000-EPC schema cap + the C3 two-person threshold + the scope-required filter are the blast-radius controls; the per-hour limiter was for cheap-to-submit CSVs, while a PATCH already costs the operator one EPC enumeration per row. **`POST /tags/bulk-patch`** (admin + editor) accepts `{scope, status?, metadata?}` with at-least-one-mutation enforced at the schema layer (`TagBulkPatchRequest._at_least_one_mutation`); `metadata` is a **full replace, not deep-merge** (matches the single-row PATCH semantics on `/tags/{id}` and avoids the "I cleared the field but my replace re-added the old keys" footgun). **`POST /tags/bulk-retire`** (admin only — more defensible default than single-row PATCH because retire is terminal and "retire all batch B" is a higher-blast-radius op than "set defective on EPCs I just hand-typed") accepts `{scope, reason?}` with `reason` capped at 500 chars and emitted into the audit-log payload when set. Method is `POST` not `PATCH` because PATCH-with-a-scope-body is non-idiomatic; "execute a scoped mutation" is the standard POST shape. **Scope contract** (`TagBulkScope` validator): exactly one of `{labels: {batch: "...", [other keys...]}, epc_list: [1..1000 normalized EPCs]}`; the `batch` key is *required* when `labels` is set (other label keys may ride along but the migration query only filters on `batch`); empty `batch` value rejected; `epc_list` validated per-entry against the canonical `_EPC_HEX_PATTERN` with dedup-on-construction. Per-request enumeration capped at **1000** via `Field(max_length=1000)` — matches the C3 transfer-request shape so the operator UI can reuse one rate-limit string. **Dry-run / confirm shape mirrors C2 import** — `?dry_run=true` runs full scope resolution + per-row `validate_status_transition` checks (skipped when `status` is None — metadata-only patch needs no transition check) + returns `TagBulkOperationResult(matched=N, updated=0, dry_run=True, sample=[first-10-EPCs], token=<mint>, expires_in=900)`; subsequent `POST .../bulk-patch?confirm=<token>` re-runs the same scope resolution, asserts the C2 content hash matches (so a batch that gained/lost members between dry-run and confirm fails with `content_mismatch` 409, never silently widens), and commits via the shared `_execute_bulk_mutation` helper. Mutual exclusion + at-least-one-of for `dry_run` / `confirm` enforced identically to C2 (400 with reason). **Empty-scope policy is 422, not silent no-op** — operators get a real signal in `TagBulkRowError(epc_hex="", error="scope matched no tags")` so a typo'd batch label can't masquerade as success. **Two-person rule reuse** — when `len(matched_rows) >= tenant.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold`, the route calls `pending_ops.create_pending(operation="tags.bulk_patch" | "tags.bulk_retire", ...)` instead of executing; returns 202 with `requires_approval=True, pending_id=<uuid>`. No new migration — C3's `tenants.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` column already covers all tag bulk ops by name. **Approve-path tamper guard re-targets the exact set the requester previewed**, not a fresh label query: the stored payload includes `resolved_epcs: [sorted-list]` so when batch B-001 grows by 50 tags between submit and approve, the approval applies only to the EPCs that were in the matched set at submit time. The new `_bulk_payload_content_hash(payload)` recomputes the C2-compatible hash from `resolved_epcs` + `status` + `metadata` + `metadata_set` so the C3 approve handler's content-hash check catches both DB tampering AND label-membership drift; `bulk_operations.py` now dispatches the hasher via a new `_CONTENT_HASHERS` map keyed by `row.operation` (`{"tags.import": import_payload_content_hash, "tags.bulk_patch": bulk_mutation_payload_content_hash, "tags.bulk_retire": bulk_mutation_payload_content_hash}`) so adding a future bulk op is one dict entry, not another approve-handler branch. Unknown operation → 409 via `_resolve_content_hasher`. **`metadata_set` distinguishes "don't touch metadata" from "explicitly set to NULL"** — tracked via `body.model_fields_set` in the route, threaded into the content hash, the stored payload, and the repo `bulk_apply(metadata_set=...)` parameter; a hash collision between these two semantically distinct intents would let an operator preview "leave metadata alone" and confirm "clear all metadata to NULL", which is exactly the kind of confirmation-token bypass C2 exists to prevent. **Repository surface** — two new methods on [`TimescaleTagRepository`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py): `resolve_bulk_scope(tenant_id, *, batch_label=None, epc_list=None) -> list[TagModel]` (XOR-validated; for `batch_label` runs a SQLAlchemy `exists()` subquery joining `entity_labels` + `labels` on `key='batch'` + value; for `epc_list` uses `TagModel.epc_hex.in_(epc_list)`; orders by `epc_hex.asc()` for deterministic per-tenant snapshots in the audit log) and `bulk_apply(rows, *, status=None, metadata=None, metadata_set=False) -> int` (mutates pre-resolved rows in place + single `session.flush()`; `metadata_set` controls write-vs-skip on the metadata column). **Audit shape** — four new action strings: `tag.bulk_patch_requested` / `tag.bulk_patched` and `tag.bulk_retire_requested` / `tag.bulk_retired`, matching C1's `tag.bulk_import_requested` / `tag.bulk_imported` pairing so a single audit-log grep distinguishes "above-threshold submit" from "actually executed" for every bulk op; payload includes `{scope_kind, scope_value, matched, updated, target_status, metadata_set, request_id, [approved_by, pending_id]}` so the C5 unified shape can hoist these into top-level columns without touching the call sites. **Executor registration** — `pending_ops.register_executor("tags.bulk_patch", _bulk_mutation_executor)` and the same for `tags.bulk_retire` at route-import time; one shared executor handles both because the approve-path logic is identical (decode JSON payload → re-resolve via `repo.resolve_bulk_scope(tenant_id, epc_list=resolved_epcs)` → delegate to `_execute_bulk_mutation`); the executor picks the audit action by inspecting `row.operation`. Tests: new file [`tests/unit/test_tags_bulk_mutate.py`](tests/unit/test_tags_bulk_mutate.py) (38 cases across 9 test classes) covers `TagBulkScope` validation (neither / both / labels-without-batch / empty-batch / oversize / bad-hex / lowercase / duplicate — 10 cases pinning every schema-layer 422), `TagBulkPatchRequest` + `TagBulkRetireRequest` (at-least-one-mutation, invalid status, reason length), `_bulk_mutation_content_hash` determinism + sensitivity (epc-order-insensitive, status / metadata / metadata_set sensitivity, the critical "metadata_set distinguishes unset from null" property, metadata key-order insensitive), `_normalize_scope` (epc passthrough, labels passthrough, post-normalize duplicate raises 400), `_validate_transitions` (None target skips, all-valid empty, invalid surfaces per-row error including `transferred_out → retired` which is the canonical terminal-state guard), the serialize → re-hash round-trip in both `label_batch` and `epc_list` shapes (proves the C3 approve-path tamper guard's hash equals the C4 dry-run mint hash), the executor registry sanity (both new ops registered, with `importlib.reload(tags_route)` in an autouse fixture to isolate from sibling tests that call `pending_ops.reset_executors`), and `TagBulkOperationResult` shape (empty defaults, dry-run branch, pending branch). `make check` clean: **1300 passed, 1 skipped** (+38 from C3's 1263), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. `openapi.json` regenerated (+373 lines for the two new endpoints + new schemas `TagBulkScope`, `TagBulkPatchRequest`, `TagBulkRetireRequest`, `TagBulkRowError`, `TagBulkOperationResult`). **Out of scope for C4** (lands as C5): unified audit-log shape keyed on `(actor, action, batch, count, request_id)` with `pending_id` / `approved_by` hoisted to top-level columns; scheduled read-only reconciliation reports (ADR 028 §Governance #5). Files: `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_tags_bulk_mutate.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

 — Two-person rule above tenant-configurable threshold ([ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 4](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Closes the loop ADR 028 §Governance #4 left for C3: "Bulk ops over the threshold create a `pending` request that a second admin must approve before it executes. Transfers already model this via `tag_transfers.status`; generalise the pattern." `POST /v1/tenants/{slug}/tags/import` with row-count `>= tenant.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` (default **10 000** — encoded as a new tenants column, see migration below) now returns **202 Accepted** with `TagImportResult(rows_created=0, rows_skipped=0, dry_run=False, requires_approval=True, pending_id=<uuid>, token=<consumed-c2-token>, sample=[...])` instead of writing — the second admin then approves via `POST /v1/bulk-operations/{pending_id}/approve` to commit, or rejects via `POST /v1/bulk-operations/{pending_id}/reject` to deny. Generalised across future bulk ops: the new `pending_bulk_operations` table is keyed by an `operation` string (currently only `"tags.import"`; C4 plugs `"tags.bulk_patch"` and `"tags.bulk_retire"` into the same registry without another migration). New migration [`migrations/versions/047_tag_bulk_two_person_threshold.py`](migrations/versions/047_tag_bulk_two_person_threshold.py) adds `tenants.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 10000` (consistent with the C1 `tag_bulk_import_rate_limit` column) and creates `pending_bulk_operations` (`id` UUID PK, `tenant_id` FK CASCADE, `operation` TEXT, `status` TEXT DEFAULT `'pending'` ∈ `{pending, approved, rejected, executed, expired}`, `requested_by`/`decided_by` FK `users.id` ON DELETE SET NULL — admin churn must not wipe audit history, `content_hash` TEXT, `row_count` INT > 0, `sample` JSONB, `payload` BYTEA — raw CSV bytes so the second admin doesn't need to coordinate file transfer; bounded by the C1 8 MiB cap, `request_id` UUID NULL — populated on execution to tie back to `tag.bulk_imported` audit rows, four TIMESTAMPTZ columns, and three CHECK constraints: status enum, `row_count > 0`, and a decided-state invariant — `pending` rows MUST have null decision fields and `approved`/`rejected`/`executed` rows MUST have non-null decision fields; `expired` is permitted either shape because lazy timeout sweeping happens in the service layer not via background job). Index `(tenant_id, status, expires_at)` for the eventual list-pending endpoint and TTL sweeper. RLS policy `tenant_isolation_pending_bulk_operations` mirroring repo convention. New service module [`src/tagpulse/services/pending_bulk_operations.py`](src/tagpulse/services/pending_bulk_operations.py) (~250 LOC) — `PENDING_BULK_OP_TTL_SECONDS = 86400` (24 h — vs the C2 token's 15 min, because the second admin needs more wall-clock than a single operator's visual review of a CSV preview), 6-value `PendingDecisionOutcome` enum (`OK`, `NOT_FOUND`, `EXPIRED`, `ALREADY_DECIDED`, `SELF_APPROVAL`, `CONTENT_TAMPER`) mirroring C2's `ConfirmationOutcome` shape for uniform 409 handling, module-scoped `_EXECUTORS: dict[str, PendingExecutor]` registry populated at route-import time via `pending_ops.register_executor("tags.import", _tag_import_executor)` (the C4 bulk PATCH / retire ops will register their own callables — service stays operation-agnostic), `create_pending()` (validates `ttl_seconds > 0`, builds row, `session.add()` + `flush()`), `approve()` (load → lazy-expire if past TTL flipping `status='expired'` in-place → already-decided guard → self-approval guard (`requested_by == decided_by` blocked, the whole POINT of two-person review is named separation of duties) → tamper guard (`content_hasher(row.payload) != row.content_hash` returns `CONTENT_TAMPER` — should be unreachable without direct DB tampering but surfaces loudly if it ever fires) → dispatch executor by `row.operation` → mark `status='executed'` + record `decided_by`/`decided_at`/`executed_at`/`request_id` from executor return), `reject()` (same guards minus tamper/dispatch, marks `status='rejected'`). Tamper guard is **injected** as a `content_hasher: Callable[[bytes], str]` so the service module imports zero domain logic — each operation's route module owns its own re-hash routine. Route changes: [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py) `import_tags` handler grows section **7a** (threshold check: if `len(valid_rows) >= tenant_row.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` → call `pending_ops.create_pending(...)` with `payload=raw`, audit-log `tag.bulk_import_requested` with `{row_count, content_hash, request_id, pending_id, requested_by}`, return 202 with `requires_approval=True`, `pending_id=pending.id`) and **7b** (sub-threshold path — call new `_execute_tag_import(...)` helper, return 201); the C2 confirmation-token path still applies on both branches so even sub-threshold imports require a fresh dry-run before commit. `_execute_tag_import()` is shared between the direct route and the approve-path executor — does `repo.bulk_create()` + audit-logs `tag.bulk_imported` with optional `approved_by` / `pending_id` keys so a single grep against the audit log distinguishes "operator A imported directly" from "operator B approved operator A's batch". `_tag_import_executor()` re-parses the stored CSV bytes via `parse_tag_import_csv()` (raises `RuntimeError` if errors surface, which is unreachable — the bytes were already validated at submit time, but we surface loudly if a future schema change breaks the round-trip), then delegates to `_execute_tag_import()`. `import_payload_content_hash()` exposes the C2-compatible hash function for the bulk-operations route to inject as the `content_hasher` on approve. New route module [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py): `GET /bulk-operations/{id}` (editor+ — for the reviewer to inspect before deciding; returns full `PendingBulkOperationResponse` metadata but deliberately NOT the raw `payload` bytes — operators inspect via the `sample` first-10-EPCs field from C2, the full CSV would inflate response sizes uselessly); `POST /bulk-operations/{id}/approve` (admin only — extra `user.user_id is None` guard rejecting tenant-API-key actors with 403 because API keys are shared credentials and the whole point of two-person review is named accountability); `POST /bulk-operations/{id}/reject` (admin only — same API-key guard; self-rejection also blocked for symmetry, the original requester should ask the reviewer to reject rather than back-channel via the API). 404 fast-fail outside the service so the standard not-found mapping stays uniform across all three endpoints; non-OK service outcomes mapped to 409 except `SELF_APPROVAL` → 403 (authorisation, not state). Audit-log entries: `tag.bulk_import_requested` (on 202), `tag.bulk_imported` (on execute, with new `approved_by` / `pending_id` keys), `tags.import.approved` / `tags.import.rejected` (on decide — keyed on `{operation}.approved` / `.rejected` so C4's `tags.bulk_patch.approved` slots in without an audit-log schema change). Schema additions in [`src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py): `TagImportResult` docstring rewritten from 4 → **5** wire branches (added the 202 two-person-rule branch with explicit "rows_created=0, rows_skipped=0, requires_approval=True, pending_id=<uuid>" semantics), two new optional fields `requires_approval: bool | None` and `pending_id: UUID | None`; new `PendingBulkOperationResponse` model (15 fields covering id, tenant, operation, status, requester, decider, content_hash, row_count, sample, request_id, all four timestamps, expires_at — payload deliberately not exposed). ORM additions in [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py): added `tag_bulk_two_person_threshold: Mapped[int] = mapped_column(Integer, nullable=False, server_default="10000")` to `TenantModel` and a full `PendingBulkOperationModel` class after `TagTransferModel` with the BYTEA payload column wired via `from sqlalchemy.dialects.postgresql import BYTEA`. Tests: new [`tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py`](tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py) (17 cases across 4 test classes) covers `create_pending` (shape, TTL=0 rejected, `requested_by=None` accepted for tenant-API-key actors), `approve` (happy-path executes + marks `executed` + records `request_id`, all 6 outcomes: not-found, expired, already-decided, self-approval blocked, content-tamper, plus a `LookupError` test asserting that an unregistered operation raises rather than silently no-ops), `reject` (happy, self-rejection blocked, not-found, already-decided, expired), and the executor registry (`register_executor` / `reset_executors` / `get_registered_operations` sorted-list semantics). An autouse fixture resets the executor registry between tests so production `register_executor("tags.import", ...)` doesn't leak. In-memory `_FakeSession` (40 LOC) supports the service's `add` + `flush` + `execute(scalar_one_or_none)` surface — no Postgres dependency. `make check` clean: **1263 passed, 1 skipped** (+17 from C2's 1246), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. `openapi.json` regenerated (+298 lines for the three new bulk-operations endpoints + `PendingBulkOperationResponse` schema). **Out of scope for C3** (lands later this sprint): list-pending endpoint `GET /bulk-operations?status=pending` (operators query the audit-log surface or the DB directly until C5 ships the unified shape — index on `(tenant_id, status, expires_at)` already exists for it); background TTL sweeper (current implementation lazy-expires on `approve`/`reject` calls — a row that's never polled stays in `pending` indefinitely in the DB, which is fine because the `expires_at` column means a query can filter accurately and a future sweeper job has all the data it needs); scope-required filters on bulk PATCH / retire (**C4** — same `pending_bulk_operations` substrate, register `"tags.bulk_patch"` and `"tags.bulk_retire"` executors); unified audit-log shape (**C5** — will hoist `pending_id`/`approved_by` into top-level columns). Files: `migrations/versions/047_tag_bulk_two_person_threshold.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/services/pending_bulk_operations.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/api/routes/bulk_operations.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_pending_bulk_operations.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 50 Phase C2 — Dry-run + confirmation-token plumbing for tag-import ([ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 2](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Closes the loop Phase C1 left open: a successful `?dry_run=true` against `POST /v1/tenants/{slug}/tags/import` now mints a single-use confirmation token bound to the previewed CSV, and the operator must echo that token via `?confirm=<token>` to commit. **Contract:** `dry_run` and `confirm` are mutually exclusive (both set → **400**) and at least one is required ("bare" submits with neither set → **400 "confirmation required: POST with ?dry_run=true first"** — pre-C2 the bare-submit path was an implicit commit, which made the dry-run "optional" in practice; closing that loophole is the whole point of the ADR rule). The token binds **`(tenant_id, user_id, operation, content_hash)`** where `content_hash = sha256(canonical-sorted normalized EPCs)`: same EPC set in a different row order hashes identically (operators legitimately re-sort spreadsheets between preview and commit), but adding/removing/changing any EPC produces a fresh hash and the token comes back as **409 `content_mismatch`**. The four-axis binding catches four distinct mistakes — `tenant_mismatch` (operator scoped their dry-run against tenant A then tried to confirm against tenant B), `user_mismatch` (operator A's preview can't be confirmed by operator B — this is the accidental-confirm guard, NOT the C3 two-person-rule which is a separate concern), `operation_mismatch` (token minted for `tags.import` can't be replayed against the C3 transfers endpoint or the C4 bulk PATCH endpoint when those land), and `content_mismatch` (the core ADR guarantee — "a second CSV cannot be confirmed with the first preview's token"). TTL = 900 s (15 min — long enough for visual review of a 10k-row preview, short enough that forgotten previews can't be weaponized days later); single-use semantics (successful `consume` pops the entry); mismatched-arg `consume` calls deliberately **do NOT** burn the token so a typo on `?confirm=...` doesn't force operators to re-dry-run; expired tokens lazy-evict on the next `consume`, opportunistic purge sweeps run on every `mint`. New primitive [`src/tagpulse/core/bulk_confirmation_tokens.py`](src/tagpulse/core/bulk_confirmation_tokens.py) (~145 LOC) — `BulkConfirmationTokenStore` with `mint()` / `consume()` / `reset()` and a 7-value `ConfirmationOutcome` enum (`OK`, `NOT_FOUND`, `EXPIRED`, `TENANT_MISMATCH`, `USER_MISMATCH`, `OPERATION_MISMATCH`, `CONTENT_MISMATCH`). Designed **generic** for reuse in Phase C3 (transfers — `operation="tag-transfers.create"`) and Phase C4 (bulk PATCH — `operation="tags.bulk_patch"`); the per-operation string is the discriminator that lets one store serve every bulk endpoint without cross-talk. Tokens are `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)` (≈43 chars, 256 bits of entropy — collisions infeasible). Thread-safe via a single module-scoped `threading.Lock`; in-process state mirroring the [`tag_import_rate_limit.py`](src/tagpulse/core/tag_import_rate_limit.py) pattern, narrow `mint`/`consume` call surface so the Sprint 60+ Redis swap (`SET token NX EX ttl` for mint, `GETDEL` for consume) is mechanical. `user_id: UUID | None` is accepted so tenant-API-key actors (no Entra user) can still gate themselves — the key holder is the binding identity in that case, and the existing `AuthenticatedUser.user_id` shape carries the right value (`None`) end-to-end. Route changes in [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py) add the `confirm` query param, the mutual-exclusion + at-least-one validation block, content-hash computation via the new `_content_hash()` helper (operates on the post-parse, post-validate `valid_rows` so a partially-invalid CSV that 422s never reaches the mint path — token is only minted when the CSV would commit cleanly), and the `BULK_CONFIRMATION_TOKENS.mint()` / `consume()` plumbing. Successful confirmations echo the consumed `token` back on the response (for audit traceability — the operator's UI can show "you applied preview {token-suffix}") and the audit-log `changes{}` payload gains a `confirmation_token` field which Phase C5's unified audit shape will hoist into a top-level column. Failed confirmations surface as **409 Conflict** with the discriminating `reason` from `ConfirmationOutcome.value` in the JSON detail, so the operator UI can render reason-specific guidance ("this CSV doesn't match the preview — re-run dry-run" vs "wrong operator — ask the original requester" vs "token expired — re-run dry-run"). Schema additions in [`src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py) extend `TagImportResult` with three optional fields — `token: str | None`, `expires_in: int | None`, `sample: list[str] | None`. `sample` is bounded at the first **10 EPCs** in the route layer so the operator can sanity-check ("did I paste the right reel?") without scrolling 10k rows; schema accepts any length so the cap can be widened later without a wire break. Docstring rewritten to enumerate the four response branches (422 errors, 200 dry-run, 201 commit, 409 bad token) and pin the mutually-exclusive-and-required intent contract. Hourly per-tenant rate limit (10/hr default from C1) advances **before** validation on both dry-run and confirm paths — each `POST` consumes one slot, the cap is on operator activity not on writes, so a churn of "preview → typo → preview → confirm" still costs four slots and that's the right answer (catches the runaway-script threat exactly). Tests: new file [`tests/unit/test_bulk_confirmation_tokens.py`](tests/unit/test_bulk_confirmation_tokens.py) (16 cases across 5 test classes) covers the full token-store surface — happy-path mint+consume, single-use semantics (second consume returns `NOT_FOUND`), `user_id=None` accepted, all five mismatch outcomes (not-found / tenant / user / operation / content) each surface as their distinct enum value, the no-burn guarantee (a bad consume followed by a good consume succeeds — the bad call doesn't poison the preview), TTL behaviour using the `now=` injection point (expired token returns `EXPIRED` once then `NOT_FOUND` on the next call due to lazy eviction; within-TTL call still works at the 59th second of a 60 s window), `mint(ttl_seconds=0)` raises `ValueError` (zero / negative TTL is a programming error not a runtime case), and module-singleton sanity (`reset()` clears state, the singleton is an instance of the store class). `make check` clean: **1246 passed, 1 skipped** (+16 from C1's 1230), ruff + mypy --strict both clean. **Out of scope for C2** (lands later this sprint): two-person rule above `tenants.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` (C3 — the C2 token store is the substrate it'll build on, with a second `mint` call by the second admin gating the actual commit), scope-required filters on bulk PATCH / retire (C4 — same token-store substrate, `operation="tags.bulk_patch"`), unified audit-log shape (C5 — will hoist the C2 `confirmation_token` into the standard column). Files: `src/tagpulse/core/bulk_confirmation_tokens.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `tests/unit/test_bulk_confirmation_tokens.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 50 Phase C1 — Bulk CSV import for the tag registry ([ADR 028 OQ 4](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** New endpoint `POST /v1/tenants/{slug}/tags/import` (editor/admin) accepts a CSV with one required `epc_hex` column (extra columns ignored — operators paste reel manifests with vendor-specific headers and we don't want to force a strip step). Enforces the ADR 028 OQ 4 governance lock end-to-end: **413 Payload Too Large** if the file exceeds 8 MiB *or* if the row count exceeds the 10 000 hard cap; **429 Too Many Requests** if the tenant has already issued more imports in the trailing hour than its `tenants.tag_bulk_import_rate_limit` allows (new column, default 10 — see below). The hourly counter advances *before* CSV parsing so a malformed payload still counts toward the cap, which catches the runaway-script threat model exactly. **All-or-nothing validation**: any per-row error (blank `epc_hex` cell, non-hex value, value outside 16..128 chars, duplicate `epc_hex` *within the same CSV*) collects into a `TagImportResult.errors[]` payload and the import returns 422 — **nothing is written** even if 9 999 rows would have been valid (per ADR 028 OQ 4 "the reconciliation burden outweighs the convenience"). The duplicate-within-CSV check is case-insensitive and reports the row number of the first occurrence so operators can grep their spreadsheet ("duplicate epc_hex in CSV (first seen on row 1)"). The endpoint accepts an opt-in `?dry_run=true` query param that runs the full validation pipeline without writing — returns 200 on a clean run or 422 with the same `errors[]` shape on failure. The confirmation-token plumbing that ties a successful dry-run to a subsequent commit lands in Phase C2; C1 ships the bare dry-run preview so operators can sanity-check before shipping a real import. New migration [`migrations/versions/046_tenant_tag_bulk_import_rate_limit.py`](migrations/versions/046_tenant_tag_bulk_import_rate_limit.py) adds `tenants.tag_bulk_import_rate_limit INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 10` — backfills cleanly without operator action; `PATCH /tenant-config` will surface it as part of the C5 governance wrap-up. Encoded as a tenants column (not a global setting) for consistency with the existing per-tenant knobs (`rate_limit_overrides`, the forthcoming `tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` in C3). New per-hour primitive [`src/tagpulse/core/tag_import_rate_limit.py`](src/tagpulse/core/tag_import_rate_limit.py) — thread-safe sliding-window counter per `(tenant_id)`, intentionally **separate** from the existing `tagpulse.core.rate_limit.RATE_LIMITER` (which is per-minute, per-route-class token bucket); the call surface (`check_and_record(tenant_id, max_per_hour)`) is narrow enough that the Sprint 60+ Redis sliding-window swap is mechanical. New CSV parser [`parse_tag_import_csv()`](src/tagpulse/services/tags.py) is pure (bytes → `(valid_rows, errors)`) so the route owns transport / persistence / rate limit and the service owns format / header / per-row syntactic validation. New repository method [`TimescaleTagRepository.bulk_create()`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py) issues a single PostgreSQL `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING ON CONSTRAINT uq_tags_tenant_epc` against `tags` — returns `(rows_created, rows_skipped)` so duplicates of EPCs already owned by the tenant are treated as idempotent re-imports (counted in `rows_skipped`, not as validation errors). All rows are written `status='registered', source='csv_import'` per ADR 028 §"Governance" rule 1 ("Default to `status='registered'` on import, never `active`"). New schemas [`TagImportRowError`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py) and [`TagImportResult`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py) — the latter's `dry_run` field is the wire-level distinguisher between "validated, not written" and "written" (which the C5 unified audit log will also key on). One audit-log entry per successful real import: action `tag.bulk_imported`, resource_type `tag`, `resource_id` = a server-generated `request_id` UUID, changes `{rows_total, rows_created, rows_skipped, request_id, source: "csv_import"}` — forward-compatible with the C5 unified-shape requirement of `(actor, action, batch, count, request_id)`. Tests: [`tests/unit/test_tags_import.py`](tests/unit/test_tags_import.py) (22 cases) — CSV happy paths (UTF-8 BOM, case-insensitive header, extra columns ignored, value normalization), error surface (empty file, missing column, invalid UTF-8, blank cell with sibling column, invalid hex, too-short EPC, in-CSV duplicates including case-equivalence cross-reference), hourly limiter (cap enforcement, zero cap blocks all, window slides at +3601 s, per-tenant isolation, `remaining()` accounting, `reset()`, module-singleton sanity), `TagImportResult` schema (default empty errors list, error serialisation). `make check` clean: **1230 passed, 1 skipped**, ruff + mypy --strict both clean. Out of scope for C1 (lands later this sprint): confirmation-token plumbing tying dry-run preview to a subsequent commit (C2), two-person rule above `tenants.tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` for above-threshold imports (C3), scope-required filters on bulk PATCH / retire (C4), unified audit-log shape keyed on `(actor, action, batch, count, request_id)` (C5). Files: `migrations/versions/046_tenant_tag_bulk_import_rate_limit.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/core/tag_import_rate_limit.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/services/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`, `tests/unit/test_tags_import.py` (new), `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 50 Phase B — Tag registry CRUD + cross-tenant transfers API ([ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Operator surface for the registry tables Phase A landed. **B1 (service layer)** — new module [`src/tagpulse/services/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/services/tags.py) wraps the existing `tagpulse.rfid.epc.decode_epc_hex` decoder in a lenient `parse_gs1_uri()` (returns the `urn:epc:id:...` for SGTIN / SSCC / GIAI / GRAI headers, `None` for raw / proprietary / malformed inputs — never raises, so a bad EPC stores `gs1_uri=NULL` and falls out of the `ix_tags_tenant_gs1_uri` partial index per OQ 2 resolution), `normalize_epc_hex()` (strip + uppercase, applied before regex validation so operators can paste lowercase / whitespace-padded values), and the operator-permitted `validate_status_transition()` graph (`registered|active → retired|defective` only; `registered → active` is the registrar-worker domain and `* → transferred_out` is the transfer-flow domain — both deliberately absent so the admin API cannot bypass the worker / the two-party transfer). New Pydantic models in [`src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py): `TagStatus` / `TagSource` / `TagTransferStatus` Literals mirroring the migration 043 CHECK enums, `TagCreate` (regex-validated canonical EPC, `source ∈ {csv_import, api, backfill}` — `transfer_in` excluded because it's server-only on the transfer-completion path), `TagUpdate` (status + metadata only — `epc_hex` is the natural key and immutable, no `batch_id` field because batch grouping rides on `entity_labels` per OQ 5), `TagResponse`, `TagTransferRequest` (`to_tenant_slug` + 1..1000 EPCs), `TagTransferResponse`. `LabelEntityType` Literal extended with `"tag"` so the labels API can attach `batch.*` rows (and any other future tag-scoped label) to registry rows — migration 045 already widened the DB CHECK in Phase A. **B2 (registry routes)** — new module [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py). `GET /tags` (viewer+) with filters `?status`, `?epc_prefix`, `?bound` (EXISTS-based check against `stock_items.binding_value` with `binding_kind='epc'` — `true` returns only bound tags, `false` only unbound, omitted returns all), and `?labels[<key>]=<value>` parsed out of the raw query string via a regex on bracketed keys (FastAPI's `Query` can't bind bracketed names directly) and joined through `entity_labels` + `labels` with `entity_type='tag'` enforced on the catalog side. `POST /tags` (editor/admin) creates one row in `status='registered'`, derives `gs1_uri` synchronously via `parse_gs1_uri` (it's a pure-Python decode — microsecond cost, no need to defer to a worker), returns 409 on the `(tenant_id, epc_hex)` unique-violation. `GET /tags/{epc_hex}` (viewer+) — path-based lookup, case-insensitive via the same `normalize_epc_hex`. `PATCH /tags/{tag_id}` (editor/admin) — applies `validate_status_transition` and returns 409 with the violation message on rejected edges; same-state patches are silently accepted so idempotent retries don't conflict. `DELETE /tags/{tag_id}` (admin) — 409 with `binding_count` if any `stock_items` row binds to the EPC (UI guard-rail), 204 on hard-delete otherwise. Every write is audit-logged with the same `(tenant_id, action, resource_type, resource_id, changes={}, user_id=...)` shape `labels.py` uses. **B3 (transfers)** — `POST /tag-transfers` (admin) initiates a cross-tenant transfer of 1..1000 EPCs. Validation: receiving tenant must exist + be `active`; self-transfer rejected (400); duplicate EPCs in the same request rejected (400); every EPC must be owned by the calling tenant **and** in `status='active'` — the response 409 enumerates `not_found` and `not_active` EPCs separately so the operator UI can show actionable diff. On success, writes one `tag_transfers` row per EPC, all sharing one server-generated `request_id`, in `status='requested'`. Phase B does **not** flip the source tag's status — that happens at acknowledgement / completion in the receiving-tenant flow (Phase C3, where the two-person approval shape from ADR 028 §4 also lands). `GET /tag-transfers` (viewer+) with `?direction=in|out` and `?status` filters, defaulting to "both sides visible" matching the RLS policy `tenant_isolation_tag_transfers`. `GET /tag-transfers/{id}` (viewer+). Repository layer [`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py) introduces `TagEpcConflictError(ValueError)`, `TagInUseError(RuntimeError)`, and a re-export of `StatusTransitionError` mirroring the labels-repo pattern. Repo exposes a privileged `update_status_to_transferred_out()` that bypasses `validate_status_transition` for the future transfer-completion path — Phase B doesn't call it yet but keeps the operator API and the privileged path separated by name so a future audit reviewer can see the asymmetry. ORM additions in [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py): `TagModel` (`(tenant_id, epc_hex)` natural key via `uq_tags_tenant_epc`, `metadata_` Python attribute mapped to `"metadata"` column, full audit columns) and `TagTransferModel` (request-grouped, FK to `users.id` on `requested_by`). Router wired into [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) after `labels_router`. Tests: 32 new unit tests across `tests/unit/test_tags_service.py` (normalization, lenient GS1 parser including malformed-hex paths, parametrized happy / rejected transitions), `tests/unit/test_tags_repository.py` (exception hierarchy + re-export sanity), `tests/unit/test_tags_schemas.py` (canonical-EPC accept, lowercase / short / non-hex rejection, `source="transfer_in"` rejection on create, transfer-request min/max bounds). `make check` clean: **1208 passed, 1 skipped**, ruff + mypy --strict both clean. Out of scope for Phase B (lands later): registrar-worker `registered → active` promotion path (Phase D), transfer acknowledgement / completion + the two-person approval flow from ADR 028 §4 (Phase C3), bulk CSV import with the 10k-row / 10-per-hour governance controls (Phase C1+C2), `?bound` filter semantics beyond stock_items (e.g. asset bindings — defer until that join surfaces a customer need). Files: `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/services/tags.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/tags.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tags.py` (new), `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `tests/unit/test_tags_service.py` (new), `tests/unit/test_tags_repository.py` (new), `tests/unit/test_tags_schemas.py` (new).

- **Sprint 50 Phase A — Tag registry schema ([ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Three additive Alembic migrations land the storage layer for the tag identity/ownership registry: **`043_tag_registry.py`** creates `tags` (`(tenant_id, epc_hex)` unique, `epc_hex VARCHAR(128)` matching the existing `tag_reads.epc_hex` column to avoid implicit-cast joins, partial index on `(tenant_id, gs1_uri) WHERE gs1_uri IS NOT NULL`, `status` ∈ `{registered,active,retired,defective,transferred_out}` and `source` ∈ `{csv_import,api,backfill,transfer_in}` enforced via CHECK — no `first_read` source per OQ 3) plus `tag_transfers` (request-grouped cross-tenant audit log with FK to `users.id`, CHECK constraints binding `failure_reason`/`completed_at` to the terminal state, three indexes for request-id and per-tenant outbound/inbound timelines, and an RLS policy that lets either side of the transfer see the row). Both tables get RLS theatre per repo convention. **`044_tag_reads_tag_known.py`** adds the soft-gating `tag_reads.tag_known BOOLEAN NULL` column (three-valued NULL/TRUE/FALSE) split into its own migration so the two concerns revert independently; the registrar worker is the only writer (service-layer contract, no DB enforcement) and no index is added — dominant access is the worker's own `WHERE tag_known IS NULL` scan on the recent hypertable chunks. **`045_tag_label_namespace.py`** extends the `labels.entity_type` CHECK constraint to include `'tag'`, detects collisions in the reserved `batch.*` namespace across **all** entity_types (Sprint 50 risk lock: refuse + manual intervention — RAISE with the colliding tenant slugs, pointing operators at the new [reserved-label-key-collision runbook](docs/runbooks/reserved-label-key-collision.md)), and backfills the four reserved label rows (`batch`, `batch.received_at`, `batch.description`, `batch.supplier`) for every existing tenant via `WHERE NOT EXISTS` against the lower(key) functional unique index. The migration's downgrade preserves any `'tag'`-typed labels still bound to entities (deletes only orphans) so a partial downgrade can't silently lose operator data. Tenant-bootstrap path updated in [`scripts/smoke_setup.py`](scripts/smoke_setup.py) — new `_seed_reserved_tag_labels()` helper called from `upsert_tenant` keeps new tenants in sync without depending on the backfill migration. Phase A is purely additive: the MQTT ingest hot path is unchanged, the registrar worker (Phase D) does not yet exist, and the labels API still treats `batch.*` as user-writable (the service-layer reservation guard lands in Phase B alongside the registry CRUD surface). Tests: `make check` clean (1176 passed, 1 skipped). Files: `migrations/versions/043_tag_registry.py` (new), `migrations/versions/044_tag_reads_tag_known.py` (new), `migrations/versions/045_tag_label_namespace.py` (new), `scripts/smoke_setup.py`, `docs/runbooks/reserved-label-key-collision.md` (new), `docs/runbooks/README.md`.

### Changed

- **Sprint 50 Phase F — Tag registry docs + governance close-out ([ADR 028](docs/adr/028-tags-as-first-class-entity.md)).** Docs-only ceremony closing out Sprint 50 — no source / schema / OpenAPI changes (Phase E shipped commit `28fed58`, 1335 passing). Six artefacts updated to reflect that ADR 028 is now implemented and that operators have a single landing page for the registry workflows. **F1 (data-models).** [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md) gains a Sprint 50 advisory blockquote under the "Where is the tag?" section pointing to ADR 028 and the new registry overview, with the opening line softened from "TagPulse intentionally has no first-class Tag entity" to "The TagPulse ingest path has no first-class Tag entity" so the (still-true) hot-path statement doesn't read as contradicting the now-shipped registry. The `tag_reads` column table gains a `tag_known BOOLEAN NULL` row with the registrar-worker-as-sole-writer note and migration `044` added to the migrations list. New top-level **"### Tag registry (Sprint 50+)"** overview section inserted before `## Database Tables` — matrix table covering all six new surfaces (`tags`, `tag_transfers`, `tag_reads.tag_known`, `pending_bulk_operations`, the four new `audit_logs` columns for unified bulk-op grep, reserved label-key namespace `batch.*`) with one-line "what it is / where to read more" rows. Three new column tables landed between `tag_reads` and `users`: `tags` (full schema from migration 043 — `(tenant_id, epc_hex)` natural key, `status`/`source` enums, partial `gs1_uri` index, `metadata` JSONB), `tag_transfers` (request-grouped cross-tenant audit log from migration 043), `pending_bulk_operations` (two-person-rule substrate from migration 047 — `payload BYTEA`, decided-state CHECK, lazy TTL semantics). **F2 (operator runbook).** New [docs/runbooks/tag-registry-operations.md](docs/runbooks/tag-registry-operations.md) (~200 LOC) is the single landing page for operators running the registry: §1 covers the `POST /tags/import` two-step dry-run → confirm flow with the 10 000-row cap (413), 10-per-hour tenant rate limit (429), content-hash bound confirmation token, all-or-nothing validation, and batch-label attachment via the reserved `batch.*` namespace; §2 documents the status lifecycle (`registered → active` worker-owned vs. `* → retired|defective|transferred_out` operator-owned, with `tag_known` three-valued semantics); §3 walks the two-person rule (`tag_bulk_two_person_threshold` default 10 000, `pending_bulk_operations` state machine, `POST /bulk-operations/{id}/approve` with content-hash tamper guard);
