Phase A4 attributed to both `e54332b` (helper + lookup table) and `9f02f38` (per-trigger config models) since the Pydantic foundation landed across the A→B handoff. **Phase H + G5 update (post-commit):** the original Phase G commit landed with Phase H deferred to a follow-up sprint with its plan preserved verbatim in roadmap §"Phase H"; the deferral was **revoked later in the same Sprint 41 PR** — Phase H + G5 shipped together (see the Phase H entry above this one). At Phase G commit time the Phase F7 UI work already dropped the **visible** `Type` field on Asset forms (a hidden `Form.Item` pinned `asset_type` so the backend, still carrying the column, kept round-tripping cleanly). Pure documentation — no source, no tests, no migration, no behaviour change in this Phase G slice itself. `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`, `docs/user-guide.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase F — UI surface for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2) shipped on TagPulse-UI [PR #46](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI/pull/46) (`ebb2f82`).** Backend cross-link entry — the UI work ships in a separate repo per the long-standing TagPulse / TagPulse-UI split, but is sprint-tied to this backend PR via [ADR 021 v2.2](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) and the reference-design remediation rows 1.1 + 3.5 (both flipped ✅ Done in the Phase G commit above). Files-changed: 20 (+1,726 / −100), 3 new. `npm run check` clean (lint + typecheck + 208/208 vitest). **F1 — Signaling Events sidebar group** in `src/components/Layout.tsx` consolidates Rules + Alerts under one Ant Menu `type: 'group'` header per UI gap 1.1; final label is "Signaling Events" (the v2.1 sensing→signaling rename is consistent across the rest of the surface). **F2 — `SignalingRuleModal`** at `src/pages/rules/SignalingRuleModal.tsx` walks Event Type → Trigger (validated against the 13-pair `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS` matrix in `src/types.ts` — impossible pairs hidden from the dropdown, not greyed) → per-trigger config form → optional Category / Label / Integration scoping; form POSTs to `/v1/tenants/{slug}/rules` with `"kind": "signaling"` body (no `/sensing-events` URL, per backend Phase E1). **F3 — RuleEditor Tabs wrapper** at `src/pages/rules/RuleEditor.tsx` makes "Signaling Event" the default create tab with a "Legacy rule" sub-tab keeping the 10 legacy `condition_type` form editable for round-tripping. **F4 — vitest coverage** in `SignalingRuleModal.test.tsx` (NEW, 16 cases) parametrizes all 13 valid pairs + 4 invalid-pair rejections; uses `PointerEventsCheckLevel.Never` + 15s per-test timeout + explicit `afterEach(cleanup)` to handle AntD motion + Select interactions cleanly. **F5 — Sidebar reorganization** consolidates top-level groups: DATA MANAGEMENT (Assets, Categories, Sites, Labels) / EDGE MANAGEMENT (Devices, Integrations) / SIGNALING EVENTS (Rules, Alerts) / INVENTORY. **F6 — Collapsible icon-mode sidebar** — Ant `Sider` with `collapsible` + `collapsedWidth={64}`; tooltips when collapsed; preference persisted in `localStorage` keyed `(tenantId, userId)` so each operator's setting travels with their account. **Surfaced + fixed a real bug** while writing F8 tests: `Sider.onCollapse(_, 'responsive')` fires on jsdom mount (default `matchMedia` returns `matches: false`) and was clobbering the persisted preference; the fix in `handleSiderCollapse(next, type)` only writes to `localStorage` when `type === 'clickTrigger'`. **F7 — Asset form drops visible `Type` field** in `src/pages/assets/AssetList.tsx` + `src/pages/assets/AssetDetail.tsx`; a hidden `Form.Item` pins `asset_type` to `'asset'` for create and preserves existing values for edit so the backend (still carrying the column until Phase H) keeps round-tripping cleanly. **F8 — `Layout.test.tsx`** (NEW, 4 cases) covers the collapsed-sidebar toggle + persistence shape + the responsive-event regression guard from F6. The regenerated OpenAPI client (`src/api/generated/*` after `npm run generate-api`) picks up Phase E's `RuleCreate` / `RuleUpdate` / `RuleResponse` signaling fields + the `kind` discriminator + the `?kind=` query param. No backend source change in this entry — purely a sprint-tied cross-link so a search of this repo's CHANGELOG for "Sprint 41" surfaces all eight phases.

- **Sprint 41 Phase E — API surface for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2): per-rule integration routing + OpenAPI regen.** Closes the API-layer half of Sprint 41 after Phases A–D (schema → service/dispatcher shell → outbound envelope → processors + on_inference). **E1 — `?kind=signaling` discriminator filter** was already shipped in Phase B2 on the existing `/v1/tenants/{slug}/rules` endpoint (per the roadmap deviation from ADR-021's original `/sensing-events` URL proposal — avoids baking a legacy URL into the API at the moment the deferred Sprint-4X taxonomy-unification ADR plans to rename `rules` → `alert_rules` anyway); this entry pins that decision and confirms no parallel URL namespace was added in Phase E. **E2 — per-rule integration routing** in [`src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py). Implements [ADR-021 v2 open question #3](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) — *replace, not augment*: when a rule's `integration_ids` column is non-empty, the WebhookDispatcher delivers the resulting alert **only** to integrations in that allow-list (intersected with the subscription set for the event type); when the column is empty or null, the dispatcher falls back to the legacy broadcast over every enabled integration subscribed to the event. Renames the internal helper `_build_alert_envelope` → `_resolve_alert_rule_context` so a single `session.get(RuleModel, rule_uuid)` per dispatcher tick now feeds **both** the Phase-C envelope build **and** the Phase-E integration filter — no second DB lookup. Helper returns `tuple[dict[str, Any], frozenset[uuid.UUID] | None]` where the second element is `None` for "broadcast" and a `frozenset` for "filter to these integration IDs". Gated on `event.topic == Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` so non-alert broadcasts (raw `tag_read.created`, `telemetry.recorded`) are never filtered — they have no rule context to consult. Three defensive paths preserve the legacy broadcast behaviour: missing `rule_id` in payload → broadcast; malformed `rule_id` (not a UUID) → broadcast; unknown `rule_id` (rule deleted between publish and dispatch) → broadcast (rather than silently dropping the alert when the operator's intent has been lost). Two intentional non-defensive paths: rule with non-empty `integration_ids` that don't intersect the subscription set → **zero deliveries** (the rule's allow-list mis-config is surfaced as missing webhook calls, not papered over with a fallback broadcast); rule allow-listing a not-subscribed integration → that integration is skipped (the filter intersects with the subscription set, doesn't bypass it). **E2 tests** — new [`tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py`](tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py) (12 tests, four `Test*` classes) mirrors the Phase C `test_webhook_envelope.py` scaffolding (same `_FakeMeter`, same `httpx.MockTransport`-backed handler that captures the request URL so the test asserts which integrations were hit, same `IntegrationService` patch that returns a controlled subscription list). `TestBroadcastFallback` (2 tests) — null and empty `integration_ids` both broadcast to every enabled subscribed integration. `TestPerRuleReplace` (3 tests) — subset allow-list delivers only to the subset; allow-list with a not-subscribed integration ID skips it (replace ∩ subscribe, not bypass); allow-list disjoint from subscription set delivers nothing. `TestPerRuleReplaceSignaling` (4 tests, parametrized over the 4 event types) — signaling rules (event_type populated) honour the filter the same way as legacy rules; the filter is event-type-agnostic by design. `TestFilterDefensivePaths` (3 tests) — missing `rule_id` / unknown `rule_id` / non-alert event all fall through to broadcast. **E3 — OpenAPI regen** via `python scripts/export_openapi.py > openapi.json`. The regenerated spec picks up the Phase A schema additions on `RuleCreate` / `RuleUpdate` / `RuleResponse` (`event_type` enum, `trigger`, `processor`, `confidence_threshold` `NUMERIC(3,2)` constrained to `[0.0, 1.0]`, `category_ids` UUID array, `asset_label_filters` / `zone_label_filters` / `site_label_filters` JSONB arrays, `integration_ids` UUID array), the extended `condition_type` regex covering the 12 `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` pairs alongside the 10 legacy values, the `kind: Literal["legacy", "signaling"]` discriminator on `RuleResponse`, and the `?kind=` query param on `GET /rules`. Diff stat: `+413/-2` lines in `openapi.json` (374,625 → 386,342 bytes). The outbound webhook envelope fields (`confidence`, `keySet`, `eventConfigurationId`, `categoryId`, `labels`) are intentionally **not** in the OpenAPI spec — they're outbound payload fields on the webhook delivery itself, not API request/response schema, so they live in the ADR-021 v2 §"Outbound envelope" section and the dispatcher tests (`test_webhook_envelope.py` Phase C; `test_signaling_envelope.py` builder). **`make check` clean: 1073 unit tests passing** (was 1061 before Phase E; +12 from the new per-rule-routing test file), `ruff check src tests` ✓, `mypy --strict` ✓. Phase E completes the API-surface half of Sprint 41 — only Phases F (UI), G (docs reconciliation), and H (drop `assets.asset_type`) remain. `src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`, `tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py`, `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase D — IsolatedZones + OverlappingZones processors + `on_inference` alert consumer (ADR-021 v2).** Lands the real Phase D processor pipeline that Phases A–C set up, completing the rule-evaluation half of Sprint 41. **D1 IsolatedZones module** [`src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py): pure-function codification of the existing "one read → at most one zone" attribution rule used by the ingestion path. Public surface: `ZoneCandidate` dataclass (id, kind, created_at, fixed_reader_ids, polygon_geojson, bbox_min/max_lat/lon); `IsolatedZoneAttribution` (zone_id, zone_kind, source∈{"reader_bound","geofence"}); `attribute_reader_bound(read_reader_id, zones)` and `attribute_geofence(latitude, longitude, zones)` that match independently; `attribute(reader_id, latitude, longitude, zones)` chains the two with reader-bound priority + geofence fallback. Deterministic-oldest tiebreak (`min(..., key=lambda z: z.created_at)`) matches `TimescaleSitesZonesRepository.get_zone_for_reader` and `IngestionService._eval_geofence_for_subject`. Geofence path uses the `bbox_*` denormalized columns as a cheap O(1) prefilter before the ring ray-cast via `tagpulse.geo.point_in_polygon` (which expects ring coords as `(lon, lat)` tuples — see [`src/tagpulse/geo/__init__.py`](src/tagpulse/geo/__init__.py)); malformed `polygon_geojson` payloads are silently skipped so one bad zone can't poison the loop for the rest of the tenant. No DB I/O — the module is callable from any code path that has already loaded the zone candidates. Phase D1 doesn't change ingestion behaviour — it extracts the existing logic into a reusable shape so the upcoming `IsolatedZonesProcessor` (future periodic runner that mirrors the ingestion attribution for retrospective queries) can share the same pure functions. **D2 OverlappingZones module** [`src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py): two layers. *Pure layer* — `AttributionRead` (asset_id, reader_id, timestamp, signal_strength, latitude, longitude); `AggregationConfig` (aggregation_window_s=60, min_rssi_dbm=-80.0, zone_bleed_filter=True, zone_bleed_share_threshold=0.10, aging_weight=1.0, aging_bucket_s=60, time_error_filter_s=5) with `from_rule_config(condition_config)` classmethod that uses **tri-state** logic for `min_rssi_dbm` — missing key → default `-80.0`, explicit `null` → `None` (floor disabled), numeric → coerce to float (regression-pinned in `test_aggregation_config_from_rule_config_*`); `ZoneAttribution` (asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers); `_attributable_zones_for_read` returns **all** matching zones (unlike IsolatedZones which picks one) — multi-membership is the entire point of the overlapping processor; `_age_weight(read_age_s, window_s, weight, bucket_s)` decays older reads inside the window; `aggregate(reads, zones, *, now, site_by_zone, config)` is the workhorse — buckets evidence per `(asset, zone)` pair, normalizes confidences per asset, applies the bleed filter (drop zones whose share is strictly below `zone_bleed_share_threshold` with re-normalization of survivors), and returns a deterministically-ordered list sorted by `(str(asset_id), str(zone_id))` so two runs over the same input always emit attribution events in the same order. *Runtime layer* — `OverlappingZonesProcessor(event_bus)` with `async run_once_for_rule(session, rule, *, now=None) -> int`: loads zone candidates via SQLAlchemy `select(ZoneModel)`; loads in-window reads via raw `text()` SQL that joins `tag_reads × asset_tag_bindings` on the three-way `binding_kind ∈ {epc, tid, device}` match (mirrors the existing `_PATH_SQL` join pattern in `tagpulse.repositories.timescaledb.asset_location`); calls `aggregate()`; publishes one `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED` event per attribution with the **coordinate-system-agnostic payload** pinned by [ADR-021 v2](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) §"`signaling.attribution_settled` payload": `{tenant_id, asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers, rule_id}` — explicitly **no** `latitude` / `longitude` / `x` / `y` / `position_*` fields (that's [ADR-024](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md) territory, Sprint 45). The reads-query is parameterised by tenant_id and the configured window with skew tolerance (`window_start = now - aggregation_window_s - time_error_filter_s`); reads whose tag is unbound at the window time are silently excluded — they have no asset to attribute to. **Dispatcher dispatch-by-processor** in [`src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py): `PeriodicSignalingDispatcher.__init__` constructs `self._overlapping_processor = OverlappingZonesProcessor(event_bus)`; `_evaluate_periodic_rule` now dispatches by `rule.processor or "isolated_zones"` — `overlapping_zones` invokes `run_once_for_rule` inside a try/except so a single bad rule doesn't break the tick (pinned by `test_dispatch_overlapping_processor_error_does_not_break_tick`); `isolated_zones` (and None) stay at the Phase B logging shell since the IsolatedZones case is already covered by the ingestion path. The `rule_evaluations` meter tick fires once per rule regardless of processor so per-tenant counts remain comparable across operator choices. **`RuleEvaluator.on_attribution_settled`** in [`src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py`](src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py): new async consumer subscribed to `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED` (wired in [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) right after the existing `Topic.TELEMETRY_RECORDED` subscription in the `workers_inline=True` block). Iterates the three `signaling.<event_type>.on_inference` condition_types (`location` / `geolocation` / `temperature` — listed all three so a future temperature processor fans out the same way without re-touching this method); applies `min_confidence` from `condition_config` (default 0.0); applies cooldown keyed `(tenant_id, rule_id, asset_id_str)` matching the convention from `on_subject_zone_changed`; resolves asset name via `_lookup_subject_name(subject_kind="asset", ...)` and zone name via `_lookup_zone_name` so alert messages are human-readable; creates alert with `severity="info"` and publishes `Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` with the full `action_type`/`action_config` payload so the WebhookDispatcher path picks it up without a second DB lookup; ticks `rule_evaluations` per rule + `alerts_fired` per fired alert. Defensive paths: missing/invalid `tenant_id` → silent return; missing `asset_id` / `zone_id` → silent return; unparseable `confidence` → silent return (these are pinned by the new test file). **Tests** — three new test files + 3 new tests added to the existing dispatcher file, 50 new tests total. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py) (17 tests): reader-bound match/no-match/ignores-geofence/oldest-tiebreak/empty-fixed-list, geofence inside-polygon/outside-bbox/in-bbox-outside-L-shape/ignores-reader-bound/malformed-polygon-skipped/oldest-tiebreak, combined `attribute()` reader-priority/geofence-fallback/no-match/no-geofence-signal/no-reader-id/empty-list. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py) (27 tests): AggregationConfig defaults/full-from_rule_config/missing-block-defaults/explicit-null-rssi-disabled; aggregate empty cases; single-zone full confidence; multi-asset independence; genuine 50/50 overlap (reader-bound + geofence on same read); uneven 80/20 share; RSSI floor drop/None-passes/disabled-when-None; window enforcement (drops old, time_error_filter extends, drops future-beyond-skew); aging-weight 1-bucket-decay confidence_unchanged_single_zone, aging-shifts-overlap (1.0/1.5 vs 0.5/1.5); bleed filter at 19/1 → drops B (10% threshold demands strictly-below, so 9/1=10% survives); bleed disabled keeps 0.95/0.05; deterministic output order; site_by_zone propagation; missing-site-dropped; three D3 synthetic-stream scenarios. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py) (7 tests): DB-mocked `_FakeSession` routing the two `execute()` calls to canned zone + read results; zero-zones returns 0 (reads query is skipped); zero-reads returns 0; happy path emits one event per attribution with correct payload shape (asserts every payload key including `contributing_readers` list and `rule_id`); explicit **forbidden-coordinate-fields** check — asserts the emitted payload has no `latitude` / `longitude` / `lat` / `lon` / `x` / `y` keys even when the underlying `tag_reads` row carried them (defends ADR-021 v2's coordinate-system-agnostic pin against accidental field leakage in a future refactor); genuine overlap emits two events with `confidence=[0.5, 0.5]`; configured window is honoured (third read at 60s ago drops when window is 30s); reads-query parameters include `tenant_id` and the skew-extended window bounds. New dispatcher tests in [`tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py) (+3 tests, now 12): rule with `processor='overlapping_zones'` is routed to `OverlappingZonesProcessor.run_once_for_rule`, rule with `processor=None` is not; both processor variants record a `rule_evaluations` meter tick; a `RuntimeError` from the processor doesn't break the tick (`last_fired` still stamped for the good rule). [`tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py) (10 tests): happy path fires alert + meter ticks; below-threshold skips alert but still records `rule_evaluations`; cooldown suppresses the second event for the same asset; cooldown is keyed per `(tenant, rule, asset)` so a different asset triggers an independent alert; one attribution event fans out to all three `event_type` on_inference rules (location + geolocation + temperature); defensive paths: missing tenant_id, invalid tenant UUID, missing asset_id/zone_id, unparseable confidence; ALERT_TRIGGERED payload includes the rule's `action_type` + `action_config` so webhook delivery works without a second DB lookup. **`make check` clean: 1061 unit tests passing** (was 1011 before Phase D; +50 new), `ruff check src tests` ✓, `mypy --strict` ✓. Phase D leaves Phase E (API surface for the new `processor` enum + per-event-type rule constructors) and Phase F (UI) as the remaining Sprint 41 work. `src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`, `src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py`.

- **Sprint 41 — pre-Phase-D coordinate-system clarification (docs only).** Pins the lat/lon-vs-local-`(x, y)` boundary in three docs so the OverlappingZones processor (Phase D) doesn't get conflated with true indoor trilateration ([ADR 024](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md), Sprint 45). Surfaced by a customer-scenario question on PR #54 about warehouses that work in a local XY grid rather than WGS84. **No code change** — the audit confirmed the existing `zones.fixed_reader_ids` + `zones.polygon_geojson` model already covers both the indoor warehouse use case (reader-bound zones, no coordinates needed) and the outdoor lat/lon use case, and the Phase D processors are zone-membership processors that operate on `(asset, zone)` pairs rather than raw coordinates. Concretely: (1) [`docs/roadmap.md`](docs/roadmap.md) — Sprint 41 Phase D header gains a **"Coordinate-system scope"** blockquote spelling out that both processors emit `(asset, zone, confidence)` not `(x, y)`, that the membership primitives are `tag_reads.reader_id ∈ zones.fixed_reader_ids` (reader-bound) OR `(tag_reads.latitude, tag_reads.longitude) WITHIN zones.polygon_geojson` (WGS84 geofence), and that true `(x, y)` trilateration is a Sprint 45 / ADR-024 deliverable; (2) [`docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) §"Processor implementation" gains a new **"`signaling.attribution_settled` payload — coordinate-system-agnostic"** sub-section pinning the event-bus payload shape: `{tenant_id, asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers, rule_id}` — explicitly no `latitude`/`longitude`/`x`/`y`/`position_*` fields, with a forward pointer to ADR 024 for `asset_positions` per-asset position fixes; (3) [`docs/user-guide.md`](docs/user-guide.md) §"Zones — three kinds" gains a **"What about local `(x, y)` coordinates inside a warehouse?"** callout immediately after the three-kinds table, telling warehouse operators to model aisles as `reader_bound` zones today and pointing at ADR 024 for the sub-meter trilateration story. Together these three edits give Phase D a coordinate-system-explicit handoff so the implementation PR doesn't drift into half-baked XY-in-`polygon_geojson` hacks, and give customers a single answer to the "we use x/y not lat/lon" question. `docs/roadmap.md`, `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/user-guide.md`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase C — outbound webhook envelope upgrade (ADR-021 v2, closes remediation gap 2.9).** Adds five additive top-level fields to every rule-fired webhook payload (`confidence`, `keySet`, `eventConfigurationId`, `categoryId`, `labels`) so downstream consumers can reason about a fired event without a round-trip back to TagPulse to fetch the source rule or matched entity. Fires for **all rules** (legacy + signaling) — legacy rules get safe defaults (`confidence=1.0`, `keySet=[]`, `eventConfigurationId=str(rule_id)`, `categoryId=null`, `labels=[]`) so the change is fully additive: existing webhook consumers see every historical payload field unchanged and pick up five new keys they can ignore. Signaling rules populate `confidence` from `rules.confidence_threshold`, `keySet` from the per-event-type identity-key table (`location` → `["asset_id", "zone_id"]`, `geolocation` → `["asset_id", "site_id"]`, `geofencing` → `["asset_id", "zone_id"]`, `temperature` → `["asset_id"]`), and `eventConfigurationId` from `rules.id` — matches the worked example in [`docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md`](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md) §"dispatcher-layer envelope". **C1 builder module** [`src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py): pure (no I/O) `build_envelope(*, rule_id, event_type, confidence_threshold, category_id=None, labels=None) -> SignalingEnvelopeFields` + `derive_key_set(event_type) -> list[str]` + `_KEY_SETS` constant. Returns a `TypedDict` so callers spread it with `**envelope_fields` into the outer payload. Legacy branch pins `confidence=1.0` regardless of the threshold column value (the concept doesn't apply to legacy rules — the column is additive on every row); signaling branch coerces `Decimal` → `float` (`NUMERIC(3,2)` from PG arrives as `Decimal` in SQLAlchemy 2.0). Defensive: missing `rule_id` → `eventConfigurationId=None`; missing `confidence_threshold` on a signaling row → 0.0 ("all"); unknown `event_type` → empty `keySet`; `derive_key_set` returns a fresh list so callers can't corrupt the module-level table; `build_envelope` deep-copies `labels` so consumers can mutate without affecting cached matched-entity rows. **C2 dispatcher wiring** [`src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py): new `WebhookDispatcher._build_alert_envelope(session, payload) -> dict[str, Any]` helper looks up the source `RuleModel` once per tick (gated on `event.topic == Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` so raw broadcast events like `tag_read.created` and `telemetry.recorded` keep the pre-Phase-C envelope shape unchanged), calls `build_envelope` with the rule columns, and returns the five-field dict. `on_event` spreads `**envelope_fields` into the outer payload **once per tick** (not per integration — multiple subscribed webhooks share one DB lookup), positioned above `enrichments` so the existing "enrichments wins on key collision" precedent is preserved. Three defensive branches: missing `rule_id` → empty dict (no new fields, falls back to pre-Phase-C shape); malformed `rule_id` (not a UUID) → empty dict; unknown `rule_id` (deleted between publish and dispatch) → safe defaults populated from the rule_id in the payload. `categoryId`/`labels` stay at safe defaults for both legacy and signaling paths in Phase C — Phase D will wire the matched-entity lookup once OverlappingZones publishes the subject identity on its alert payload. **C3 conformance tests** — two new test files, 34 new tests total. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py) (24 tests, four `Test*` classes): `derive_key_set` for each of the 4 event_types + None + unknown + a fresh-copy regression guard; `build_envelope` legacy path (safe defaults; threshold column ignored; categoryId/labels passthrough when provided — Phase D forward-compat); signaling path (per-event_type keySet, `Decimal` and `float` threshold coercion, None threshold → 0.0 fallback, eventConfigurationId from rule_id, categoryId UUID/string normalization, labels propagation, empty-labels → empty-list, labels fresh-copy); defensive path (rule_id=None → eventConfigurationId=None, UUID serialization). [`tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py`](tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py) (10 tests, four `Test*` classes) exercises the full dispatcher path against an `httpx.MockTransport`-backed client so assertions run against the actual on-the-wire JSON body a consumer would receive, not just the in-memory dict: (a) legacy rule preserves every historical alert field + gains the 5 new fields with safe defaults; (b) signaling rule populates `confidence`/`keySet`/`eventConfigurationId` per event_type (parametrized over all 4); (c) non-`ALERT_TRIGGERED` events (`Topic.TAG_READ_CREATED`) emit pre-Phase-C envelope with no new fields injected (regression guard against accidental fan-out); defensive paths cover missing `rule_id`, unknown `rule_id` (deleted rule), and malformed `rule_id`. Test infrastructure: `_build_dispatcher_with_fake_session` wires a fully-mocked async session whose `session.get` dispatches on `model is RuleModel` / `model is IntegrationModel` so a single fake covers both the envelope-builder lookup and the post-deliver `last_triggered` update; `IntegrationService` is patched in the `webhook` module to a stub that returns a controlled integration list without touching the DB. **No behaviour change for existing rules' historical fields** — the new fields are additive top-level keys; webhook consumers that schema-validate get a one-line update to accept the new keys, consumers that ignore unknown JSON keys (the dominant case) see no break at all. Phase C closes [`reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) row 2.9 (outbound event envelope) and unblocks Phase D — the OverlappingZones processor needs the envelope to carry the `confidence` it computes. `src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py`, `src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py`, `tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase B — signaling-rule kind filter, per-scope cap enforcement, periodic dispatcher shell, and `signaling.attribution_settled` topic (ADR-021 v2).** Plumbing-only slice — wires the schema landed in Phase A through the service, API, worker, and event-bus layers without changing evaluator behaviour. Real processor logic lands in Phase D; the outbound-envelope upgrade lands in Phase C. **B1 schema extensions** in [`src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py): per-trigger Pydantic config models (`SignalingPeriodicConfig` cadence_minutes 1..1440, `SignalingOnChangeConfig` min_delta+cooldown_s, `SignalingOnInactivityConfig` inactivity_minutes+cooldown_s, `SignalingOnInferenceConfig` min_confidence∈[0,1], `SignalingOnEntryConfig` / `SignalingOnExitConfig` zone_id+optional subject_kinds, `SignalingOverlappingZonesProcessorConfig` aggregation_window_s∈{30,60,300,1800}); the `_SIGNALING_TRIGGER_CONFIGS` lookup table; the `validate_signaling_condition_config(condition_type, condition_config) -> BaseModel | None` helper that returns the parsed model for signaling condition_types, `None` for legacy, and raises `ValidationError` on a bad payload. `SIGNALING_DEFAULT_CAP_PER_SCOPE: int = 5` constant for the per-`(tenant_id, event_type, category_id)` active-signaling-rule cap. `RuleCreate` and `RuleUpdate` extended with the nine Phase A columns (`event_type`, `trigger`, `processor`, `confidence_threshold`, `category_ids`, `asset_label_filters`/`zone_label_filters`/`site_label_filters`, `integration_ids`); a `RuleCreate._signaling_columns_match_condition_type` model_validator auto-populates `event_type` and `trigger` from a `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` condition_type, rejects mismatched explicit values, and rejects signaling-only fields on legacy condition_types so a client can't smuggle a `category_ids=[…]` onto a `threshold` rule. `RuleResponse` gets a computed `kind: Literal["legacy","signaling"]` populated by a model_validator (event_type None → "legacy", else "signaling"); the validator overrides any caller-provided value so `kind` is always authoritative. **B1+B2 service** in [`src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py`](src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py): new `SignalingScopeCapExceededError(Exception)` carrying tenant_id, event_type, category_id, current_count, cap. `RulesService.create_rule(tenant_id, rule, *, allow_cap_override=False)` calls `validate_signaling_condition_config` then `_enforce_signaling_cap` (skipped on override). `RulesService.list_rules(tenant_id, *, enabled_only=False, kind=None)` filters via `RuleModel.event_type.is_(None)` for legacy / `.is_not(None)` for signaling — uses the existing `idx_rules_signaling_active` partial index from migration 040 for the signaling path. `RulesService.update_rule(tenant_id, rule_id, patch, *, allow_cap_override=False)` re-runs the cap when `event_type`/`category_ids`/`enabled` changes and re-runs the validator when `condition_type`/`condition_config` changes. `RulesService.count_active_signaling_rules_for_scope(tenant_id, event_type, category_id, *, exclude_rule_id)` uses `func.cardinality(RuleModel.category_ids) == 0` for the broadcast scope (`category_id IS NULL`) and the PG-idiomatic `literal(category_id) == any_(RuleModel.category_ids)` for a specific category — cleaner than `ARRAY.contains()` and avoids the pyright `Argument of type "list[UUID]" cannot be assigned` error. `_enforce_signaling_cap` raises `SignalingScopeCapExceededError` when count ≥ cap; legacy rules (event_type=None) and disabled rules short-circuit without invoking the counter. **B2 API routes** in [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py): `POST /rules` and `PATCH /rules/{id}` gain `override: bool = Query(default=False)` (admin-only — editor passing `?override=true` returns 403 before any DB work); `SignalingScopeCapExceededError` is mapped to HTTP 409 with structured detail `{"error": "signaling_scope_cap_exceeded", "event_type", "category_id", "current_count", "cap", "override_hint"}`; admin-with-override that touches a signaling rule writes one `audit_logs` row per call via `AuditLogger(session=session).log(..., action="signaling.cap_override", resource_type="rule", resource_id=<rule.id>, changes={event_type, category_ids})`. `GET /rules` gains `kind: Literal["legacy","signaling"] | None = Query(default=None)` for the discriminator filter; omitting the param returns all rules (backwards-compatible). **B3 worker shell** — new module [`src/tagpulse/signaling/`](src/tagpulse/signaling/) with `PeriodicSignalingDispatcher` in [`src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py): mirrors the existing `InventoryRuleWorker` lifecycle (`start`/`stop`/`_loop`/`run_once`); reads cadence from `condition_config.cadence_minutes` (1..1440, validated); tracks in-memory `_last_fired: dict[UUID, datetime]` for cadence accounting; iterates active rules whose `condition_type` is one of `SIGNALING_PERIODIC_CONDITION_TYPES = ("signaling.location.periodic", "signaling.geolocation.periodic", "signaling.temperature.periodic")` via the new `RulesService.get_active_rules_by_condition_types_all_tenants(...)` helper. Phase B implementation of `_evaluate_periodic_rule` is a shell — it logs and records a `rule_evaluations` usage-meter tick but doesn't create alerts yet (Phase D adds the real processor pipeline). Worker is wired into the FastAPI lifespan in [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) behind `settings.workers_inline=True`, alongside the existing dwell_worker / inventory_worker; stored on `app.state.periodic_signaling_dispatcher`. **B4 event bus** — new `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED = "signaling.attribution_settled"` in [`src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py`](src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py), in-process (per ADR-010) for the upcoming attribution-settled fan-out the location/geolocation/temperature processors will publish in Phase D. **B5 tests** — four new test modules + ~30 new tests in `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, ~50 new tests total: [`tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py) (4 tests — enum value, list iteration for WebhookDispatcher discovery, end-to-end publish+subscribe with `AsyncEventBus(capacity=100, overflow="raise")`, multi-subscriber fan-out); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py) (9 tests — condition_types match ADR; empty rules no-op; first tick fires all three rule types; second tick within cadence skips; tick after cadence elapsed fires + advances last_fired; multiple cadences independent; invalid cadence_minutes skipped with warning; evaluator hook records meter tick; start/stop lifecycle); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py) (15 tests covering cap enforcement at 4/5/6, legacy skip, disabled skip, broadcast scope, multi-category any-over-cap rejection, create_rule cap-check invocation, override bypass, invalid-config rejection before cap, legacy create unchanged, update enable re-checks cap, update override bypasses, list_rules SQL shape for kind=signaling/legacy/none); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py) (10 tests via FastAPI + ASGITransport + dependency_overrides covering GET ?kind=signaling/legacy/none/bogus, POST 409 detail shape, POST override admin-only 403, POST admin override 201 + audit row, POST override on legacy rule no audit, PATCH 409, PATCH admin override 200 + audit row). **`make check` clean**: 963 unit tests passing (+~50 from Phase A baseline), `ruff check` ✓, `mypy` ✓ (no issues in source files). No behaviour change for existing rules — the new fields default to None / empty / 0.0 / False so pre-Phase-B rules round-trip identically; the cap only applies to rules where `event_type IS NOT NULL`. Phase B is the gate to Phase C (envelope upgrade) and Phase D (real processor logic). `src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py`, `src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/__init__.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase A — schema + Pydantic foundation for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2).** Lays the groundwork for the rest of Sprint 41 by landing the additive schema + the discriminator helper the evaluator (Phase B), envelope (Phase C), and API (Phase E) will all build on. **Migration `040_rules_signaling_events.py`** extends `rules` with nine additive columns — `event_type VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `trigger VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `processor VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `confidence_threshold NUMERIC(3,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0.0`, `category_ids UUID[] NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'`, `asset_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `zone_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `site_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `integration_ids UUID[] NULL` — all nullable or defaulted so existing rows survive untouched; `event_type IS NULL` is the implicit `kind = legacy` discriminator the API + UI use to keep the new "Signaling Events" namespace separate from pre-existing rules. Plus partial index `idx_rules_signaling_active ON rules (tenant_id, event_type, trigger) WHERE enabled = true AND event_type IS NOT NULL` that keeps the upcoming evaluator's hot path narrow (only currently-enabled signaling rules show up — no full table scan on a tenant that has thousands of legacy rules and zero signaling rules yet). `trigger` is a non-reserved keyword in PostgreSQL so the column does not need quoting; matches ADR-021 verbatim. `RuleModel` in [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py) mirrors the migration with proper types (`Decimal` for `confidence_threshold`, `ARRAY(UUID(as_uuid=True))` for the two UUID arrays — first use of `ARRAY` in the codebase), all with server-defaults matching the migration so SQLAlchemy and Postgres agree on the default values. **Pydantic foundation** in [`src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py): `_RULE_CONDITION_PATTERN` regex extended with the 12 new `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` values, each `(event_type, trigger)` pair listed explicitly so impossible combinations like `signaling.temperature.on_entry` reject at parse time rather than reaching the evaluator. New `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS: dict[str, frozenset[str]]` constant is the authoritative map of which triggers are legal for each event type (`location` gets all 4 non-spatial triggers including `on_inference`; `geolocation` and `temperature` get the same minus `on_inference`; `geofencing` gets only `on_entry` / `on_exit` — entry/exit are spatial primitives that don't apply to subject-bound metric streams, and `on_inference` only makes sense for location attribution). `SIGNALING_PROCESSORS: ("isolated_zones", "overlapping_zones")` constant for symmetric lookup. New `split_signaling_condition_type(condition_type: str) -> tuple[str, str] | None` helper is the in-process discriminator the upcoming evaluator + service will use to route a rule's condition_type to its (event_type, trigger) handlers without re-parsing strings — returns `None` for legacy `condition_type` values, signaling-shaped-but-invalid pairs (the regex would also reject these before they reach the helper, but the helper is defensive), and malformed inputs; the tuple-returning case is guaranteed to be one of the 12 valid pairs in `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS`. **Tests**: 51 new unit tests in [`tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`](tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py) — `TestSignalingConditionTypes` parametrizes all 12 valid pairs through `RuleCreate` (asserts each is accepted), a fail-list of 16 invalid pairs (cross-product errors like `signaling.temperature.on_entry`, made-up event types like `signaling.humidity.on_change`, wrong namespace depth like `signaling.location.on_change.extra`, wrong prefix like `signal.location.on_change`), a regression guard ensuring all 10 legacy `condition_type` values still validate, and a `test_twelve_pairs_is_the_full_matrix` count-check that trips if the regex and `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS` ever drift apart; `TestSplitSignalingConditionType` parametrizes the 12 valid pairs through the helper (asserts each returns the expected tuple) plus a 10-case fail-list (legacy types return None, signaling-shaped-but-invalid returns None, wrong shape / empty string return None). Full unit suite delta: +51 tests; `python -m pytest tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py` → 58 passed (was 7). **Docs**: [`docs/data-models.md`](docs/data-models.md) §"rules" table updated with the nine new columns + the `idx_rules_signaling_active` partial-index note + Migration column updated to "006 (initial), 040 (Sprint 41 signaling-event columns + partial index)"; `condition_type` Notes column updated from the stale "threshold, absence, rate_change" to spell out "10 legacy values … + 12 signaling values (`signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>`) per ADR-021 v2"; new `signaling.*.periodic` condition-config example added under #### Condition config shapes (cadence_minutes + processor_config nested block). **Terminology note**: this PR also renames `sensing` → `signaling` throughout the new Phase A code + ADR-021 v2 content + Sprint 41 roadmap plan, aligning with Azure-Monitor's "Signal → Condition → Action" vocabulary that the deferred Sprint 4X taxonomy-cleanup ADR will ratify. The ADR file path (`docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`) stays for link stability; the title + body are updated. Historical CHANGELOG entries (PR #45, #51, vendor-neutrality sweep) that reference "Sensing Events" are intentionally left as-is — they describe shipped work as-written. **Out of scope for this slice (still part of Sprint 41 Phase A, follow-up commits on this PR)**: full Pydantic discriminated-union BaseModel per trigger (`SignalingPeriodicConfig`, `SignalingOverlappingZonesProcessorConfig`) — deferred to Phase B where the evaluator actually consumes them; integration test for migration round-trip + index predicate verification — covered by the existing `tests/integration/test_migration_round_trip.py` harness via `make migration-check` (requires a TimescaleDB container so it's CI-gated, not part of `make check`). No behaviour change yet — the new columns are additive and nothing reads them until Phase B lands the evaluator. `migrations/versions/040_rules_signaling_events.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, `docs/data-models.md`, `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`.

- **`docs/roadmap.md` — Sprint 41 plan section: Configurable Sensing Events (ADR 021 v2) + ADR 019 closure + UI navigation overhaul.** Locks scope for the next sprint per the canonical-plan rule reasserted in PR #51. New `## Sprint 41 — Configurable Sensing Events (ADR 021 v2)` section inserted between the "Methodology drift in Sprints 36–40" subsection and the `## Backlog (not scheduled)` heading. **Eight phases** (A schema migration → B evaluator + service → C outbound envelope upgrade → D processor implementations → E API surface → F UI → G docs + remediation reconciliation → **H drop `assets.asset_type` to close [ADR 019](docs/adr/019-categories.md)**), each with planned-item bullets that name the exact files, columns, condition_type values, event-bus topics, and remediation rows they touch. Phase H is a **breaking API change** — drops the `?asset_type=` query param (returns HTTP 400 with a `?category_id=` hint for one release), removes `asset_type` from `AssetCreate` / `AssetUpdate` / `AssetResponse`, drops the column itself, and backfills `category_id` to NOT NULL; the EPC parser `asset_type` bits stay (they are RFID-binary semantics, not the DB column). Includes an explicit "Out of scope" subsection naming the **five deferrals** (ADR 023 MQTT → Sprint 42, ADR 024 Position Estimation → Sprint 45 — depends on this sprint's `processor` enum being live, legacy-rule backfill of `category_ids` / `*_label_filters`, Postgres ENUM migration for `condition_type`, EPC-parser variable rename) so future audits don't refile them as gaps. Sprint workstream PR is opened by `scripts/start-sprint.sh 41 sensing-events` per the canonical convention after this section lands; this PR is the planning lock so the implementation PR has scope to point at. Pure documentation — no source, no tests, no migration, no behaviour change; `make check` clean. `docs/roadmap.md`.

- **Repo vendor-neutrality sweep — scrub external-product brand name + contributor-local sibling-repo paths + vendor-specific tag terminology (forward-only).** Repositions TagPulse as an independent Azure IoT learning project (FastAPI + TimescaleDB + Container Apps + Key Vault + MQTT) by removing the one literal external-product brand mention, the 14 references to a contributor-local sibling-repo path that leaked the filesystem layout of one machine, and the ~10 vendor-specific tag-terminology hits that traced back to a single proprietary vocabulary. All wording is neutralized to "an external IoT cloud-platform reference design (held locally as a learning aid, not committed to this repo)" with audits renamed to "schema/API audit notes" and "UI/IA audit notes". Vendor-specific terminology replaced with TagPulse-native equivalents throughout (the foreign word for "RFID tag" → `tag`; the foreign word for "tag registry" → `tag registry`; the foreign word for "tags page" / "tags nav item" → `Tags page` / `Tags nav item`; the foreign phrase for "exact visual parity" → `visual-perfect parity`). Six docs touched ([docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) — brand mention + all sibling-path hits + all terminology hits + new §7 vendor-neutrality clause; [docs/adr/019-categories.md](docs/adr/019-categories.md), [docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md](docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md), [docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md), [docs/adr/022-soft-assets.md](docs/adr/022-soft-assets.md), [docs/adr/023-outbound-connections-mqtt-kafka.md](docs/adr/023-outbound-connections-mqtt-kafka.md) — `Implements:` frontmatter + body terminology; [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md) — Categories terminology aside), one source file ([src/tagpulse/models/database.py](src/tagpulse/models/database.py) — `CategoryModel` docstring), one migration ([migrations/versions/037_categories.py](migrations/versions/037_categories.py) — module docstring), and this CHANGELOG (sprint-33 entry + the line above). Forward-only: history-rewrite of already-pushed commits was intentionally **not** performed — earlier commits keep their original wording in the published git history; new commits going forward use the neutral wording. PR descriptions on GitHub that link to the affected docs may still contain the original phrasing and are out of repo control; edit them in the GitHub UI if a fully-clean external surface is required. No code behaviour change, no schema change, no test change — pure documentation/docstring rewording. `make check` clean.

- **`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` — Sprint 39 row 2.2a flipped Commit → ✅ Done.** ADR 020 Phase B orphan `entity_labels` cleanup landed in [#47 `7ce3292`](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/commit/7ce3292) per the previous Sprint 39 bullet (the slice that wired `TimescaleLabelRepository.delete_for_entity` into the three hard-delete repository methods for sites, zones, and categories). §3.1 row 2.2a Status column updated from **🟠 Commit (in flight, #47)** to **✅ Done ([#47](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/47), `7ce3292`) / 39**; Notes column unchanged (still spells out the polymorphic-FK reason that `count_associations()` overcounts when orphans exist, and the soft-delete vs hard-delete split that makes assets and devices intentionally exempt). Doc update only — no source, no tests, no migration. Closes the lone ADR 020 Phase B clause that survived the Sprint 35 ship train. `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`.

- **Sprint 39 — ADR 020 Phase B: orphan `entity_labels` cleanup on hard-delete entity handlers (row 2.2a).** Closes the lone unshipped clause of ADR 020 — "Orphan cleanup happens in the entity-delete handlers (Phase B)" — that survived the Sprint 35 Phases A/C/D/E ship train. The problem: sites, zones, and categories hard-delete via `await self._session.delete(row)` in [`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py) and [`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/categories.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/categories.py) with no cleanup of the polymorphic `entity_labels` rows that pointed at them. The `entity_labels` table holds a regular `label_id` FK to `labels` (`ON DELETE RESTRICT` per the ADR / Phase A) but **only a polymorphic `entity_id`** to the owning entity (no FK — couldn't have one because the same column targets five different tables), so the entity-delete path leaves the association rows behind as dangling pointers. `count_associations()` on the parent label (in [`labels.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py)) cannot join the entity table for tenant scope — that join is impossible for the polymorphic case — so orphan rows are indistinguishable from live ones and **inflate the count permanently**. Concrete user-visible failure mode: an admin deletes the three sites that were all tagged `priority=p1`, then tries to delete the now-unused `priority` label via `DELETE /labels/{id}`, and gets back `409 Conflict { "message": "Label … still has 3 association(s)", "association_count": 3 }` even though `GET /sites?labels[priority]=p1` returns the empty array. The 409 is unresolvable from the UI because `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` looks up by `(entity_type, entity_id)` and the operator has no way to discover which dead `entity_id`s the orphan rows point at. The fix adds `TimescaleLabelRepository.delete_for_entity(tenant_id, entity_type, entity_id) -> int` (placed alongside the existing `disassociate` method since it's the catalog-table sibling) that runs a tenant-scoped JOIN-then-delete: `SELECT entity_labels WHERE entity_labels.entity_id = :eid JOIN labels ON labels.tenant_id = :tid AND labels.entity_type = :etype` and then `session.delete(row)` per match, returning the row count for audit/observability. Tenant scoping is done via the JOIN to `labels.tenant_id` rather than a bare `DELETE … WHERE entity_id = …` because the association table has no `tenant_id` column of its own — matching the rest of the module's tenant-scoping pattern (`disassociate`, `count_associations`, `get_association`). The new method is wired into the three hard-delete repository methods *before* `await self._session.delete(row)` is called, so the cleanup and the entity delete are in the same transaction and either both happen or neither does. Order: (1) `TimescaleSiteRepository.delete` — call `delete_for_entity(tenant_id, "site", site_id)` between the existing `select … scalar_one_or_none()` and `session.delete(row)`; cache invalidation unchanged. (2) `TimescaleZoneRepository.delete` — same pattern with `"zone"`; `_geofence_cache_invalidate(tenant_id)` still runs after the flush. (3) `TimescaleCategoryRepository.delete` — same pattern with `"category"`, placed *after* the existing `CategoryInUseError` guard (which protects against asset references, not label references — a category with labels but zero assets used to fall through to a successful delete that leaked labels; now it cleans up properly). Asset and device hard deletes do not exist — assets soft-delete to `status='retired'` via `TimescaleAssetRepository.delete` and devices soft-delete via `POST /devices/{id}/decommission`. Both are **intentionally** unchanged because soft-delete keeps the entity row alive, label associations remain valid (and historically useful: a retired asset still shows its tagged `building=warehouse-a` location for audit purposes), and the row's `status` discriminator means the entity won't appear in default list queries anyway. The `delete_for_entity` method is a no-op (returns 0, skips the flush) when the entity had no labels — the cheap path for the common case. The module docstring in [`labels.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py) is updated to mention `delete_for_entity` in the association-methods list with a cross-reference to the calling sites. **Tests:** new [`tests/unit/test_orphan_label_cleanup.py`](tests/unit/test_orphan_label_cleanup.py) (4 tests) pins the contract for the three hard-delete repository methods using an in-memory `_RecordingSession` that captures every `execute` / `delete` / `flush` in order so the test can assert (a) `TimescaleSiteRepository.delete` issues two SELECTs (entity lookup + orphan SELECT) before the `session.delete(row)`, with the orphan SELECT compiling to SQL containing `from entity_labels`, `join labels`, `labels.tenant_id`, and `labels.entity_type`; (b) when the entity SELECT returns `None` the orphan cleanup is **skipped entirely** (no second execute, no delete) and `delete()` returns `False` — defends against a regression that would run an orphan SELECT against a tenant the caller doesn't actually own a row in; (c) `TimescaleZoneRepository.delete` follows the same contract with the orphan SELECT containing `labels.entity_type` and `entity_labels.entity_id`; (d) `TimescaleCategoryRepository.delete` runs three SELECTs in the right order — `count_referencing_assets` first (which raises `CategoryInUseError` and short-circuits the rest if the count is non-zero), then category lookup, then orphan cleanup — before the `session.delete(row)` and the `flush`. Plus 4 new repository-level tests in [`tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py`](tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py) under a new `TestDeleteForEntity` class: (1) `test_select_is_tenant_scoped_via_labels_join` compiles the SELECT and asserts `join labels`, `labels.tenant_id`, `labels.entity_type`, and `entity_labels.entity_id` all appear (regression guard against a future refactor that drops the JOIN and tries to use a bare `tenant_id` predicate that doesn't exist on `entity_labels`); (2) `test_returns_zero_when_no_orphans` confirms the empty-result path returns 0 and skips the `flush()` (cheap path matters because most entity deletes will have zero labels — paying a transaction flush per empty cleanup would matter under load); (3) `test_deletes_each_row_and_flushes_once` confirms multiple rows are deleted individually via `session.delete(row)` (so SQLAlchemy's identity map sees each removal — important if anything else in the same transaction touches `entity_labels`) but `flush()` runs exactly once; (4) `test_predicates_bind_entity_type_and_id` compiles with `literal_binds=True` and asserts the entity_type literal and entity_id UUID both appear in the compiled SQL string (defends against accidental string coercion or predicate drop). The shared `_CapturingSession` helper in `test_labels_repository.py` mirrors the dialect-compile pattern already established by `tests/unit/test_assets_repository_filters.py` (Sprint 37 row 2.8a) — no Postgres needed, compiles against the postgres dialect via `sqlalchemy.dialects.postgresql`. Full unit suite: 821 passed + 1 skipped (was 817 + 1 before; +4 in `test_labels_repository.py`, new file `test_orphan_label_cleanup.py` adds 4). `make check` clean: `ruff check` ✓, `mypy` ✓ (no issues in 103 source files). **Doc updates**: new row 2.2a in §3.1 of [`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) tracks the slice (Severity 🟠, Decision **Commit (in flight, #47)**) with the full failure-mode explainer and call-site list; row 2.2 itself is untouched (remains ✅ Done — the original five-PR ship train still owns Phases A/C/D/E and that decision didn't change). Will flip 2.2a → ✅ Done with the merge SHA per the doc's own §7 update-rule once #47 lands. No migration needed — the schema is correct as shipped in Sprint 35; this is a pure repository-layer logic bug. No API change — every behavioural change is internal to the entity-delete repository methods; HTTP responses are unaffected. `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/categories.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py`, `tests/unit/test_orphan_label_cleanup.py`, `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase E — Labels docs + remediation flip.** Closes out the Sprint 35 backend story by documenting the labels surface for end users and updating the scope-lock doc to reflect what shipped. New `## Labels` section in [`docs/user-guide.md`](docs/user-guide.md) (between **Inventory** and **Tenant Settings**, with a matching TOC entry) covers the four things an operator actually needs to know: (1) where labels sit relative to Categories (the single primary-classification slot on assets) and the `metadata` JSONB escape hatch (long blobs, structured nested data, integration-specific payloads); (2) the two-level catalog + associations model — a catalog row defines what `key` can exist for a given `entity_type`, an association attaches a `(key, value)` pair to a specific entity instance, and the same `key` is independent across entity types so `location` on Assets and `location` on Sites don't collide; (3) the eight tenant-scoped endpoints with explicit role gates per row (`GET /labels` viewer+, `POST/PATCH /labels` editor/admin, `DELETE /labels/{id}` admin-only with `409 + association_count`; `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` viewer+, `POST` editor/admin with `409 + cap:30`, `DELETE` editor/admin) — the URL segment is plural (`assets`/`sites`/`zones`/`devices`/`categories`) per the existing REST convention and lookup happens by `(tenant, entity_type, lower(key))` so clients never need to know the synthetic catalog UUID to attach a value; (4) the deep-object `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on `GET /assets`/`/sites`/`/zones`/`/devices` with worked examples from ADR 020 (single pair, multi-key AND, comma-separated OR within a key, the four-key combined form), the AND-across-keys-OR-within-values semantics spelled out, the three guard rails repeated verbatim (≤ 5 distinct keys/request, ≤ 20 values/key, value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$`), the explicit rejection of the repeated-parallel `?label.key=X&label.value=Y` form (query-param order isn't guaranteed across middleware), and a tagging-a-Boston-asset walkthrough showing `curl` invocations for catalog create → association attach → filtered list with `--data-urlencode` for the `[`/`]` characters. Format rules table reproduces the key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$`, value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$`, optional `#RRGGBB` color, case-insensitive key uniqueness per `(tenant, entity_type)`, and the 30-per-entity cap with its dual API + DB trigger enforcement. The five audit-log event names emitted on every mutation (`label.created`, `label.updated` only when `_diff` is non-empty, `label.deleted`, `label.associated`, `label.disassociated`) are cross-linked from the existing **Audit Log** section's preset filters. [`docs/operator-quickstart.md`](docs/operator-quickstart.md) is **intentionally untouched** — that doc is strictly operations (deploys, alert routing, on-call triage cheat-sheet) and labels are a feature surface, not an operational concern; bolting on a Pointers-section link just to tick the original Phase E checklist would have been bookkeeping noise. [`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) row 2.2 (Labels first-class) flipped **Commit → ✅ Done** with all four implementing PRs and short SHAs ([#36](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/36) `fd38046` kickoff · [#37](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/37) `c5db1a7` schema · [#38](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/38) `fe0b732` API · [#39](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/39) `4493a02` filter) per the doc's own §7 "Updating this document" rule; row 3.9 (Asset Detail Events Log tab + Labels chips) **stays Commit** because the chips half is UI work in TagPulse-UI that hasn't shipped, but gains an annotation that the backend prerequisites are now in place (links back to row 2.2) so the chip PR isn't blocked on more backend work. The §2 sprint roadmap bullet for Sprint 35 flipped from `🟡 in flight` to `✅ backend shipped — … UI chips pending TagPulse-UI` with all four PR links inline. `docs/user-guide.md`, `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase C — Labels deep-object filter (ADR 020).** Lights up the `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on the four entity list endpoints (`GET /assets`, `GET /sites`, `GET /zones`, `GET /devices`) that Phase B intentionally deferred. New module `src/tagpulse/api/label_filter.py` exposes two purpose-built primitives. (1) `parse_label_filter(query_params)` — pure parser over Starlette's `QueryParams.multi_items()` so duplicate `labels[KEY]=…` entries on the same request merge correctly; returns `dict[str, list[str]] | None` (`None` when no `labels[...]` keys are present so the call site can short-circuit), raises `LabelFilterError(ValueError)` on any guard-rail violation. Guard rails mirror ADR 020 §"Filter encoding" verbatim: ≤ 5 distinct keys/request (`LABEL_FILTER_MAX_KEYS`), ≤ 20 values/key (`LABEL_FILTER_MAX_VALUES_PER_KEY`), key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$` and value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (imported from `schemas.py` so the catalog and the filter can't drift), and any empty segment — leading comma, trailing comma, double comma, or fully-empty `labels[k]=` — rejects with `"Empty value …"` rather than silently matching nothing. Keys fold to lowercase so `labels[Location]=` and `labels[location]=` merge into one bucket (matches the catalog's `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` functional unique index from migration 039); values stay case-sensitive. (2) `apply_label_filter(stmt, *, tenant_id, entity_type, entity_id_col, labels)` — pure SQLAlchemy applicator that appends one correlated `EXISTS` per key onto the caller's `Select`, joining `entity_labels → labels` and binding `LabelModel.tenant_id = :tid AND LabelModel.entity_type = :et AND lower(LabelModel.key) = lower(:key) AND EntityLabelModel.value IN (:v1, :v2, …)`. Tenant scoping is enforced inside the EXISTS — a guess-the-UUID attack on another tenant's label can't bypass the `tenant_id` check on the join side. The four list routes now accept `request: Request`, run the parser, surface `LabelFilterError` as a 400, and pass `labels=` through their service. Service signatures (`AssetService.list_assets`, `SiteZoneService.list_sites` / `.list_zones`, `DeviceService.list_devices`) gained the `labels: dict[str, list[str]] | None = None` kwarg (default `None` preserves existing call sites). Repository `.list()` methods on `TimescaleAssetRepository`, the site + zone repos, and `TimescaleDeviceRepository` now invoke `apply_label_filter` between their existing per-field WHEREs and the `ORDER BY / LIMIT / OFFSET` tail. `DeviceRepository` Protocol updated to mirror the new kwarg. **Why the manual `Request.query_params` parse instead of a typed FastAPI `Query` parameter:** OpenAPI 3.0 supports `style: deepObject, explode: true` (which is what ADR 020 specifies) but FastAPI's `Query()` machinery doesn't surface deep-object query params as a single typed value — the `[`/`]` characters in the param name aren't legal Python identifiers and Pydantic v2 won't bind them. Going through `request.query_params.multi_items()` keeps the route signature clean, lets the guard-rail errors return a real 400 with a useful message, and crucially **does not change the generated `openapi.json`** (the spec gate stays green without manual schema patches — verified locally). **AND across keys, OR within values** is the SQL contract: each key adds one `EXISTS`, and within an EXISTS the value list compiles to `entity_labels.value IN (…)` — equivalent to the ADR's example SQL. Performance shape is index-friendly: each `EXISTS` is a fast probe via `entity_labels(label_id, entity_id)` PK + `labels(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` functional unique index. **Tests:** 50 new unit tests in `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py` cover parser happy-path (single pair, multi-key AND, comma-split OR, the four-key combined form from the ADR), duplicate-key merge, dedup-within-key, key case-folding, the full guard-rail matrix (max keys + at-max accepted, max values + at-max accepted, parametrised key + value regex with allowed and disallowed inputs, empty/leading/trailing/double comma all rejected), `apply_label_filter` pass-through for `None` and `{}`, and SQL-shape assertions (compile against the postgres dialect with `literal_binds=True` so the test reads what the DB actually sees: one EXISTS per key, `entity_type` bound to the singular form, key bound lowercased). The existing fake repositories in `tests/unit/test_device_service.py` and `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py` picked up the new `labels=` kwarg (accepted-but-ignored at the fake layer — repository-level SQL behaviour is covered in the new test module). Full unit suite now 807 tests (+50 from Phase B's 757). `src/tagpulse/api/label_filter.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/devices.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/sites_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/device_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/sites_zones_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/devices.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py`, `tests/unit/test_device_service.py`, `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase B — Labels API (ADR 020).** Builds the catalog + per-entity association REST surface on top of the Phase A schema. **Pydantic schemas** in `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py` add `LabelEntityType` (`Literal["asset","site","zone","device","category"]`, lockstep with the migration 039 `CHECK` literal list), `LabelCreate` (`entity_type` + `key` + optional `color`), `LabelUpdate` (`key` / `color` only — `entity_type` is intentionally absent because ADR 020 declares it immutable), `LabelResponse` (full row inc. `created_by` / `updated_by` opaque JWT UUIDs), `LabelAssociationCreate` (`key` + `value`; the repository looks up the catalog row by `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` rather than requiring the client to know the synthetic UUID), and `LabelAssociationResponse` (joined view carrying `entity_type` / `key` / `color` alongside the polymorphic `entity_id`). All regex patterns mirror the DB `CHECK` constraints exactly — `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$` for keys, `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` for values (hyphen-included per the Phase A contradiction fix), `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$` for colours. **TimescaleDB repository** in `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py` (`TimescaleLabelRepository`) provides `list_for_tenant` / `get` / `find_by_key` / `create` / `update` / `count_associations` / `delete` for the catalog, plus `list_for_entity` / `get_association` / `associate` / `disassociate` for the per-entity surface. Domain exceptions (`LabelKeyConflictError` extends `ValueError`; `LabelInUseError` and `LabelCapExceededError` extend `RuntimeError`) replace raw `IntegrityError` so the route layer doesn't have to know about SQLSTATEs. A pure `_pg_sqlstate(exc)` helper normalises asyncpg's `.sqlstate` and psycopg2's `.pgcode` so the same error mapping works under either driver; mapped codes are `23505` → `LabelKeyConflictError` (functional unique index on `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` or composite PK collision on `entity_labels`) and `23514` → `LabelCapExceededError` (raised by the `trg_enforce_label_cap` BEFORE INSERT trigger on the 31st row per entity). `LabelCapExceededError.CAP = 30` is asserted in tests so any future cap bump trips the unit suite if the migration and the constant drift. Tenant scoping on the polymorphic `entity_labels` side is enforced by joining through `labels` on every read and delete — never by `label_id` alone — so a guess-the-UUID attack on another tenant cannot disassociate their rows. **Routes** in `src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py` ship eight endpoints per ADR 020 §"API path deviation": `GET /labels?entity_type=` (viewer+), `POST /labels` (editor/admin), `GET /labels/{id}` (viewer+), `PATCH /labels/{id}` (editor/admin; 400 if the payload smuggles `entity_type`), `DELETE /labels/{id}` (admin only; 409 with `{"message": ..., "association_count": N}` if in use), `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` (viewer+), `POST /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` (editor/admin; 404 if the key isn't in the catalog, 409 with `{"message": ..., "cap": 30}` on cap, 409 on duplicate), and `DELETE /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels/{label_id}` (editor/admin). The URL segment is the **plural** form (`assets` / `sites` / `zones` / `devices` / `categories`) per the existing REST convention; an `_ENTITY_TYPE_FROM_URL` mapping bridges to the singular DB value, and an unknown segment returns 404 ("Unknown entity kind") before any DB work happens. A `_diff(before, after)` helper builds the audit `changes` dict over the `key` / `color` field pair only (mirrors the Categories pattern); `updated_at` is intentionally excluded so a no-op PATCH doesn't write a noise audit row. **Audit log events** emitted via `AuditLogger(session=session).log(...)`: `label.created`, `label.updated` (only when `_diff` is non-empty), `label.deleted`, `label.associated`, `label.disassociated`. **OTel counter** `tagpulse_labels_associations_total{tenant_id, entity_type}` added to `src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py` and incremented on every successful `POST /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels`, so dashboards can spot tenants approaching the 30-per-entity cap or track tag-driven inventory growth per entity kind. **Router wiring** in `src/tagpulse/api/main.py` adds `labels_router` import (alphabetical, between `inventory_imports_router` and `metrics_router`) and the matching `app.include_router(labels_router)` at the end of the include block (after Categories). **Tests**: 64 schema tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_schemas.py` cover `LabelCreate` (entity-type enum, key length / regex parametrised across allowed + disallowed chars, color hex validation), `LabelUpdate` (empty-payload accepted, `entity_type` not in `model_fields`, `exclude_unset=True` keeps explicit `color=None` clearable), `LabelAssociationCreate` (value length / regex, hyphen accepted per the Phase A contradiction fix), `LabelAssociationResponse` (kwargs round-trip), and `_diff` (no-change → empty, single-field changes, both-field changes, explicit clear-to-null); 12 repository-helper tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py` cover `_pg_sqlstate` (asyncpg `.sqlstate` vs psycopg2 `.pgcode`, both-present preference, none-present return), the three domain exceptions (class hierarchy, payload, `CAP=30` constant), parametrised across the three classes. Full unit suite now 757 tests (+76 from Phase A's 681). The deep-object `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on `/assets` / `/sites` / `/zones` / `/devices` is deliberately deferred to Phase C — it's cross-cutting across four routers + four services + four repositories, and warrants its own focused review window. `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase A — Labels catalog schema (ADR 020).** Migration `039_labels_catalog.py` introduces two tenant-scoped tables. (1) `labels` — catalog of label *keys* scoped to one `entity_type` (`asset` / `site` / `zone` / `device` / `category`); functional UNIQUE index on `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` enforces case-insensitive uniqueness per entity-type slot (so `location` on Sites and `location` on Assets are independent). DB-side CHECK constraints enforce the `entity_type` enum, the key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$`, and the optional `color` regex `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$`. (2) `entity_labels` — polymorphic association `(label_id, entity_id, value)`; `label_id` FK is **`ON DELETE RESTRICT`** so deleting a catalog row that's still referenced returns 409 + `association_count` at the API layer (matches the Categories pattern from ADR 019, *not* the CASCADE the original ADR draft showed). `entity_id` has no FK — it points polymorphically at `assets` / `sites` / `zones` / `devices` / `categories` rows; orphan cleanup happens in the entity-delete handlers in Phase B, not in the DB. Value regex is `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (hyphen added vs the ADR draft so `warehouse-a` style values actually validate; matches k8s/AWS/GCP tag value conventions). A `enforce_label_cap()` PL/pgSQL function + `BEFORE INSERT` trigger backstops the 30-labels-per-entity cap; SQLSTATE `23514` surfaces as a 409 in the API. RLS is enabled on both tables (theatre-only per the repo convention; the app filters explicitly by `tenant_id` in every query). `LabelModel` + `EntityLabelModel` ORM classes in `src/tagpulse/models/database.py` mirror the migration; `created_by` / `updated_by` are plain `UUID NULL` columns without an FK (no `users` table in TagPulse — auth is JWT-based, mirrors `audit_logs.user_id` from migration 015). 16 new unit tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_models.py` introspect the ORM shape so anyone editing the migration without touching the models (or vice versa) trips a fast unit test before the integration suite runs. Three contradictions in the merged ADR 020 are fixed alongside the schema that crystallizes them: (a) `ON DELETE CASCADE` → `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (consistent with the 409 spec in the §"API path deviation" section), (b) value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.]{1,64}$` → `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (so the §"Filter encoding" `warehouse-a` examples validate), (c) `created_by/updated_by UUID REFERENCES users(id)` → `UUID` (no FK; no `users` table exists). The original `/v1/tenants/{slug}/...` API surface block in the ADR is now explicitly labelled "superseded by §'API path deviation' below" so future readers don't think two endpoint shapes were specified. `migrations/versions/039_labels_catalog.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_models.py`, `docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md`.

- **Sprint 35 kickoff — ADR 020 Labels first-class ratified.** Status flipped **Proposed → Accepted** at the start of the implementing sprint. The three Open Questions are now closed inline: (Q1) `entity_type` is a `CHECK` constraint with a literal list (`'asset','site','zone','device','category'`) — matches the Categories `category_type` precedent in ADR 019, avoids enum-add-value migrations later; (Q2) pre-seeded common keys (`location`, `owner`, `priority`) are **deferred** until one cycle of operator UX feedback on the chip UI; (Q3) cross-entity label propagation is **out of scope** for this ADR (separate follow-up if a customer asks; the `entity_labels` shape doesn't preclude it). Added a §"API path deviation" subsection capturing that shipped paths are `/labels` + `/{entity_type}/{id}/labels` rather than the original `/v1/tenants/{slug}/...` draft (matches the Categories deviation in ADR 019). Added a §"Filter encoding" subsection specifying that label-based filters on existing list endpoints (`GET /assets`, `/sites`, `/zones`, `/devices`) use **OpenAPI `style: deepObject, explode: true`** with semantics **AND across distinct keys, OR within comma-separated values of the same key** (e.g. `?labels[location]=warehouse-a,warehouse-b&labels[priority]=high`). Same shape as Prometheus/Loki/Grafana label selectors. Guard rails: ≤ 5 distinct keys/request, ≤ 20 values/key, each value matches `^[A-Za-z0-9_.]{1,64}$`. Repeated-parallel `?label.key=X&label.value=Y` form is explicitly rejected (query-param order not guaranteed across middleware). SQL shape is one correlated `EXISTS` per key, fast via the existing `entity_labels(label_id, entity_id)` PK + `labels(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` unique index. The cap-30 `BEFORE INSERT` trigger backstop got concrete `enforce_label_cap()` plpgsql in the schema block. §2 of `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` now marks Sprint 35 as **🟡 in flight** linking [#36](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/36); rows 2.2 + 3.9 (chips half) will flip to ✅ Done per §7 when the implementing PR merges. `docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md`.

Added a new §3.3 row for **QW4 `<LastUpdate timestamp onRefresh/>`** widget so it's tracked alongside the other quick-wins. The 2.1 / QW6 rows also pick up the colour-swap note: the default `colorPrimary` is **Tailwind blue-600 `#2563eb`** (was teal `#0d9488` during planning) to match the reference design's primary accent. Per the §7 update-rule in the doc itself.
- **`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` — sprint 33/34 status hygiene.** Flipped the seven rows whose implementing PRs have merged: backend 2.1 (Categories) / 2.6 (`installer` role ride-along) / 2.7 (sites structured-address) / 2.8 (`assets.category_id` + `external_ref`) plus UI 1.1 Categories nav item / 3.2 Locations two-tab (tabs portion; Soft Assets column still waits for ADR 022 / Sprint 39) / 3.3 Categories page. Each row now carries the merge PR + short SHA so the table is a true status board rather than a planning artefact.
