Per the §7 update-rule in the doc itself.
- **Sprint 34 sites structured-address + Site/Transporter discriminator (gap 2.7).** Adds the Site vs. Transporter distinction and the geolocation + structured-address columns required by the Locations UI redesign. Alembic migration `038_sites_structured.py` adds `sites.kind VARCHAR(16) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'site'` with `CHECK (kind IN ('site','transporter'))`, `latitude` / `longitude` DOUBLE PRECISION with per-axis range CHECKs **and** an `ck_sites_latlon_paired` both-or-neither invariant, and `street_line1` / `street_line2` / `city` / `region` / `postal_code` / `country` (CHAR(2) with `~ '^[A-Z]{2}$'` CHECK for ISO 3166-1 alpha-2). Existing rows backfill to `kind='site'`; lat/lon and structured-address columns are nullable so the migration is online and zero-downtime. The legacy free-form `sites.address` TEXT column is **retained this release as a compatibility shadow** (mirrors the Sprint 34 categories `assets.asset_type` precedent — drop in a later migration once UI + clients have switched). `SiteCreate` / `SiteUpdate` gain matching fields with Pydantic validators: lat in `[-90, 90]` and lon in `[-180, 180]` (via `Field(ge=…, le=…)`), `country` normalised to uppercase ISO alpha-2 via a `mode="before"` `field_validator` (so whitespace and casing are tolerated before length checks fire), a `model_validator` that enforces the lat/lon paired invariant on `SiteCreate` and on `SiteUpdate` *only when both fields appear in the patch payload* (partial updates defer to the DB CHECK so the PATCH ergonomics stay clean), and a second `model_validator` on `SiteUpdate` that rejects explicit `null` for the NOT-NULL columns `name` / `kind` / `default_timezone` at 422 so the DB never sees the NULL and returns 500. `SiteModel.country` uses `CHAR(2)` to mirror the migration. `SiteResponse` and the TimescaleDB repository plumb all new fields through; the existing `update()` path needs no change because it already dispatches via `model_dump(exclude_unset=True)` + `setattr`. 34 new schema tests in `tests/unit/test_sites_structured_schemas.py` cover the kind enum, lat/lon range + paired logic for create + patch, country normalisation, a full-payload round-trip, and the explicit-null rejection (parametrized across `name` / `kind` / `default_timezone`, plus regression coverage that omission stays legal and nullable columns remain clearable); the existing `_site()` fixture in `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py` extended with the new defaults so the 10 service-level tests still pass.
- **Sprint 34 Categories backend — ADR 019 ratified.** Categories become a first-class tenant-scoped entity (gap 2.1 of the reference-design audit). New `categories` table via Alembic migration `037_categories.py` with `UNIQUE(tenant_id, name)`, `CHECK` on `category_type IN ('liquid_container','reference_tag','rti_container','object')`, `CHECK` on `required_tags >= 1`, RLS policy `tenant_isolation_categories`, and a backfill that creates one `category_type='object'` row per distinct `(tenant_id, asset_type)` already in `assets`. `assets` gains a nullable `category_id` FK (`ON DELETE RESTRICT`) backfilled to the matching new category by name; `assets.asset_type` is kept this release as a compatibility shadow (per ADR — drop in a later migration once UI + clients have switched). New router `src/tagpulse/api/routes/categories.py` exposes `GET /categories` (viewer+), `POST /categories` (editor/admin), `GET /categories/{id}` (viewer+), `PATCH /categories/{id}` (editor/admin; rejects `category_type` mutation with 400 — immutability is API-enforced per the ADR), and `DELETE /categories/{id}` (admin; 409 with `asset_count` payload if any asset still references it). All mutations audited (`category.created` / `category.updated` / `category.deleted`). Routes use the established current-tenant scoping pattern (`Depends(get_current_tenant)`) rather than the `/v1/tenants/{slug}/…` paths drafted in ADR 019 — see the route docstring for the deviation. ADR 019 status flipped Proposed → Accepted. `docs/adr/019-categories.md`.
- **`installer` user role (gap 2.6).** Joins the existing `admin` / `editor` / `viewer` set on `UserCreate` / `UserUpdate`. Pydantic-only change — the underlying `users.role` column is `String(50)` with no DB-level constraint. No new `require_role` callsites yet; the role is wired into authn so existing admin tooling can issue installer API keys. Higher-privilege site/zone-write paths follow in Sprint 38 when the Bridge/Gateway split lands. `src/tagpulse/models/user_schemas.py`.
- **`AssetCreate` / `AssetUpdate` external_ref validator (gap 2.8).** Rejects any of the URL-unsafe characters `. : / ? # \ [ ] @ , | & ! = $ ' * + ; %` (forbidden-character list pulled verbatim from the schema/API audit row 2.8). Empty / whitespace-only values normalise to `None`. Pydantic field validator; surfaces as 422 from the existing assets endpoints. 66 unit tests in `tests/unit/test_categories.py` covering all four `category_type` values, immutability of `category_type` on `CategoryUpdate`, `required_tags >= 1`, name/UPC length caps, the full per-character forbidden-char matrix for `external_ref`, and the four-role acceptance set for `UserCreate` / `UserUpdate`. The schema uses TagPulse's `tag` terminology throughout (see `docs/data-models.md` §"Where is the tag?").
- **Sprint 33 QW6 backend slice — per-tenant branding.** Three nullable columns on `tenants` (`logo_url VARCHAR(2048)`, `display_name VARCHAR(255)`, `brand_color VARCHAR(7)`) via Alembic migration `036_tenant_branding.py`, exposed through three endpoints in `src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_branding.py`: `GET /tenant/branding` (any authenticated role; current-tenant read), `PATCH /tenant/branding` (admin; PATCH semantics — explicit `null` clears an override; audited via `tenant.branding.update`), and the unauthenticated `GET /branding/{slug}` for the login page to skin itself before the user has credentials. Validation is format-only at the API: HTTPS-only logo URL, ≤2048-char URL, ≤255-char display name, `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$` brand colour. The deeper content-length / MIME-type check listed in §3.3 is deferred to the operator's upload/CDN tier (notes in the route docstring). 20 schema unit tests in `tests/unit/test_tenant_branding.py`. Pairs with the UI-only Light/Dark theme toggle and lands the full QW6 row of the sprint-33 quick-wins track.
- `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` — sprint-33 scope-lock for the external reference-design gap audits (schema/API + UI/IA notes held locally, not committed to this repo). Each ~25 gap forced to Commit / Defer / Drop with sprint slot. Backend: Categories (S34), Labels (S35), Sensing Events (S36), MQTT Connections (S37), Bridge/Gateway split + Connectivity Monitor (S38), Soft Assets (S39). - `docs/adr/019-categories.md` — Categories as a first-class entity (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 34). Unblocks ADR 021 scoping and the `categoryId` field in the outbound event envelope.
- `docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md` — Labels catalog + per-entity associations (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 35). Coexists with existing `metadata` JSONB rather than replacing it.
- `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md` — **revised to v2** during sprint-33 review. v1 proposed a parallel `sensing_event_configs` table; v2 extends `rules` (8 nullable columns + new `sensing.<event_type>.<trigger>` condition types) after recognising ~60% overlap with the existing `rules`/`alerts` surface. All four reference event types (Location/Geolocation/Temperature/Geofencing) ship in one Sprint-36 migration. Outbound envelope upgrade (`confidence`/`keySet[]`/`eventConfigurationId`/`categoryId`/`labels[]`) is dispatcher-layer and benefits all rules, not just sensing ones. v2 decision history recorded in the ADR's "Decision history" section.
- `docs/adr/022-soft-assets.md` — auto-create policy for unassociated reads in opt-in Locations + convert-to-asset flow (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 39).
- `docs/adr/023-outbound-connections-mqtt-kafka.md` — MQTT outbound dispatcher + Jinja2 body templating + per-connection rate-limit + integration Monitor endpoint (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 37). Kafka/Pub-Sub dispatchers explicitly deferred to backlog.
- `docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md` — indoor position estimation via multi-reader RSSI triangulation in grid-style sites (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 40). Surfaced post-audit by SME review of football-field-size deployments. Extends ADR 021 v2's `processor` enum with a third value (`trilateration`), adds `devices.position_x/y/z`, `sites.coord_system JSONB`, new `asset_positions` Timescale hypertable, and a `devices/{device_id}/status` MQTT topic for periodic reader-level status. Ships one reference algorithm (`weighted_centroid_log_distance`) behind a pluggable interface plus a first-class BYO-precomputed-positions ingest path so customers running Zebra Aurora / Impinj ItemSense / Mojix / RFcode RTLS can POST resolved fixes directly. Five of seven prerequisites already in place today (`tag_reads.signal_strength`, `tag_reads.reader_antenna`, `tag_reads.sensor_data`, `tag_reads.tag_data`, reader-side `telemetry_readings subject_kind='device'`).
- `scripts/mqtt_tap.py` — read-only in-VNet MQTT subscriber for triage. Run via `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> mqtt_tap.py -- [flags]` to inspect raw payloads the broker is delivering (default mirrors the worker's two topic filters: `tenants/+/devices/+/+` and `tenants/+/subjects/+/+/telemetry`). Supports `--tenant-id`/`--device-id` narrowing, `--duration` and `--max-messages` exit conditions, and JSON pretty-printing by default. Strictly observational — no DB writes, no state mutations. Pairs with `scripts/mqtt_canary.py` (publisher) and `scripts/azd-logs.sh` (worker-log tail).
- `scripts/tag_reads_near.py` — read-only in-VNet `tag_reads` inspector for triage "what landed near time T?". Run via `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> tag_reads_near.py -- --at <iso-ts> [flags]`. `--at` accepts any ISO-8601 timestamp with timezone (e.g. `2026-05-17T21:49:55Z` or `2026-05-17T14:49:55-07:00`); symmetric `--window` (default 5 min) or asymmetric `--before`/`--after` in seconds; optional `--device-id`/`--tenant-id` narrowing. Emits one JSON object per row to stdout (id, device_id, tag_id, timestamp, created_at, signal_strength, reader_antenna, epc_hex, tid, sensor_data, tag_data, lat/lng/accuracy/source) plus a one-line summary to stderr (count, earliest, latest, distinct devices, antennas seen). Useful companion to `mqtt_tap.py` for confirming what made it past the subscriber + ingestion path.
- `.githooks/pre-push` — blocks `git push origin main` from a clone that opts in via `git config core.hooksPath .githooks`. `scripts/start-sprint.sh` now sets this automatically; existing clones can opt in with the one-liner now documented in `CONTRIBUTING.md`. Bypass: `git push --no-verify`. Workaround for GitHub Free not supporting branch protection / rulesets on private repos.
- `docs/runbooks/github-workflows.md` — operator-facing catalog of every workflow in `.github/workflows/` (trigger, schedule, purpose, manual-run, failure triage). Linked from `docs/runbooks/README.md`.
- `docs/guides/contributor-workflow.md` — developer-facing guide covering branching, the sprint model (planning unit, not a branch), multi-PR workflow, CHANGELOG conflict resolution, and the release model (current continuous-deploy + future SemVer-tag flow). Linked from `CONTRIBUTING.md`.
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` — scheduled Mon–Fri 13:00 UTC (+ `workflow_dispatch`). Starts the dev PG Flex server if `Stopped`, restarts the active api revision to drain the stale asyncpg pool, runs `make doctor ENV=dev` as a sanity check. Closes the "every morning the dev env is dead" loop. Scope: dev only.
- `.github/workflows/dev-kv-cleanup.yml` — scheduled nightly 00:00 UTC (+ `workflow_dispatch`). Purges all entries from the dev KV `ipRules` and resets `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled` to match the Bicep baseline. Operators who ran `azd-grant-operator-kv.sh dev --allow-my-ip` and forgot to revoke get auto-cleaned. Scope: dev only.

### Fixes

- **Sprint 36 — auto-deploy backend to `dev` on every successful `main` build.** Closes the gap that left Sprint 34 (`d6dec19` categories) and Sprint 35 phases A/B/C/E (labels) un-deployed for a week: the user-visible symptom was the Categories page hanging ~5 s on every navigation because `GET /categories` returned 404 (the route was on `main` but the live `tpdev-api` revision was the May 9 image), and TanStack Query's default retry chain (1 s + 2 s + 4 s) only gave up after the third 404. Until now, `deploy-azure.yml` was `workflow_dispatch` + `v*`-tag only, so backend merges only reached `dev` when an operator manually triggered the workflow — which had not happened since 2026‑05‑10. The fix adds a third trigger on `workflow_run` after `build-and-push` completes on `main`: this guarantees the matching `sha-<40hex>` images already exist in ACR before the verify step runs (a `push: branches: [main]` trigger would race the upstream build). The job's `if` short-circuits when `github.event.workflow_run.conclusion != 'success'` so a failed build cannot deploy. `environment` and the concurrency group both default to `dev` on the new trigger (`inputs.environment || (github.event_name == 'workflow_run' && 'dev') || 'production'`), preserving the existing `v*`-tag → `production` and manual-dispatch → operator-picked behaviour, and keeping the per-env concurrency lock so a dev rollout cannot cancel a production rollout. `actions/checkout@v4` pins to `${{ github.event.workflow_run.head_sha || github.sha }}` because `workflow_run` otherwise checks out the default-branch HEAD at trigger time rather than the commit that produced the image being rolled out — without the pin, `scripts/azd-network-check.sh` and the other in-tree helpers would drift from the deployed code. The image-tag resolver gains a matching `workflow_run` branch that emits `sha-${TRIGGER_SHA}` (the full 40-char form `build-and-push.yml` already tags via `docker/metadata-action` `type=sha,format=long`); the existing short-SHA expansion path in "Expand image tag" is untouched. No new permissions or GitHub Environment variables required — re-uses the `dev` environment's OIDC federated credential already in place since Sprint 22 C4. `.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml`.

- `scripts/azd-logs.sh` — cap `--tail` at 300 (was 1000, which `az containerapp logs show` rejects with `--tail must be between 0 and 300`, breaking `make logs ENV=<env> SERVICE=<api|worker> SINCE=<duration>`). While here, surface that `SINCE` is *approximate*: `az containerapp logs show` has no time-based filter (only `--tail N` and `--follow`), so the script now emits a one-line stderr note when `SINCE` is provided. For true time-windowed queries, use `az monitor log-analytics query` against the env's Log Analytics workspace.
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `azd()` wrapper — extend the upgrade-nag filter to also strip azd 1.25's "Update available:" message (was leaking into command-substituted output and corrupting `RG` / `KV_NAME` / `ACR_NAME` in `azd-doctor.sh`, causing false reds for resource group, ACR, and KV).
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` — extend schedule to Mon–Sun (`1-7`) so the dev env is also warm for weekend on-call paging.
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` — fix cron expression: `1-7` is out of range for the day-of-week field (valid 0–6) and GitHub Actions silently disabled the schedule, so no scheduled wake fired on Sat May 16 or Sun May 17. Switched to `0 13 * * *` (every day) with a comment documenting the gotcha.
- `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` — probe `/health/ready` instead of the non-existent `/healthz` (was a false red).
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `aca_name` — fall back to ACI lookup for `mqtt` (current dev shape is `tp${env}-mqtt` ACI, not a Container App) so doctor reports its real state.
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `azd_env_resolve` — add `acrName` and `AZURE_ACR_LOGIN_SERVER`/`acrLoginServer` (FQDN-derived) fallbacks for `ACR_NAME` so the doctor's ACR-image check works without manually setting `AZURE_CONTAINER_REGISTRY_NAME`.
- `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` — KV-reachable yellow now prints the exact remediation command (`azd-grant-operator-kv.sh <env> --allow-my-ip`) instead of "firewall? RBAC?".
- `scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh` — fix `--allow-my-ip` against vaults with `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled`. The probe parser was looking for `Client address:` in the error, but PE-only vaults return `ForbiddenByConnection` with no client address; the probe returned empty and the script bailed before applying the firewall update. Now detects `ForbiddenByConnection` and falls straight to `api.ipify.org` instead.
- `docs/runbooks/db-failover-and-restore.md` §A1 — derive PG short name from `postgresFqdn` (azd env) instead of the non-existent `POSTGRES_SERVER_NAME`, which silently produced `--name ""` and hung the `az` call.
- `docs/runbooks/db-failover-and-restore.md` §A3a — document the api-revision restart needed to drain asyncpg's stale connection pool after the Flex server returns from `Stopped`.

### Earlier in Unreleased

- **Edge sim: explicit TLS knobs in `paho_smoke_publisher.py`** ([clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py](clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py), [clients/pi/README.md](clients/pi/README.md), [clients/pi/examples/.tp_paho_edge.env.example](clients/pi/examples/.tp_paho_edge.env.example)). Sprint 28 C6 opened `tcp/8883` on the dev broker but the smoke publisher had no `tls_set()` call, so pointing `BROKER_PORT=8883` at the broker silently hung at the TLS handshake (broker drops the connection because the client is sending raw MQTT bytes into a TLS listener). Added `--tls-ca PATH` / `TLS_CA=` and `--insecure` flags; TLS is auto-enabled when `BROKER_PORT==8883`. README now has a "TLS (port 8883)" section explaining that the dev broker's self-signed CA is **not** in the system trust store and must be distributed out-of-band.

- **CI: `deploy-azure.yml` now accepts short SHA tags** ([.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml](.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml)). `build-and-push.yml` tags ACR images with the full 40-char commit SHA (`type=sha,format=long`) but operators almost always have a 7-char short SHA in hand from `git rev-parse --short HEAD` or the GitHub UI. Passing `image_tag=sha-aeed4a4` previously failed at the verify step even though the image was sitting in ACR as `sha-aeed4a499b618e933f0caa05e524f204d9b3ce5b`. New "Expand image tag (short SHA → full SHA)" step probes ACR after Azure login and resolves any `sha-<4-39 hex>` prefix to its unique long-form match (errors with the candidate list if ambiguous). Verbatim tags (full SHA, `latest`, `v*`) continue to work unchanged.

- **Fix: MQTT subscriber crashed permanently on a single malformed payload** ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py), closes [#18](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/18)). One bad publish on `…/tag-reads` raised a `TypeError` out of `_handle_tag_read` (either `argument after ** must be a mapping, not list` for an array body, or `got multiple values for keyword argument 'device_id'` when the body carried its own `device_id`) and killed the subscriber task. The worker container kept reporting healthy while ingest was silently dead until restart. Three fixes:
  1. `_handle_tag_read` now accepts a single object **or** an array of objects, strips any body-supplied `device_id` (topic-derived id always wins), and per-element catches both `ValueError` and `TypeError` so one bad element only drops itself.
  2. The top-level `run()` loop wraps `_handle_message` in `try/except Exception` so any unhandled crash is logged and the loop continues consuming. `CancelledError` still propagates for graceful shutdown.
  3. `_run_mqtt_subscriber` in [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) is now a supervised reconnect loop with 1s → 60s exponential backoff so a transient failure (or any future regression that escapes the per-message guard) cannot take ingest fully offline.

  Regression coverage: [tests/unit/test_mqtt_subscriber_resilience.py](tests/unit/test_mqtt_subscriber_resilience.py) — five tests covering JSON list payload, single dict containing `device_id` (with assertion that topic-derived id wins), garbage bytes, JSON scalar, and a `run()`-loop test that verifies a handler `RuntimeError` doesn't stop subsequent messages from being consumed.
- **Docs: corrected MQTT `tag-reads` payload shape** ([docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md](docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md), [docs/design/edge-device-contract.md](docs/design/edge-device-contract.md), closes [#19](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/19)). The onboarding guide showed the HTTP `/tag-reads/batch` shape (`[{"device_id": …, …}]`) for the MQTT topic; literally following the docs triggered the [#18](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/18) crash. Now documents the canonical single-object shape (no `device_id` — derived from the topic), notes that the array form is also accepted, and adds an explicit "tag-read payload shape (MQTT)" subsection to the edge-device-contract spec.
- **Docs: deployment topology section in [README.md](README.md)** — new "Deployment topology (CI/CD vs local azd)" table clarifying that `build-and-push.yml` is registry-only, `deploy-azure.yml` is the canonical CI path that creates ACA revisions, and local `azd deploy` produces the distinctive `<app>--azd-<unix_ts>` revision suffix. Closes the documentation ask in [issue #17](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/17). Audit confirmed `build-and-push.yml` does not deploy — the 2026-05-09 07:49 UTC `tpdev-api--azd-1778312957` revision was a concurrent local `azd deploy`, not the workflow.
- **Docs: domain concepts 101 guide** ([docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md](docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md)). New plain-English primer for newcomers covering the seven primitives (Device, Tag, Asset, Product, Lot, Stock Item, Binding), why bindings have three kinds (`epc` / `tid` / `device`), where location lives (on the device, derived for everything else), the asset-tracking model (flat: asset ↔ point-in-time `asset_tag_bindings`), the inventory-tracking model (3-level: product → lot → stock_item with inline binding columns), and an end-to-end workflow comparison table mapping each step to its API call **and** UI screen. Cross-linked from [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md).
- **Edge sim: `drive_track.sh` learns `TAG_ID=...`** ([clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh](clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh)). When `TAG_ID` is set, each waypoint is published as a `tag-reads` message (with the lat/lon embedded under `location`) instead of a `/location` device-GPS update. This is what `asset_current_location`, the Data Explorer, and the Asset Path tab actually consume — pure `/location` messages only update `devices.last_lat/lon` and don't appear in those views. Without `TAG_ID`, behaviour is unchanged.
- **Fix: `GET /assets/{id}/path` returned 500** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py)). The merged-path SQL referenced `tr.reader_id`, which is not a column on `tag_reads` (the actual column is `tr.device_id`, as already used by the `asset_current_location` view in migration 024). Every call surfaced as `UndefinedColumnError: column tr.reader_id does not exist` and broke the **Assets → Path** tab in the admin UI for any asset with an active binding. Fixed by switching to `tr.device_id`. Added a unit-level regression assertion against `_PATH_SQL` in [tests/unit/test_asset_location.py](tests/unit/test_asset_location.py); the bug originally slipped through because every existing path test stubbed the repository.
- **Edge smoke publisher — movement simulation** ([clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py](clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py)). Added `--track PATH`, `--track-loop`, and `--track-interp HZ` for replaying a CSV waypoint file (`lat,lon[,accuracy,dwell_s]`) over a single MQTT session, with optional linear interpolation between sparse waypoints to produce smooth high-rate GPS streams. Sample track at [clients/pi/examples/tracks/boston-loop.csv](clients/pi/examples/tracks/boston-loop.csv). For shell-driven low-rate playback (one MQTT connect per point), added [clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh](clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh). Documented in [clients/pi/README.md](clients/pi/README.md) under "Simulating device movement".
- **Inventory simulator revamp — `scripts/simulate_inventory.py`** ([scripts/simulate_inventory.py](scripts/simulate_inventory.py)). Replaced the 3-SKU / shared-`LOT-A` / one-shot-reads scenario with a practical "Boston DC" warehouse: 1 site, 4 reader-bound zones (Receiving Dock / Cold Storage / Pick Floor / Shipping Dock) each with their own anchor reader, 4 distinct products with **distinct lot codes per product** (`VAX-2604-A`, `MILK-0501` near-expiry, `YOG-0428-B`, `CHS-0301-K`), and a finite pool of stock units with **stable SGTIN-96 serials** so re-runs update existing `stock_items` instead of inflating thousands of one-shot rows. Each unit follows a randomised per-unit timeline (Receiving → Cold Storage → Pick Floor → Shipping; ~30% stop in Cold, ~20% reach Pick, ~50% ship out), generating real `subject.zone_changed` events and ENTER/TRANSFER/EXIT rows in `stock_movements`. Reads are sent at the zone-bound reader for the unit's current stage so per-zone counts on **Stock Levels** reflect actual movement. Idempotent: re-running reuses the existing site / zones / devices / products / lots / mapping / stock items. New flags: `--units` (scale pool), `--tick`, `--seed`, `--duration` (replaces old `--devices` / `--interval`). [docs/quickstart.md §6c](docs/quickstart.md) rewritten with the new scenario; new [docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md §3b](docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md) example for running it via `scripts/azd-job.sh` against a deployed env (no `--api-key` needed; KV-injected).

### Fixed

- **`azd` shell wrapper silently swallowed command failures, breaking `make doctor`.** Two related defects in [`scripts/lib/azd-common.sh`](scripts/lib/azd-common.sh) + [`scripts/azd-doctor.sh`](scripts/azd-doctor.sh) caused `make doctor ENV=dev` to exit `2` with no error message even when the underlying `azd env select dev` had failed. (1) The `azd()` wrapper captured the exit status with `if ! out=$(command azd "$@" 2>&1); then local rc=$?; …`. Inside the body of an `if ! cmd; then` branch bash's `$?` is the *inverted* status — always `0`, because the shell only enters that branch on non-zero — so `rc` was silently `0` and every failed `azd` call was reported as success. Rewritten to `out=$(...); rc=$?; if (( rc != 0 )); then ...; fi`. (2) The trailing `[[ -n "$out" ]] && printf '%s\n' "$out"` made the function's exit status equal to the string-non-empty test, so a successful no-output call (e.g. newer `azd env select` versions) returned `1`. Replaced with an explicit `if` block and a final `return 0`. (3) `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` invoked `azd_env_resolve "$ENV_NAME" 2>/dev/null` to silence noise, but that helper calls `die()` on failure (which exits the whole script rather than returning), so the `else` branch printing a red status line was unreachable and operators got only `make: *** [Makefile:NN: doctor] Error 2`. Stderr is no longer redirected — the underlying error message now reaches the operator. Inline comments in both files document the trap so the obvious-looking refactor (collapsing back to `if !` or to `&&`) doesn't get reapplied. Pure shell change, no tests added (no shell test harness in this repo).

### Backend — Inventory gap-fill (B1–B4)

- **B1** `DELETE /lots/{id}` (admin only) — hard-delete with referential integrity check; returns 409 if stock items reference the lot.
- **B2** `POST /stock-movements` (editor+) — manual stock adjustment endpoint; supports `enter`, `exit`, `adjustment` movement types with required `reason` text; distinct from ingestion-driven movements.
- **B3** `DELETE /stock-items/{id}` (admin only) — hard-delete consumed/damaged items; returns 409 for `in_stock` unless `?force=true`.
- **B4** `PATCH /tag-data-mappings/{id}` (admin only) — update `semantic_field`, `tag_data_key`, `transform` fields.

- **A2** Product detail edit form (admin) — modal with name, sku, gtin, category, unit, attributes.

### Ops — `azd-job.sh` log-streaming fix (kills the `azd-kv-get.sh` flake)

- **Symptom.** `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev <secret>` (and any `azd-job.sh`-based wrapper) routinely returned `error: could not extract output from job log` for short-lived scripts (`get_kv_secret.py`, ~2s wall-clock). The wrapper waited 20 s then issued exactly **one** Log Analytics query — but Container Apps → Log Analytics ingestion lag is highly variable in centralus (typically 60–120 s, sometimes >2 min), so the query landed before the row was indexed and returned empty. Operators had to re-run with `--update-only` after a manual `sleep 90`. Made `azd-kv-get.sh` effectively unusable for interactive secret retrieval.
- **Fix — two-tier log fetch in [scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh).**
  1. **Wait for terminal status first** (5 s poll instead of 10 s) so we don't race a still-running container.
  2. **Try the Container Apps data-plane log endpoint first** — `az containerapp job logs show --execution <name> --container tools --format text --tail 300 --only-show-errors`. This hits the live-logs API on the ACA env and bypasses Log Analytics entirely; ~instant when it works. Strip the `<RFC3339> <stream> F ` prefix the data-plane format adds so callers get bare log lines (matters for `azd-kv-get.sh`, which greps between sentinels and pipes the value to `export FOO=$(…)`).
  3. **Fall back to Log Analytics with retry** — 12× 20 s poll (4-min cap) when the data-plane returns nothing (e.g. replica already garbage-collected on `--update-only`). Eliminates the single-shot race.
  - Net: `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev --list` and `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev <name>` now return clean output in <30 s for the live path, with a graceful fallback for stale executions.
- **`scripts/azd-kv-get.sh` — strip the wrapper's 4-space indent inside the sentinel block** ([scripts/azd-kv-get.sh](scripts/azd-kv-get.sh)) so `printf '%s\n' "$(echo "$PAYLOAD" | tail -1)"` returns the raw secret value, not `    <value>` with leading whitespace. Header comment updated to reflect the data-plane-first strategy.
- **End-to-end validated** against `tpdev`: `--list` returns the 6 KV secrets in <20 s; single-secret retrieval (`mqtt-broker-password`, 32-byte value) round-trips cleanly into a shell variable.
- **Backlog (Sprint 24+).** "Production-grade Bastion + jumpbox standard for staging + production envs" already on the [Sprint 23 deferred list](docs/roadmap.md#deferred-to-sprint-24) covers the structural alternative — laptop direct-to-KV access via a VNet-resident jumpbox — for operators who prefer Azure Portal "Show Secret Value" over the tools-job round-trip.

### Ops — In-VNet KV secret retrieval (`scripts/azd-kv-get.sh` + `scripts/get_kv_secret.py`)

- **Closes the corporate-proxy / WSL2 / Cloud Shell hole in `azd-grant-operator-kv.sh --allow-my-ip`.** The IP-allowlist path assumes a stable operator egress IP, but operators behind a corporate firewall (or running `az` from Azure Cloud Shell / an Azure VM) get a rotating SNAT IP from a Microsoft-owned pool, so each retry of `az keyvault secret show` fails with a different `ForbiddenByFirewall` client address. Allowlisting the entire pool is impractical and the network team won't hand it out.
- **[scripts/get_kv_secret.py](scripts/get_kv_secret.py).** Tiny tools-job-side script: `argparse` + `DefaultAzureCredential` + `SecretClient.get_secret(name)`. Reads `--vault` from `$TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` (which `tools-job.bicep` already wires in alongside `DATABASE_URL` etc.) and prints the value bracketed by `===KV_SECRET_BEGIN===` / `===KV_SECRET_END===` sentinels so the wrapper can grep it cleanly out of the streamed Log Analytics tail. `--list` enumerates secret names via `client.list_properties_of_secrets()` (bracketed by `===KV_SECRET_LIST_BEGIN===` / `===KV_SECRET_LIST_END===`) so operators don't have to guess.
- **[scripts/azd-kv-get.sh](scripts/azd-kv-get.sh).** Operator-facing one-liner: `export FOO=$(scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev tagpulse-test-corp-admin-key)` for retrieval, `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev --list` for the menu. Delegates to `scripts/azd-job.sh` with `--allow-stale` (the wrapper itself doesn't ship in the image; the script body does, as long as the image was built since this commit landed). Captures the streamed output, awks the value/names out of the sentinels, prints them to stdout. Exit-code propagation + full-log dump on failure. The script header now also documents the standard secret-name menu (Bicep-seeded `jwt-secret` / `postgres-admin-password` / `mqtt-broker-password` plus the smoke-setup `tagpulse-<tenant-slug>-{admin,editor,viewer}-key` pattern).
- **[docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md §3d](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) updated** — step 2 now leads with the tools-job route as the preferred path for Sprint 23-B-hardened envs, with the IP-allowlist fallback documented as "only if your laptop has a stable public IP", and inlines the secret-name menu + `--list` discovery command. The common-failures-table `ForbiddenByConnection` row points at both options with the corporate-proxy caveat called out.
- **No code in `src/`, no infra changes.** Reuses the existing tools-job UAMI's `Key Vault Secrets User` role and the existing `azd-job.sh` execution + log-tailing plumbing.

### Ops — Operator KV-access helper (`scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh`)

- **New [scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh](scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh).** Closes the operator-self-service gap that bit the first `tpdev` smoke run: after `smoke_setup.py --regenerate-key` pushed the rotated admin/editor/viewer API keys to KV, retrieving them from a laptop with `az keyvault secret show` failed twice — once on RBAC (`ForbiddenByRbac`), then again on network ACL (`ForbiddenByConnection / Public network access is disabled`). The api/worker UAMIs and the `tpdev-tools` UAMI receive their KV roles at provision time via [identity.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep), but Bicep deliberately doesn't pin a human principal so the same template works for any operator. The script handles both gaps in one call:
  - **RBAC mode (default)** — assigns "Key Vault Secrets User" (read-only) to the signed-in identity at the deployment KV scope. Idempotent; skips if the assignment already exists. Use `--role "Key Vault Secrets Officer"` for write access, `--principal <oid>` to grant a different principal (e.g. a CI service principal).
  - **Network-ACL mode (`--allow-my-ip` / `--revoke-my-ip`)** — flips `publicNetworkAccess` from `Disabled` (Sprint 23-B hardening default) to `Enabled` with `defaultAction=Deny` + the operator's current public IP added to `ipRules`. Net effect: private-endpoint traffic AND your one IP reach the data plane; everything else stays blocked. The corresponding `--revoke-my-ip` flips it back to fully private. Pairs with `--allow-my-ip` running RBAC in the same invocation so a fresh operator gets both in one shot.
- **Documented in [docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md §3d](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md).** Step 2 of the seed-demo-tenant flow now points at the script with both branches called out (open-network vs Sprint 23-B-hardened envs).

### Docs — Edge primer staleness audit

- **[docs/refs/edge-hardware-and-rfid-primer.md](docs/refs/edge-hardware-and-rfid-primer.md) — refresh "Still to land" list.** The primer claimed Sprint 14 telemetry/location wiring + `epc`/`tid`/`tag_data` fields, Sprint 16 token-revoke handling + conformance harness, and Sprint 17b client-side mTLS were all outstanding — every one of those landed in its named sprint. Replaced with a "Shipped since" block (with file links) and a tighter "Still open" list capturing the genuine remaining gaps: no `MqttTransport.update_token()` hot-swap, conformance harness doesn't yet exercise telemetry/location/token-revoke, and Sprint 17c broker-side mTLS rollout is still planned.

### Ops — `azd-job.sh` env-wipe fix + smoke_setup connection robustness + tools-job AZURE_CLIENT_ID

- **`scripts/azd-job.sh` — preserve env on container PATCH** ([scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh)). The wrapper sends an ARM PATCH to `properties.template.containers[0]` to override the container's `command` + `args` at start time. ARM PATCH replaces the container object wholesale (matched by `name`), so the previous body — which only set `name`/`image`/`command`/`args` — silently wiped every Bicep-declared env var on the tools-job (`DATABASE_URL`, `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL`, `TAGPULSE_API_URL`, `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME`, the lot). Symptom: `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py …` hit `[Errno 111] Connect call failed ('127.0.0.1', 5432)` because `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` wasn't there to override the local-dev default. PATCH body now round-trips the existing `env` + `resources` arrays via `jq`.
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py` — connect via component env vars when present** ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py)). Even with `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` restored, asyncpg's DSN parser blew up on the Flex Server admin password (`ValueError: invalid literal for int() with base 10: 's6oETxfj3tY9WL'`) because the Bicep-generated password contains URL-special characters. New `_connect_db()` helper prefers `POSTGRES_HOST` / `POSTGRES_USER` / `POSTGRES_PASSWORD` / `POSTGRES_DB` (already wired by [tools-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep)) as kwargs to `asyncpg.connect(..., ssl="require")`, falling back to `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` for local dev. Sidesteps DSN-encoding entirely.
- **`tools-job.bicep` — wire `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` so `DefaultAzureCredential` resolves the UAMI** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). After (1) and (2) above, `smoke_setup --regenerate-key` got all the way to the Key Vault push step and then died with `ManagedIdentityCredential: '(invalid_scope) 400, Unable to load the proper Managed Identity'`. The UAMI was attached, but the `azure-identity` SDK's managed-identity probe couldn't pick *which* identity to use. Fix: surface `identity.outputs.clientId` as a new `userAssignedIdentityClientId` param on the tools-job module and set it as `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` env var on the container. The api/worker are unaffected because they reach KV via ACA's `secretRef`-with-`identity` path (different code path) rather than the SDK.
- **End-to-end validated.** `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py -- --full --with-roles --with-subject-telemetry --regenerate-key` now succeeds against `tpdev` — provisions tenant + admin/editor/viewer users with KV-pushed keys, site + geofence zones, telemetry model, rules, Sprint 19 opt-in, Sprint 21 cutover probe.

### Docs — Deployment paths

- **[docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) — new "Deployment paths" section.** Documents the three distinct flows that put TagPulse on Azure (CI `build-and-push.yml` on push to `main`, `deploy-azure.yml` on `v*` tag / manual dispatch, and operator `azd up` / `azd deploy`) with a comparison table showing which flow builds images, which updates Azure, and which invokes the `azd` predeploy/postdeploy hooks. Captures the recurring confusion that follow-up PRs touching `scripts/azd-*.sh` (e.g. PR #15) do not auto-deploy — those hooks only run in the local operator flow.

### Ops — `azd up` hook fixes (follow-up to PR #14)

- **`scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh` — fix `get_azd` helper** ([scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh](scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh)). The previous shape (`azd env get-value KEY 2>/dev/null | tr -d '\r'`) silently captured `azd`'s "key not found" error text as the value, because `azd env get-value` writes that error to **STDOUT** (not stderr) and the caller only checked emptiness. The pg-ensure script's predeploy hook then tried to query `az postgres flexible-server show -n "$PG_FQDN%%.*"` with the multiline error string and exited 1 on every `azd up`. Helper now gates on the subprocess exit code (matches the working pattern already used in `azure.yaml`'s postprovision hook). Also adds a fallback to the canonical Bicep output name `postgresFqdn` when `AZURE_POSTGRES_FQDN` (an alias only set by `azd-network-check.sh` callers) is unset.
- **`scripts/azd-network-check.sh` — extract IP + soft-fail on ACA exec throttle** ([scripts/azd-network-check.sh](scripts/azd-network-check.sh)). Two changes: (1) `az containerapp exec` now prefixes its stdout with `INFO: Connecting to the container '<name>'...` (CLI 2.65+); the previous `tail -1` captured that line as the resolved IP, breaking the `^10\.10\.` regex assertion — replaced with `grep -Eo '([0-9]{1,3}\.){3}[0-9]{1,3}' | tail -1`. (2) The ACA exec websocket is aggressively rate-limited (HTTP 429) on back-to-back `azd deploy` runs, and a hard fail there blocked every subsequent deploy until the throttle cleared. Inside-VNet resolution failures are now WARN by default (one quick retry then continue); set `AZURE_NETWORK_CHECK_STRICT=true` to restore the hard fail on first VNet rollouts or CI smokes. The outside-VNet block check (KV public REST → 403) still runs unconditionally.

### Ops — Postgres auto-stop self-heal

- **New [scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh](scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh).** Idempotent: no-op when the Flexible Server is `Ready`, starts it (and polls up to ~5 min) when `Stopped`. Triggered by a real outage on `tpdev`: Burstable-tier (B1ms) Flex servers auto-stop after 7 days of inactivity, which silently 5xx's the entire backend — the api replica keeps running but every DB call fails (`asyncpg.exceptions.ConnectionDoesNotExistError` → `TimeoutError on asyncpg.connect`), `/health/ready` flips unhealthy, and ACA stops routing ingress traffic. Reads `AZURE_RESOURCE_GROUP` + `AZURE_POSTGRES_FQDN` from `azd env` (or plain env vars), derives the server name from the FQDN's first label.
- **Wired as `predeploy` hook in [azure.yaml](azure.yaml).** Ensures `azd deploy` self-heals before pushing new images, so the postdeploy migrations-job poll doesn't hang against a dead DB.
- **Runbook entry** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) common-failures table). Documents the `Stopped`-server failure mode (the symptom is "backend completely down" — easy to misdiagnose as ACA, networking, or app-level) plus the manual recovery: start the server, then `az containerapp revision restart` to drain the stale asyncpg connection pool.

### Sprint 26 — Audit remediation

- **D3 cherry-picked onto `main`.** The original D3 commit `948d358` ("`smoke_setup.py --key-vault-name` pushes keys to KV") was authored on the abandoned planning branch `sprint-26/ops-tooling-job` and never merged. PR #11's tools-job set `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` and granted `Key Vault Secrets Officer` to the workload UAMI on the assumption the script honored it; PR #12's runbook step "pull the rotated key from Key Vault" was therefore broken. Cherry-picked the D3 commit (script changes + `[azure]` extra deps in [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)) so the tools-job, the role assignment, and the runbook all line up with real code paths. ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py))
- **Runbook fix: `azd env get-value uiFqdn` → `staticWebAppHostname`** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) §3d step 4). `uiFqdn` is not an `azd` env output; the SPA hostname is exposed as `staticWebAppHostname` (matches §3a + §3b earlier in the same runbook). The drill would have failed at the manual-verification step.
- **Roadmap markers: Sprint 26 phases flipped `[planned]` → `[shipped]`.** Heading "(planned)" → "(shipped)"; A1 / A2 / B1 / B2 / C1 / C2 / D3 lines updated. D1 / D2 were already shipped from the previous PR.

### Sprint 26 — Tools-job validation (D1 + D2)

- **D1 — Post-deploy seed-tenant smoke section** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). New `### 3d — Seed the demo tenant + verify Tenant ID login` subsection between Phase 3c (operational scripts contract) and Phase 4 (CI/CD). Four-step drill: `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py -- --full --with-roles --with-subject-telemetry --regenerate-key`, pull the freshly rotated admin key from Key Vault (job's `--key-vault-name` default keeps plaintext out of Log Analytics), curl `GET /tenant/config` to confirm the api sees `Test Corp`, then verify the SPA Tenant ID login flow lands on the dashboard. Closes the Sprint 25 follow-up where the deployed SPA had no working tenant out of the box. Includes a fallback diagnostic (`az containerapp job execution list`) for the two known failure modes (KV Secrets Officer not yet propagated, tools-job in the wrong VNet).
- **D2 — CI smoke that the api image still imports `scripts/`** ([.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). New `Smoke — tools image imports scripts/` step, gated on `matrix.component == 'api'`, runs `docker run --entrypoint python <imageid> -c "import scripts.smoke_setup, scripts.simulate_devices, scripts.simulate_assets, scripts.simulate_inventory, scripts.benchmark_pg_metrics"`. Catches the failure mode where someone moves a script under a subdirectory or renames a module without updating the tools-job runbook. Required `load: true` on the `docker/build-push-action` step so the just-built image is available in the local daemon for the smoke (coexists with `push: true` on non-PR builds).

### Sprint 26 — Tools-job + wrapper (B1 + B2 + C1 + C2)

- **B1 — New module [`deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep).** Container Apps Job (manual trigger, `replicaTimeout: 1800` so `smoke_setup --full` + a slow simulator warm-up fit, `replicaRetryLimit: 0` since operational scripts aren't migration-style idempotent). Reuses the api image (Sprint 26 A1 baked `scripts/` into it) and the workload UAMI (so KV / ACR / Postgres access "just works"). Default command is a no-op import smoke (`python -c "import scripts.smoke_setup"`); `scripts/azd-job.sh` overrides command + args at start time. Env wiring matches `migrations-job.bicep` for `POSTGRES_*` + `DATABASE_URL`, plus three sprint-26 additions: `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` (raw asyncpg URL for `smoke_setup.py`), `TAGPULSE_API_URL` (in-cluster api FQDN), and `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` (so the D3 KV-push code path is the default inside the job — plaintext keys never hit Log Analytics).
- **B1 ride-along — Key Vault Secrets Officer on the workload UAMI** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep)). New role assignment so the tools-job can *write* secrets to KV (not just read them). Grant is on the same UAMI used by api/worker/migrations — slightly broader than strictly needed but avoids fragmenting the identity model. The api/worker code paths never call `set_secret`, so in practice only the tools-job exercises the role. Closes the D3 follow-up the previous PR called out.
- **B2 — Wired `toolsJob` into [`workload.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep) + outputs** ([deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep)). New module call (depends on `apiApp` for the FQDN, `kv` for the vault name, `postgres` for secrets). New `toolsJobName` output so `scripts/azd-job.sh` resolves the job from `azd env get-values` instead of hard-coding. Image points at `tagpulse-api:${imageTag}` — same tag as the api/worker, so `azd deploy api` keeps the tools-job in lock-step with the api's bundled `scripts/`. `az bicep build deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep` clean.
- **C1 — `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> <script> [-- <script args…>]`** ([scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh)). Resolves `toolsJobName` + RG from `azd env get-values`, patches the job's container `command` + `args` via `az rest` (the `containerapp job update` CLI doesn't expose them yet — preview gap), starts the execution, polls `properties.status` with a 30-min timeout, then tails Log Analytics filtered by `ContainerJobName_s` + `ExecutionName_s`. Distinct exit codes for usage (1), azd/auth failure (2), timeout (3), and non-`Succeeded` terminal status (4). `--update-only` skips the start and re-tails the most recent execution — recovers from terminal disconnect mid-run. Refuses to run with a dirty working tree or unpushed commits unless `--allow-stale` is passed (the job runs the *deployed* image, so local script edits are silently invisible until the next `azd deploy`).
- **C2 — New runbook [docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md](docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md).** Four worked examples (seed the demo tenant, rotate the demo admin key, push fake telemetry for a load smoke, re-tail after disconnect), an explicit "what NOT to run via the job" table (`load_test.py`, the workflow scripts, future destructive scripts), the stale-image gotcha, and a troubleshooting matrix covering the LA ingestion lag, the `Forbidden` case if the D3 role assignment didn't take, and the `ImportError: scripts.smoke_setup` case (image pre-dates A1).

### Sprint 26 — Tools-job image (A1 + A2)

- **A1 — `COPY scripts/ scripts/` in the base stage** ([Dockerfile](Dockerfile)). Single line after `COPY migrations/`; ~50KB image growth. The api / worker / migrations targets all inherit it (nothing in `scripts/` is invoked at startup, so no cold-start cost). Unlocks the planned `tools-job` (Sprint 26 B1) running off the same image — no separate "tools" repo, ACR push, or build pipeline. Implicit-namespace-package import (`python -c "import scripts.smoke_setup"`) verified locally; D2 will wire the same smoke into the GHA build.
- **A2 — Phase 3c "Operational scripts" runbook section** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). Documents the contract every "live-safe" script must satisfy (`TAGPULSE_API_URL`, `TAGPULSE_API_KEY`, `DATABASE_URL`/`TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL`, optional `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME`), classifies each existing `scripts/*.py` as live-safe (`smoke_setup`, the simulators, `benchmark_pg_metrics`) or local-only (`load_test`, the operator workflow scripts), and explains the laptop-vs-tools-job split. The next sprint-26 PR (B1+B2+C1+C2) will land the actual job + wrapper this section now points at.

### Sprint 26 — Device Developer & Operator Guide

- **New `docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md`** ([docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md](docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md)). Single landing doc for "I want to point a real RFID reader (or any sensor) at TagPulse." Combines the audiences ops + dev had to cross-reference between five separate files: an MQTT primer (broker model, QoS choice, LWT pattern), the topic taxonomy (device-keyed + Sprint 19 subject-scoped variants), payload examples for `tag-reads` / `telemetry` / `location` / `status` lifted directly from the Pydantic schemas, the HTTP fallback table, the reference Python edge client (`clients/pi`) snippet, the live `tpdev` cheat-sheet (api FQDN, MQTT FQDN, demo tenant UUID), an end-to-end laptop smoke (`smoke_setup.py` → `simulate_devices.py` → `GET /tag-reads`), and a troubleshooting table covering the silent ACL drop, clock-window rejections, token rotation semantics, and full-buffer loops. The doc explicitly defers to [docs/design/edge-device-contract.md](docs/design/edge-device-contract.md) as the authoritative wire spec rather than restating it — keeps the contract single-sourced.

### Sprint 26 — D3 (early): Key Vault push for `smoke_setup.py`

- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py --key-vault-name <vault>`** ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py), [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml), [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)). Promoted from "Sprint 27+ deferred" into Phase D3 because the Sprint 26 tools-job's stdout will land in Log Analytics with 90-day retention — printing plaintext keys there would create a leak path the runbook can't honestly recommend against. When the flag is set (or `$TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` is exported), each freshly issued admin/role API key is pushed to KV as `tagpulse-<tenant-slug>-<role>-key` via `azure-keyvault-secrets` + `DefaultAzureCredential` (lazy-imported so pure-local dev keeps working without the optional `azure` extra installed). The script's stdout shows only vault + secret name + version; the end-of-run `export TAGPULSE_API_KEY=…` line becomes `export TAGPULSE_API_KEY=$(az keyvault secret show --vault-name <vault> --name <secret> --query value -o tsv)` so an operator with `Key Vault Secrets User` can still pick the key up. `azure-identity>=1.19` + `azure-keyvault-secrets>=4.9` added to the existing `[azure]` optional-extra; the api image will pick them up when Sprint 26 A1 lands the `COPY scripts/` line. Bicep follow-up (the tools-job's MI getting `Key Vault Secrets Officer` on the env's vault) lands with B1 — until then the flag works from a developer laptop with `az login`.

### Sprint 25 — Hotfix: SWA CORS plumbing

- **`corsOriginsExtra` parameter wired through Bicep** ([deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep)). Sprint 24 A2 surfaced `Settings.cors_origins` in `/health/ready` but never passed an env var to the api Container App, so every cloud deploy ran with the dev default `http://localhost:5173` and the SPA's fetches got blocked by the browser. `workload.bicep` now feeds `'${corsOriginsExtra},https://${ui.outputs.defaultHostname}'` into the api module so the SWA hostname is auto-appended at provision time. The SWA module's `apiUrl` setting is no longer wired from `apiApp.outputs.fqdn` (would create a module cycle now that the api references the SWA hostname); the UI repo bakes `VITE_API_BASE_URL` at build time from `vars.VITE_API_BASE_URL` so the runtime app-setting was cosmetic anyway. Verified live against `tagpulse-dev-rg`: `/health/ready` reports both origins in `config.cors.allow_origins`.
- **SWA `azd-service-name=ui` tag** ([deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). The Phase D rotation cron filters `az staticwebapp list --query "[?tags.\"azd-service-name\"=='ui']"`; without the tag the lookup returned empty and the cron would silently no-op. Adds the standard `azd-service-name` tag the api / worker / migrations modules already use.

### Sprint 25 — Frontend Resilience & Observability (Phase A — backend health & CSP support)

> [docs/roadmap.md § Sprint 25](docs/roadmap.md). Phase A unblocks the UI repo's remaining slices: B5 (CSP report-only header in `staticwebapp.config.json`) needs A3 to ship first, and B3/B4 (deploy-time + post-deploy smokes) need a healthy api with the new `/health/live` contract.

- **A1 — `/health/live` SPA-polling contract** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py), [Dockerfile](Dockerfile), [.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). Body shape switches from the legacy `{"status":"ok"}` to `{"status":"alive","version":"<git-sha>","build_time":"<iso8601>"}`; `Cache-Control: no-store` is set on the response so the SWA edge / browser back-cache never memoize a stale "alive" (which would silently defeat the SPA's startup gate when the api goes down). Build identity is baked at image build time via the new `BUILD_VERSION` + `BUILD_TIME` Docker build-args; the GHA matrix populates them with `${{github.sha}}` and a UTC ISO-8601 timestamp computed once per job. Local `docker build` without `--build-arg` keeps the dev sentinels (`dev` / `unknown`). `/health` (no path suffix) is unchanged for k8s probes that pre-date `/live`.
- **A2 — CORS preflight max-age** ([src/tagpulse/core/config.py](src/tagpulse/core/config.py), [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). New `Settings.cors_preflight_max_age_seconds` (default 0; the strict-mode validator forces 600 in non-dev when left at 0, and explicit non-zero values from `CORS_PREFLIGHT_MAX_AGE_SECONDS` survive untouched). Wired into `CORSMiddleware`'s `max_age=`. Cuts 60–80ms off the first-paint-to-login-button latency on cold tabs by letting the browser cache the OPTIONS preflight result.
- **A3 — `POST /security/csp-report` endpoint** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/security.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/security.py)). Accepts both browser report shapes: the Chromium/Safari legacy `application/csp-report` envelope (`{"csp-report": {...}}`) and the Reporting API `application/reports+json` array of `{type, body}` envelopes. Emits a structured WARN log with `(client_ip, blocked_uri, document_uri, violated_directive, source_file, line_number, column_number, user_agent)` and increments the Prometheus counter `tagpulse_csp_violations_total{directive=...}`. Per-IP sliding-window rate limit at 10 reports / 60s — same in-process trade-off as the Sprint 22 A4 limiter; a multi-replica api may admit up to 10·N reports/min cluster-wide, which is fine for this endpoint. Open without auth (browsers don't send credentials on report POSTs by design); `/security/csp-report` is added to the tenant-keyed limiter's bypass list. Returns `204` on success, `429` when capped, and `204` (logged + dropped) on malformed JSON so a misbehaving extension cannot 500 the api.
- **A4 — Runbook update** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). `/health/live` smoke now asserts the new `{status, version, build_time}` shape + `Cache-Control: no-store`. New **§3b — SPA-vs-api consistency smoke** pulls `index.html` from the SWA, asserts `/health/ready` against the embedded api URL, and verifies the SWA hostname is in `config.cors.allow_origins` — catches the most insidious post-deploy failure (SPA built against a stale `VITE_API_BASE_URL`). New **§3c — CSP violation triage** documents the report shape, the Log Analytics KQL for top violations, and the triage priority order (`script-src` / `connect-src` are policy actually breaking the SPA; `img-src` / `font-src` are typically third-party extension noise).
- **Tests** — 13 new unit tests in [tests/unit/test_sprint25_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint25_phase_a.py) cover the `/health/live` contract (body shape, `Cache-Control: no-store`, latency budget, legacy `/health` unchanged), the CORS max-age policy in dev / non-dev / explicit-override paths, and the CSP-report endpoint across both report shapes, the per-IP rate limit, the no-auth contract, and the malformed-JSON path. `make check` clean (516 unit tests + 1 skipped, ruff + mypy green).

### Sprint 25 — Frontend Resilience & Observability (Phase D — operational + Phase E — multi-cloud follow-up)

> [docs/roadmap.md § Sprint 25](docs/roadmap.md). Phase D automates the SWA deployment-token rotation that Sprint 24 A1 wired by hand; Phase E promotes the Sprint 24 D3 portable-UI stub into executable recipes paired with a cross-cloud DR-drill walkthrough.

- **D1 — `scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh <env>`** ([scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh](scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh)). Runs `az staticwebapp secrets reset-api-key`, re-reads the new value, and writes it into the `9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI` repo's `<env>` GitHub Environment secret via `gh secret set --body -` so the token never touches a temp file. Prints the new token's last-4-chars for operator audit; the full token is written via the `gh` pipe and then dropped. Built-in 60-day idempotency gate (parses the JSONL audit log) refuses to rotate twice in quick succession unless `--force` is passed — the safety net against a manual rotation racing the cron. Mirrors the Sprint 24 A1 script's bash conventions (`set -euo pipefail`, `az`/`azd`/`gh`/`jq` preflight, `azd env get-value` capture). Audit log lives in `deploy/azure/.audit/ui-token-rotation.jsonl` (gitignored — local trail only; the GHA cron in D2 keeps the canonical record in run logs). Distinct exit codes for usage / pre-rotation auth failure (1), post-rotation `gh` failure (2 — operator must complete manually), and idempotency-gate refusal (3).
- **D2 — `.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml`** ([.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml](.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml)). Quarterly cron (`'0 9 1 1,4,7,10 *'` — 09:00 UTC on the 1st of Jan/Apr/Jul/Oct) plus `workflow_dispatch` with optional comma-separated env-list and `force: bool` inputs. Matrix runs D1 against `dev` / `staging` / `production`, each leg gated by the env-list input so a manual run can target a single env. OIDC-federated `azure/login@v2` per Environment using the `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` / `AZURE_TENANT_ID` / `AZURE_SUBSCRIPTION_ID` variables already wired by `scripts/azd-cicd-setup.sh` (Sprint 22 C4); the cron job re-hydrates the azd env from the live RG (looks up the SWA by `azd-service-name=ui` tag) instead of relying on persisted state. Cross-repo `gh secret set` uses a fine-scoped repo-only PAT (`UI_REPO_SECRETS_PAT`) — rotate it alongside the SWA tokens; the audit log captures last-4-chars on every run. On any matrix-leg failure, opens a GitHub issue tagged `ops` + `security` with the run URL and a manual-recovery one-liner.
- **E1 — `deploy/portable/ui/` executable recipes** ([deploy/portable/ui/README.md](deploy/portable/ui/README.md)). Promoted the Sprint 24 D3 structure-only stub into three concrete provider blocks: AWS S3 + CloudFront with the two-pass cache-headers split (hashed assets `public, max-age=31536000, immutable`; `index.html` `no-store, must-revalidate`) followed by a targeted CloudFront invalidation on `/index.html` only; Cloudflare Pages via `wrangler pages deploy ./dist --project-name=tagpulse-ui` (Cloudflare auto-provisions the project on first deploy and handles the cache-headers split itself); and GCP Cloud Storage + Cloud LB using the same two-pass pattern. New **Cross-cloud DR drill** section paired with the Sprint 22 D-3 backend DR runbook documents the full UI-failover path: fetch the `dist.zip` artifact from the UI repo's GHA build, rebuild against a backup-backend FQDN if the api hostname differs (`VITE_API_BASE_URL` is build-time-bound), run the upload recipe, and CNAME the user-facing custom domain to the backup CDN with a pre-staged TTL=60 record. Per-provider drill notes call out IAM scope (AWS), atomic-deploy semantics (Cloudflare), and edge-invalidation propagation lag (GCP). Real Bicep / Terraform for the AWS path is still deferred Sprint 26+ (gated on a real customer asking for AWS hosting).

### Hotfix — Azure MQTT broker reachability (`/health/ready` 503)

- **Emit `MQTT_BROKER_HOST` + `MQTT_BROKER_PORT` from Bicep** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep)). Pydantic `Settings` reads `MQTT_BROKER_HOST` / `MQTT_BROKER_PORT`, **not** `MQTT_BROKER_URL`; the Bicep contract was URL-only, so on Azure both the `/health/ready` TCP probe and the worker subscriber fell back to the Settings defaults (`localhost:1883`) and the readiness check stayed 503 with `mqtt: down (Connection refused)` even though the broker container was reachable from the Container Apps subnet. The module now derives `brokerHost` / `brokerPort` by stripping `mqtt://` / `mqtts://` from `mqttBrokerUrl` and injects both env vars into the api + worker container env (alongside the existing `MQTT_BROKER_URL` for forward-compat).
- **Mosquitto entrypoint chowns the generated password file** ([docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh](docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh)). When the entrypoint runs as root and writes `/mosquitto/config/mosquitto.passwd` via `mosquitto_passwd -b -c`, the file is owned by root and the unprivileged `mosquitto` user (uid 1883) cannot read it — broker exits with `Error: Unable to open password file ... Permission denied`. The script now `chown mosquitto:mosquitto` + `chmod 0640` the file after generation so the broker can start under its own uid.

### Hotfix — Azure PG Flex compatibility for TimescaleDB

- **Pin `postgresVersion` to `15`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep)). Azure Database for PostgreSQL Flexible Server **does not** ship the TimescaleDB extension on PG16 yet; `CREATE EXTENSION timescaledb` on PG16 silently drops the connection mid-statement. The Bicep default was `'16'`, so a fresh provision produced an unusable database. Pinning to PG15 (which is fully supported) is the only reliable path until Microsoft adds PG16 support.
- **Include platform `shared_preload_libraries` defaults when adding `timescaledb`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep)). The Flex Server `shared_preload_libraries` parameter **overwrites** the platform value rather than appending; setting it to `'timescaledb'` alone removes the platform-managed `pg_cron` and `pg_stat_statements` and leaves the server in a state where `CREATE EXTENSION timescaledb` again drops the connection. Value is now `'pg_cron,pg_stat_statements,timescaledb'` and the parameter has a long-form comment explaining the overwrite-not-append behavior.
- **Migration 031 is license-aware and idempotent** ([migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py](migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py)). Azure PG Flex ships TimescaleDB in **Apache-2** edition only; continuous aggregates (`CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW … WITH (timescaledb.continuous)` + `add_continuous_aggregate_policy`) are TSL-licensed and fail with `FeatureNotSupportedError: functionality not supported under the current "apache" license`. The `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds` column is now added with `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` so partial runs don't break re-execution; `current_setting('timescaledb.license', true) = 'apache'` short-circuits both `upgrade()` and `downgrade()` past the cagg DDL. Local Docker (TSL edition) gets caggs as before; Azure Flex skips them and the application falls through to live `time_bucket()` queries.
- **`TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository.aggregate()` falls back to live `time_bucket` when caggs are absent** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)). A process-cached `pg_class` probe (`_caggs_available`) detects whether `cagg_telemetry_1m` and `cagg_telemetry_1h` exist; when they don't, both the `bucket_seconds=60` and `=3600` paths route to the same live `time_bucket(make_interval(secs => :secs), …)` SQL the `else` branch already used. Apache-edition deployments serve `/telemetry/aggregates` correctly with no client-visible difference (the only cost is computing aggregates from the raw hypertable on each request).

### Hotfix — Azure deploy DATABASE_URL incompatible with asyncpg

- **Bicep `DATABASE_URL` switched from `?sslmode=require` to `?ssl=require`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/migrations-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/migrations-job.bicep)). Migrations job + api + worker all use `postgresql+asyncpg://...`; asyncpg's `connect()` does not accept the libpq query parameter `sslmode`, so the migrations job crashed with `TypeError: connect() got an unexpected keyword argument 'sslmode'` and the api revision never became ready (the readiness probe stayed 503 because the schema was never applied). Symptom: `curl https://${apiFqdn}/health/live` hangs because both revisions of `tpdev-api` are `ActivationFailed` with 0/1 replicas ready. Diagnosis path: Container Apps env Log Analytics → `ContainerAppConsoleLogs_CL | where ContainerName_s == 'migrations'` → traceback shows the offending kwarg. Fix is a one-character change (`sslmode` → `ssl`); both forms mean "TLS required" but only the latter is asyncpg-native. ARM template `deploy/azure/bicep/main.json` regenerated.

### Sprint 24 — Frontend cloud deployment (backend prerequisites + skeletons)

> [ADR-018](docs/adr/018-frontend-cloud-deployment.md), [docs/design/frontend-deployment.md](docs/design/frontend-deployment.md), [docs/roadmap.md § Sprint 24](docs/roadmap.md). Phases A/C/D land here; Phase B (the actual SPA shipping path) ships in [9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI).

#### Phase A — Backend prerequisites

- **`scripts/azd-ui-token.sh`** ([scripts/azd-ui-token.sh](scripts/azd-ui-token.sh)). Read-only helper that prints the Static Web App `apiKey` for env `<env>` to stdout via `az staticwebapp secrets list`. Refuses to print to a TTY without `--print` to keep the deployment token out of bash history / scrollback. Reads `AZURE_STATIC_WEB_APPS_NAME` + `AZURE_RESOURCE_GROUP` from `azd env get-value` using the same stdout-error-trap `get()` helper as the other azd scripts. A1.
- **`/health/ready` surfaces `cors.allow_origins`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py)). New `cors.allow_origins` array under the existing `config` snapshot; closes the most likely "SPA loads but every API call is blocked by CORS" failure mode by letting operators verify the SWA hostname is wired into the deployed api revision without shelling into the container. A2.
- **`static-web-app.bicep` audit pinned** ([tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py)). Test asserts no `apiKey`/`listSecrets` output and pins the exact output set (`defaultHostname`/`id`/`name`) so a future contributor can't accidentally land the SWA deployment token in `azd env get-values` or git-status traces. A3.
- **First-deploy runbook Phase 3a** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). New step between the smoke tests and CI/CD wiring: copy `staticWebAppHostname` Bicep output into `CORS_ORIGINS` in `deploy/azure/.env.<env>`, then `azd-env-load.sh <env> && azd provision` to push the new origin list into the api revision. Order matters — without this, the SPA loads but every fetch is rejected by the strict-mode CORS validator. A4.

#### Phase C — Operator documentation

- **`docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md`** ([docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md)). Six-phase checklist mirroring [azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md): prereqs → per-env bootstrap (UI repo) → first manual deploy → smoke tests → CI/CD wiring → production cutover gates. Top-N common-failures table, decommission recipe, cross-references to the SWA Bicep + token helper. C1.
- **README cross-links** ([README.md](README.md), [deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md), [docs/runbooks/README.md](docs/runbooks/README.md)). Both deployment-section READMEs now link to the UI runbook alongside the backend runbook; runbooks index updated with the new entry plus the previously-undocumented `azd-survival-guide.md` and `sprint-23-network-cutover.md` rows. C2, C3.

#### Phase D — Multi-cloud UI skeletons

- **`deploy/aws/ui/`** ([deploy/aws/ui/README.md](deploy/aws/ui/README.md), [deploy/aws/ui/main.tf](deploy/aws/ui/main.tf)). README with provider-mapping table (Azure SWA → S3 + CloudFront + ACM + Route 53), two-pass upload recipe (1-year immutable for hashed assets, no-cache for `index.html`), CORS-coupling note. `main.tf` is a `# TODO Sprint 25+` stub. D1.
- **`deploy/gcp/ui/`** ([deploy/gcp/ui/README.md](deploy/gcp/ui/README.md), [deploy/gcp/ui/main.tf](deploy/gcp/ui/main.tf)). Same shape (Cloud Storage + Cloud LB + managed SSL + Cloud DNS). D2.
- **`deploy/portable/ui/README.md`** ([deploy/portable/ui/README.md](deploy/portable/ui/README.md)). Provider-agnostic notes: the `dist/` bundle is identical across providers; only the upload command and the CORS allow-list differ. Cross-cloud DR appendix (one-line recipe per provider). D3.

#### Tests

- **`tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py`** ([tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py)). 11 static checks covering A1 (script exists + executable + TTY-guard + `--help`), A2 (`_config_snapshot` + parsing parity with the CORS middleware), A3 (no `apiKey` output + pinned output set), A4 (runbook documents `staticWebAppHostname` + `CORS_ORIGINS` + `azd-env-load.sh` + `azd provision`).

### `azd up` postdeploy hook robustness

- **Drop `az deployment sub show --name $AZURE_ENV_NAME` lookups** ([azure.yaml](azure.yaml)). Newer `azd` versions create the subscription deployment with a name distinct from `$AZURE_ENV_NAME`, so the per-output `az deployment sub show` calls in the `postdeploy` hook (and the ACR fallback in `postprovision`) failed with `DeploymentNotFound` after a successful image push. Hook now reads `migrationsJobName`, `keyVaultName`, `postgresFqdn`, `apiAppName`, `acrName` directly from `azd env get-value` (azd auto-promotes those Bicep outputs to env values during provision), via the existing stdout-error-trap `get()` helper. Same `azd up` deploy that previously tripped over the missing deployment now runs migrations + the network smoke end-to-end.

### Bicep `azd-service-name` tags on Container Apps + jobs

- **`workload.bicep` tags `apiApp`/`workerApp`/`migrationsJob`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). Each module call now passes `tags: union(tags, { 'azd-service-name': '<api|worker|migrations>' })`. `azd deploy` resolves which Container App to update by scanning Azure for resources tagged with the matching service name from `azure.yaml`; without this, `azd deploy` fails with `unable to find a resource tagged with 'azd-service-name: api'` after a successful `provision`. The common `tags` object is preserved (not overwritten) via `union()`.

### CI/CD onboarding scripts

- **`scripts/azd-cicd-setup.sh <env>`** + **`scripts/azd-cicd-verify.sh <env>`** ([scripts/azd-cicd-setup.sh](scripts/azd-cicd-setup.sh), [scripts/azd-cicd-verify.sh](scripts/azd-cicd-verify.sh)). Idempotent automation for Phase 4 of [docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md): creates the GitHub Environment, the Entra app + service principal, the federated credential (subject `repo:9owlsboston/TagPulse:environment:<env>`), the Contributor + AcrPush role assignments, and the 5 Environment-scoped variables (`AZURE_CLIENT_ID` / `AZURE_TENANT_ID` / `AZURE_SUBSCRIPTION_ID` / `AZURE_RESOURCE_GROUP` / `AZURE_ACR_NAME`). Verify script does a read-only drift check (exits non-zero on first failure). Replaces the manual `az ad app …` snippet that was previously copy-pasted from [deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md). Runbook Phase 4 updated to point at the scripts as the recommended path.

### Sprint 23 — Network hardening (in progress)

> ADR-017, [docs/roadmap.md § Sprint 23](docs/roadmap.md). Companion to the Sprint 22-C deploy; targets the corporate `Modify`-mode storage policy + the same-day KV `publicNetworkAccess` enforcement.

#### Phase A — Same-day mitigation (shipped)

- **Custom Mosquitto image, no Azure Files dependency** ([docker/mosquitto.Dockerfile](docker/mosquitto.Dockerfile), [docker/mosquitto.prod.conf](docker/mosquitto.prod.conf), [docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh](docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh)). New production image bakes the hardened conf (`allow_anonymous false`, `password_file /mosquitto/config/mosquitto.passwd`, persistence enabled) into `eclipse-mosquitto:2`; the entrypoint materialises the password file from `MOSQUITTO_USERNAME` + `MOSQUITTO_PASSWORD` at boot via `mosquitto_passwd -b -c` and fast-fails if either var is missing. Side-steps the corporate `Modify`-mode storage policy that silently reverted `allowSharedKeyAccess=true` and broke the Sprint 22 Mosquitto Files mount. Trade-off: broker retained-message persistence is lost across restarts (acceptable for v1 — devices republish on reconnect; obviated by Sprint 24 EMQX). A1, A3 of [Sprint 23 § Phase A](docs/roadmap.md).
- **`mqtt.bicep` rewritten without storage** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/mqtt.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/mqtt.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep)). Removed the `storage`/`fileService`/`share`/`configShare` block, `volumes`, both `volumeMounts`, the `mqttStorageName` workload variable, and the `mqttStorageAccountName` output from both workload and main. Module now takes `acrLoginServer`/`imageTag`/`userAssignedIdentityId`/`useImagePlaceholders` and attaches the existing UAMI plus an explicit `imageRegistryCredentials: [{ server, identity }]` block — ACI requires both for managed-identity ACR pull, a knock-on the design doc had missed. ACI placeholder image is `mcr.microsoft.com/azuredocs/aci-helloworld:latest` (different from the ACA placeholder). A2.
- **`scripts/azd-mqtt-build.sh`** + preprovision wiring ([scripts/azd-mqtt-build.sh](scripts/azd-mqtt-build.sh), [azure.yaml](azure.yaml)). New preprovision step (between `azd-kv-recover.sh` and `azd-image-check.sh`) builds `tagpulse-mqtt:$TAG` + `:latest` into ACR via `az acr build` (cloud-build, no local Docker). Skips cleanly on first provision when ACR doesn't exist yet, and skips when the tag already exists. Replaces the deleted `scripts/azd-bootstrap-mqtt.sh` (file-share seeding is no longer needed). A1.
- **`azd-image-check.sh` now gates on all four ACR repos** ([scripts/azd-image-check.sh](scripts/azd-image-check.sh)). Loops over `tagpulse-api`/`worker`/`migrations`/`mqtt`; placeholders only flip OFF when ALL_PRESENT=true so the new mqtt image participates in the first-provision handoff. A2.
- **First-deploy runbook updated** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). Phase 2 MQTT bootstrap section deleted; two stale common-failures rows replaced (entrypoint env-var fast-fail + first-provision placeholder-retry message); two callouts added (custom image build via `az acr build` + the `allowSharedKeyAccess` policy that mandates Phase A in subscriptions where it's enforced). A4.
- **Phase A test suite** ([tests/unit/test_sprint23_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint23_phase_a.py)). 11 static checks against the Dockerfile, conf, entrypoint, mqtt.bicep, image-check, mqtt-build, and the bootstrap-script removal. A5.

#### Phase B — VNet + private endpoints (shipped)

- **Per-env VNet + 3 subnets + 2 NSGs** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/network.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/network.bicep)). New module: `${namePrefix}-vnet` 10.10.0.0/16 with `aca-infra` (10.10.0.0/23, delegated to `Microsoft.App/environments`, NSG with `AzureCloud:443` inbound), `pe` (10.10.2.0/27, `privateEndpointNetworkPolicies: 'Disabled'`, empty NSG for audit), and `mgmt` (10.10.3.0/27, placeholder for future Bastion). Outputs `id`/`name`/`acaSubnetId`/`peSubnetId`/`mgmtSubnetId`. B1.
- **VNet-integrated Container Apps environment** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-apps-env.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-apps-env.bicep)). New `infrastructureSubnetId` param (default `''` = legacy non-VNet env, Sprint 22 behaviour preserved). When non-empty, the module sets `vnetConfiguration.infrastructureSubnetId` + `internal: false` (public ingress on the api stays — only egress is on the VNet; Front Door + WAF + private ingress is post-Sprint-23).
