The property is immutable post-create, so existing Sprint 22 envs require `azd down --purge --force` + reprovision (see runbook below). B2.
- **Generic `private-endpoint.bicep` module + 3 PE instantiations** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/private-endpoint.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/private-endpoint.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). One reusable module creates a `Microsoft.Network/privateEndpoints` resource in the `pe` subnet, a Private DNS Zone, a VNet link, and a `privateDnsZoneGroups` config so the PE NIC IP auto-registers. Workload instantiates it three times: `kvPrivateEndpoint` (zone `privatelink.vaultcore.azure.net`, group `vault`), `postgresPrivateEndpoint` (zone `privatelink.postgres.database.azure.com`, group `postgresqlServer`), `acrPrivateEndpoint` (zone `privatelink.azurecr.io`, group `registry`). B3, B4, B5.
- **Public network access toggle for KV + Postgres + ACR Premium bump** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/keyvault.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/keyvault.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/acr.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/acr.bicep)). KV: new `disablePublicNetworkAccess` param swaps `publicNetworkAccess` to `Disabled` and `networkAcls.defaultAction` to `Deny` when on. Postgres: same param wraps `network.publicNetworkAccess` and makes the `AllowAllAzureIPs` firewall rule conditional `if (!disablePublicNetworkAccess)` (the Postgres API rejects firewall rules when public access is off). ACR: new `enablePrivateEndpoint` param bumps the SKU from Basic to Premium (~$11/mo per env) because Basic SKU does not support PEs; `publicNetworkAccess` stays `Enabled` per ADR-017 (closing it is Sprint 24+ work — GHA hosted-runner pushes need it). New `output id` on Postgres so the PE module can target it. B3, B4, B5.
- **Two opt-in feature flags + safety guard** ([deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). `enableVnetIntegration` (env var `AZURE_ENABLE_VNET`) and `disablePublicNetworkAccess` (env var `AZURE_DISABLE_PUBLIC_NETWORK_ACCESS`), both default `false` so the Sprint 22 deploy path keeps working unchanged for envs without the corporate `Deny`-mode policy. Workload-level safety guard: setting `disablePublicNetworkAccess=true` *without* `enableVnetIntegration=true` would close the public KV/Postgres firewall *and* skip the PEs that replace them — bricking the env. The Bicep coerces the combination to "effective false" via a derived `disablePublicNetworkAccessEffective` var which is what every dependent module reads, and surfaces the actual decision via the new `disablePublicNetworkAccessEffective` deployment output. B3-5 + audit remediation.
- **Migration runbook** ([docs/runbooks/sprint-23-network-cutover.md](docs/runbooks/sprint-23-network-cutover.md)). Six-step cutover for an existing Sprint 22 env: set the two env vars, `azd down --purge --force` (ACA env recreate is destructive — KV state preserved by `azd-kv-recover.sh`), `azd provision`, `azd deploy`, verify Forbidden from outside + 10.10.x.x resolution from inside the api app, optional break-glass rollback path. Includes the "why this is a cutover, not a migration" callout (immutable `vnetConfiguration` property), a five-row common-failures table, and the safety-guard verification command. B6.

#### Phase C — Tooling & CI (shipped)

- **`scripts/azd-network-check.sh`** + postdeploy wiring ([scripts/azd-network-check.sh](scripts/azd-network-check.sh), [azure.yaml](azure.yaml)). New script (no-op unless both feature flags are `true`) confirms KV + Postgres FQDNs resolve to `10.10.x.x` from inside the api Container App — uses `python -c "import socket; ..."` instead of `nslookup`/`dig` because the slim Python container ships neither. Then asserts the public KV REST endpoint returns Forbidden. Wired into the `postdeploy` hook after migrations succeed. C1.
- **GHA smoke step** ([.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml](.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml)). New "Network smoke (VNet + private endpoints)" step (gated on `vars.AZURE_ENABLE_VNET == 'true'`) runs the same `azd-network-check.sh` against the deployed env, failing the workflow if a misconfiguration leaves clients hitting the public IP. C2.
- **Preflight `Microsoft.Network` registration** ([scripts/azd-preflight.sh](scripts/azd-preflight.sh)). When `AZURE_ENABLE_VNET=true`, the preflight now appends `Microsoft.Network` to the required RP list and auto-registers it (subject to the existing `--no-register` opt-out). No change for envs without the flag. C3.

#### Tests

- **Phase B test suite** ([tests/unit/test_sprint23_phase_b.py](tests/unit/test_sprint23_phase_b.py)). 40 static checks across `network.bicep`, `private-endpoint.bicep`, KV/PG/ACR toggles, ACA env VNet param, workload feature-flag wiring, the safety-coerced effective var + output, `main.bicep` + `main.bicepparam` env-var reads, `azd-network-check.sh` (executable + Python socket usage + flag guards), `azd-preflight.sh` Microsoft.Network registration, the postdeploy hook wiring, the GHA smoke step, and the cutover runbook contents (immutability callout + both env-var names + the `azd down --purge --force` invocation).

#### Audit + remediation

- **Sprint 23 plan tightened after audit** ([docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)). Reconciled four discrepancies between the roadmap entry and ADR-017 surfaced during a pre-implementation audit on the Sprint 23 branch: (1) Phase B feature-flag name normalised to `disablePublicNetworkAccess` (was `disableKeyVaultPublicAccess` in the roadmap), default `false` so opt-in (was `true`, which would have regressed Sprint 22 envs); (2) ACR firewall allow-list dropped from B5 — GHA hosted-runner egress can't be allow-listed cleanly, so closing public ACR is moved to the new "Deferred to Sprint 24+" item; (3) Phase A2 expanded with the actual `mqtt.bicep` knock-on changes (drop `mqttStorageName` var, drop `output mqttStorageAccountName`, add `acrLoginServer`/`imageTag`/`userAssignedIdentityId` params, add `imageRegistryCredentials` block — ACI requires this for managed-identity ACR pull) plus an explicit `git rm scripts/azd-bootstrap-mqtt.sh`; (4) Phase C tooling switched from `nslookup` to `python -c "import socket; …"` because the slim Python container doesn't ship `nslookup`/`dig`. Added Phase A5 (test plan) and a `make check`-clean acceptance criterion. ADR-017 D1 marked `[shipped]` (it landed on the Sprint 22-C merge).
- **Phase A/B audit gap remediated.** Initial Phase B implementation passed the two flags through to KV/PG/ACR independently. Audit found the brick scenario: `AZURE_DISABLE_PUBLIC_NETWORK_ACCESS=true` *without* `AZURE_ENABLE_VNET=true` would close the firewalls *and* skip the PEs. Fixed by introducing the `disablePublicNetworkAccessEffective` derived var as the single source of truth + a deployment output for visibility + a runbook callout + a unit test that asserts both the var and the output are present.
- **Post-implementation audit pass** (commit on PR #3). Four gaps caught + fixed: (1) `disablePublicNetworkAccessEffective` was emitted by `workload.bicep` but the runbook's verification command queries `main.bicep` outputs — `main.bicep` now re-exports the value with a usage-doc comment + a test asserting the propagation; (2) [deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md) hardening backlog still listed KV/PG private endpoints as deferred — split into a new "Shipped in Sprint 23" section + an updated "Deferred to Sprint 24+" section, and the Postgres SKU table row updated to reference the new flag (D2); (3) [docs/runbooks/azd-survival-guide.md](docs/runbooks/azd-survival-guide.md) common-gotchas table missing the `allowSharedKeyAccess` storage policy symptom and the KV `Forbidden` symptom that operators will hit post-Sprint-23 — added three new rows (storage policy → Phase A mandate, KV `Forbidden` → DNS check + dev/prod break-glass, network module subnet-delegation failure → cutover runbook pointer) plus the safety-guard tripwire (`disablePublicNetworkAccessEffective=false` after setting both flags = forgot to set `AZURE_ENABLE_VNET=true`) (D3); (4) Roadmap B7 "Bastion-or-jumpbox decision" reclassified `[shipped]` — the recommendation is captured in ADR-017 + the cutover runbook ((c) deploy-time toggle for dev, (a) Bastion in `mgmt` subnet for production), production Bastion provisioning itself stays in the Sprint 24+ backlog.

### Sprint 22 — Cloud Readiness

#### Phase C — Azure deployment (shipped)
- **First-deploy hardening hot-fixes** ([azure.yaml](azure.yaml), [scripts/azd-kv-recover.sh](scripts/azd-kv-recover.sh), [scripts/azd-image-check.sh](scripts/azd-image-check.sh), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam)). The first real `azd up` against a fresh subscription surfaced two chicken-and-egg failures that the design doc didn't cover, both now self-healed by `preprovision` hooks: (1) **soft-deleted Key Vault collisions** — KV names are globally unique and soft-delete reserves the name for 7–90 days, so a teardown + redeploy hit `VaultAlreadyExists`. `azd-kv-recover.sh` now lists soft-deleted vaults across regions, recovers same-region collisions in place, purges cross-region ones, and as a last-resort dodges purge-protection by setting a 4-char `AZURE_KV_NAME_SUFFIX` consumed by the new `keyVaultNameSuffix` Bicep param. The script remembers the active suffix to avoid bumping on every run. (2) **`MANIFEST_UNKNOWN` on first provision** — Bicep refers to `${ACR}/tagpulse-{api,worker,migrations}:${tag}` but those images don't exist before the first `azd deploy`. `azd-image-check.sh` now probes ACR and toggles `AZURE_USE_IMAGE_PLACEHOLDERS`, which the workload Bicep honours by swapping in public `mcr.microsoft.com/azuredocs/containerapps-helloworld` and `quickstart-jobs` images. `azd deploy` later replaces them via `az containerapp update --image …`. Both flags default to safe values and are no-ops on warm subscriptions.
- **`scripts/azd-env-load.sh` suppresses azd upgrade-nag spam.** azd re-emitted the "out of date" notice on every `env get-value` invocation, drowning the per-var loader output. The wrapper now collects the nag once and prints it at the end if seen.
- **azd 101 / survival guide** ([docs/runbooks/azd-survival-guide.md](docs/runbooks/azd-survival-guide.md)). Mental model (project / services / env), lifecycle command table, hooks (preprovision / postprovision / postdeploy) explainer keyed to TagPulse's three hooks, diagnostic cheat sheet (`azd env get-values`, `az deployment sub list`, `az containerapp logs show --follow`), and a top-N gotchas table covering the issues hit during Sprint 22 first-deploy. Linked from [docs/runbooks/README.md](docs/runbooks/README.md).
- **[ADR-017 — Network hardening](docs/adr/017-network-hardening.md)** (proposed, follow-up to ADR-016). Records the Sprint 23 plan: Phase A drops the Mosquitto storage-account dependency entirely (custom image, `MOSQUITTO_USERNAME`/`MOSQUITTO_PASSWORD` bootstrap) to side-step the corporate `Modify`-mode policy on `allowSharedKeyAccess`; Phase B introduces a per-env VNet, three private endpoints (KV / Postgres / ACR), and feature-flagged `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled` ahead of the same-day enforcement on KV. Roadmap entry under [docs/roadmap.md § Sprint 23](docs/roadmap.md).
- **Bicep IaC under [deploy/azure/bicep/](deploy/azure/bicep/)** — subscription-scope [main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep) + [main.bicepparam](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam) creates the resource group and delegates to [workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), which composes 10 modules: [acr](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/acr.bicep) (Basic, no admin), [keyvault](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/keyvault.bicep) (RBAC mode, seeds `jwt-secret`/`postgres-admin-password`/`mqtt-broker-password`), [monitoring](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/monitoring.bicep) (Log Analytics + workspace-based App Insights), [postgres](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep) (Flexible Server `Standard_B1ms` with TimescaleDB extension allow-list + `shared_preload_libraries`), [mqtt](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/mqtt.bicep) (single-node Mosquitto on ACI with Azure Files-backed config + data shares), [container-apps-env](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-apps-env.bicep) (Consumption profile, log-analytics destination), [identity](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep) (UAMI + AcrPull + KV Secrets User role assignments), [container-app](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep) (parameterized for api: external HTTP ingress + http-scaler 50 conc/replica + 3 probes vs. worker: no ingress + `WORKERS_INLINE=true`), [migrations-job](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/migrations-job.bicep) (`Microsoft.App/jobs` manual-trigger, 600s replicaTimeout), [static-web-app](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/static-web-app.bicep) (Free tier for TagPulse-UI). All KV-backed secrets resolved via UAMI; no app-side passwords in env vars. Phase C1.
- **azd v2 orchestration** ([azure.yaml](azure.yaml)). Three services (`api`, `worker`, `migrations`) targeting the matching Dockerfile stages with images pushed to ACR. **postprovision hook** captures `AZURE_ACR_LOGIN_SERVER` from the deployment outputs + sets `AZURE_IMAGE_TAG = git rev-parse --short HEAD`. **postdeploy hook** runs the migrations Container Apps Job and polls `properties.status` every 10s for up to 10 minutes — `Succeeded` exits 0, `Failed`/`Degraded` exits 1 — so api/worker revisions only roll after schema upgrade. Phase C2.
- **OTel → App Insights** ([src/tagpulse/core/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/core/telemetry.py), [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml), [Dockerfile](Dockerfile)). New `[azure]` extra pins `azure-monitor-opentelemetry>=1.6`; the build stage now installs `pip install ".[azure]"`. `setup_telemetry()` soft-imports `configure_azure_monitor` and uses it when `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING` is set, taking precedence over the OTLP exporter path. Non-Azure deployments are untouched (extra is opt-in at runtime via the env var). The Container Apps Bicep already wires `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING`, `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME=${appName}`, and `OTEL_RESOURCE_ATTRIBUTES=service.namespace=tagpulse,deployment.environment=production`. Phase C3.
- **CD workflow** ([.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml](.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml)). Triggers on `v*` tag push or `workflow_dispatch`. OIDC federates to Azure (no PATs); `production` GitHub environment gates manual approval. Verifies all three images exist in ACR at the target tag, runs the migrations job to completion (10 min timeout), then `az containerapp update` for api + worker. Final smoke test: 12 retries × 10s on `https://${api-fqdn}/health/ready`. Phase C4.
- **Build pipeline now dual-pushes to GHCR + ACR** ([.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). New `azure/login@v2` (OIDC) + `az acr login` steps run on push to `main` / `v*` tags only when `vars.AZURE_ACR_NAME` is set. The `docker/metadata-action` `images` input is now multi-line so the same build pushes to `ghcr.io/9owlsboston/tagpulse-{component}` and `${ACR}.azurecr.io/tagpulse-{component}` simultaneously. PR builds remain build-only (no push). Provenance attestation continues against GHCR. Closes the [ADR-016](docs/adr/016-multi-cloud-deployment-strategy.md) follow-up to make ACR the production image source-of-truth.
- **Deploy walkthrough** ([deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md)). Cost breakdown (~$40–50/mo idle), prerequisites, `azd up` flow, the **one-time Mosquitto bootstrap** (ACI cannot inject volume contents on first boot — `mosquitto_passwd` + `mosquitto.conf` upload to the `mosquitto-config` Azure Files share), smoke-test recipe with `scripts/smoke_setup.py --full`, CD env-var/variable contract, and the explicit hardening backlog (private endpoints, Front Door + WAF, EMQX, passwordless Postgres) deferred by design.
- **First-deploy checklist runbook** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). Six-phase sequential checklist covering prerequisites (CLI versions, RP registration, RBAC), per-env `.env.<env>` bootstrap, first `azd up` + MQTT broker file-share seeding, smoke tests (`/health/live`, `/health/ready` field-by-field, `smoke_setup.py --full`, App Insights traces, worker logs), per-environment CI/CD wiring (GitHub Environment + federated credential + role assignments + 5 Environment variables), and production cutover gates (backups, KV soft-delete, alerts, hardening-backlog review). Plus a top-10 common-failures table and a decommission recipe (`azd down --purge --force`). Linked from [README.md](README.md), [deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md), and [docs/runbooks/README.md](docs/runbooks/README.md). Closes Phase E2.
- **MQTT broker bootstrap automated** ([scripts/azd-bootstrap-mqtt.sh](scripts/azd-bootstrap-mqtt.sh)). Single-command helper replaces the 6-step manual snippet — derives RG + storage account from the selected azd env, reads `AZURE_MQTT_PASSWORD` from `deploy/azure/.env.<env>`, runs `mosquitto_passwd` via the `eclipse-mosquitto:2` Docker image, uploads `mosquitto.conf` + `mosquitto.passwd` to the `mosquitto-config` Azure Files share, restarts the ACI. Idempotent for password rotations. Runbook + deploy README updated to call the script (manual fallback collapsed under `<details>`).
- **Key Vault purge-protection now env-conditional** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/keyvault.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/keyvault.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). Hardcoded `enablePurgeProtection: true` was leaking the KV name for 7 days after every dev `azd down`. The module now takes an `enablePurgeProtection` parameter (default `true` so staging/production stay safe-by-default) and `workload.bicep` passes `appEnvironment != 'dev'`. Dev teardowns can now reuse the same `${namePrefix}-kv-*` name immediately.
- **`scripts/azd-preflight.sh` case-insensitivity fix.** Azure normalises some resource provider namespaces to lowercase (e.g. `microsoft.insights`), causing the script's case-sensitive `grep -Fxq` to flag them as missing even when registered. Now lowercases both sides of the comparison in both the initial check and the auto-register polling loop.
- **[ADR-016](docs/adr/016-multi-cloud-deployment-strategy.md) flipped to Accepted** with a Phase C implementation-notes section recording the UAMI-only identity model, ACI Mosquitto bootstrap caveat, OTel auto-detect path, and the GHCR → GHCR+ACR pivot rationale (cross-region pull latency + ACR Basic ≪ GHCR private storage at our image volume).

#### Phase B — Container & migration pipeline (shipped)
- **Multi-target Dockerfile** ([Dockerfile](Dockerfile)). Three production stages share one `build` + `base` layer and differ only in CMD: `api` (HTTP only, defaults `WORKERS_INLINE=false`), `worker` (MQTT subscriber + inventory/dwell/alert/analytics/webhook workers, defaults `WORKERS_INLINE=true`), and `migrations` (one-shot `alembic upgrade head` via `ENTRYPOINT`). A `default` stage aliases `api` to preserve `docker build .` back-compat. Healthcheck flipped from `/health` to `/health/live`. Phase B1.
- **`workers_inline` Settings flag + `lifespan` gate** ([src/tagpulse/core/config.py](src/tagpulse/core/config.py), [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). New boolean (default `True` for dev / single-container compatibility) controls whether the FastAPI process boots `RuleEvaluator`, `InventoryRuleWorker`, `DwellTracker` + `DwellWorker`, `AlertDeliveryService`, analytics modules, the `WebhookDispatcher`, and the MQTT subscriber task. `event_bus` and `usage_meter` always start because HTTP routes / SSE depend on them. Production cloud deploys set `WORKERS_INLINE=false` on the API container and run a sibling worker container from the same image. Phase B1.
- **`docker-compose.yml` mirrors the split** ([docker-compose.yml](docker-compose.yml)). New `worker` and `migrations` services; `app` now sets `WORKERS_INLINE=false` and depends on `migrations: service_completed_successfully` so local-up matches the cloud rollout topology.
- **Pre-rollout k8s migrations Job** ([deploy/common/migrations-job.yaml](deploy/common/migrations-job.yaml)). Provider-agnostic `batch/v1 Job` running the `tagpulse-migrations` image with `restartPolicy: OnFailure`, `backoffLimit: 2`, `ttlSecondsAfterFinished: 3600`. `DATABASE_URL` mounted from a `tagpulse-database` Secret. Same image + env-var contract is reused by the Helm chart (B4) and the Container Apps Job in Phase C. Phase B2.
- **GitHub Actions `build-and-push.yml`** ([.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). Matrix-builds `tagpulse-{api,worker,migrations}` from the matching Dockerfile targets via `docker/build-push-action@v6` with GHA build cache scoped per component. Tags: `sha` (always), `latest` (on `main`), `pr-{n}` (PRs, no push), version tags (`v*`). Build provenance attestation via `actions/attest-build-provenance@v1` pushed to GHCR. PRs build-only (no registry push). Phase B3.
- **Helm chart `deploy/common/helm/tagpulse`** ([deploy/common/helm/tagpulse/](deploy/common/helm/tagpulse/)). Provider-agnostic chart with templates: `api-deployment` (`WORKERS_INLINE=false` + readiness `/health/ready` + liveness `/health/live` + Prometheus pod annotations), `api-service`, `api-hpa` (CPU-based, default 2–10 replicas), `worker-deployment` (`WORKERS_INLINE=true`, `strategy: Recreate` so MQTT never double-subscribes, single replica until consumer-group support lands in Sprint 23+), `migrations-job` (Helm `pre-install,pre-upgrade` hook so api/worker only roll after schema upgrade), `serviceaccount`, `poddisruptionbudget` (api only — worker is single-replica today), and an optional `servicemonitor` for Prometheus Operator clusters (Sprint 22 E1). Shared env-var block in `_helpers.tpl` keys all secrets off a single `tagpulse-secrets` Secret (cloud overlays wire to Key Vault / Secrets Manager / etc.). Pod + container `securityContext` defaults to non-root, no-privilege-escalation, read-only-root-fs. Phase B4.

#### Tests
- **13 new tests + 1 opt-in render check** in [tests/unit/test_sprint22_phase_b.py](tests/unit/test_sprint22_phase_b.py): `workers_inline` Settings flag (default + override); static check that `main.py`'s `lifespan` branches on `settings.workers_inline`; Dockerfile declares `api` / `worker` / `migrations` stages, `api` defaults `WORKERS_INLINE=false`, `worker` defaults `WORKERS_INLINE=true`, `migrations` runs alembic; k8s migrations Job manifest parses with the right kind / restartPolicy / image; GHA workflow's `component` matrix is exactly `{api, worker, migrations}`; Helm chart `Chart.yaml` parses, all required templates exist, `values.yaml` defaults are sane, `migrations-job` template carries the Helm pre-rollout hook. The actual `helm template` render is opt-in via `TAGPULSE_HELM_RENDER_CHECK=1` to avoid snap/auth hangs in CI.
- **Full unit suite green at 440 tests** (was 427; +13 new). `make check` clean (ruff + mypy + pytest).

#### Phase A — Config & runtime hardening (shipped)
- **`Settings` strict-mode validator** ([src/tagpulse/core/config.py](src/tagpulse/core/config.py)). New `environment: Literal["dev","staging","production"]` field; `jwt_secret` and `database_url` no longer fall back to dev sentinels in staging/production; CORS wildcard `*` and blank entries rejected when `environment != "dev"`; `strict_migration_check` is forced `True` outside dev. Closes the "every cloud deployment shares the same JWT key if env var unset" foot-gun (Phase A1).
- **Explicit CORS methods/headers** ([src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). `cors_allow_methods` / `cors_allow_headers` are first-class `Settings` fields; the FastAPI `CORSMiddleware` now receives parsed lists instead of `["*"]`. Phase A2.
- **Geofence-flag startup WARN** ([src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). When `environment != "dev"` boots with `geofence_evaluation_enabled=False`, `lifespan` logs a structured WARN; the flag is also surfaced in `/health/ready`'s config snapshot. Phase A3.
- **In-process per-tenant rate limiter** ([src/tagpulse/core/rate_limit.py](src/tagpulse/core/rate_limit.py), [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). Token-bucket keyed on `(tenant_id, route_class)` with route classes `ingest` / `read` / `write` / `admin` and per-class globals in `Settings`. Bypass list for `/health`, `/metrics`, `/auth/login`, `/docs`, `/openapi`, `/redoc`. 429 response carries `Retry-After: 60` and a JSON body `{detail, route_class, limit_per_min}`. Closes the Sprint 15 / backlog "global API rate-limit middleware" deferral and removes the public-internet DoS surface flagged in the cloud-readiness review. Phase A4.
- **Per-tenant rate-limit overrides** ([migrations/versions/033_tenant_rate_limit_overrides.py](migrations/versions/033_tenant_rate_limit_overrides.py), [src/tagpulse/models/database.py](src/tagpulse/models/database.py), [src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py)). New `tenants.rate_limit_overrides JSONB` column accepting `{"ingest"|"read"|"write"|"admin": positive_int}`. `PATCH /tenant/config` validates keys + values, `{}` clears, audited via the existing `AuditLogger`, and on change the limiter cache is invalidated for the tenant via `RATE_LIMITER.invalidate(tenant_id)`. Phase A4.
- **`/health/ready` and `/health/detail` config snapshot** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py)). Both bodies now embed `config: {environment, max_ingest_payload_bytes, ingest_clock_enforce, geofence_evaluation_enabled, rate_limit_enabled, strict_migration_check}` so Container Apps / k8s operators can verify env-var wiring without shelling into the container. Phase A5.
- **`/health/live` alias** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py)). New liveness route distinct from `/health/ready` (DB + MQTT subscriber + migration-head check). Existing `/health` still returns liveness for backward compatibility. Phase A6.
- **Startup migration-version assertion** ([src/tagpulse/core/migration_check.py](src/tagpulse/core/migration_check.py), [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). `MigrationVersionMismatch` raised from `lifespan` when `alembic_version` ≠ code's `head` while `strict_migration_check=True` (forced outside dev). `expected_head_revision()` is `lru_cache`'d. `/health/ready` runs the same check. Phase A7.

#### Tests
- **19 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_sprint22_cloud_readiness.py](tests/unit/test_sprint22_cloud_readiness.py): `Settings` strict-mode (dev defaults preserved; production rejects dev secrets, wildcard / blank CORS; staging behaves like production; strict-migration-check force-set); `classify_route` for admin / ingest / read / write; `RateLimiter` token-bucket exhaustion, per-tenant isolation, override-supersedes-global; `rate_limit_middleware` bypasses `/health`, abstains without `X-Tenant-ID`, returns 429 + `Retry-After: 60` after the limit; `/health/live` and `/health` both 200; `expected_head_revision()` resolves to `>= "033"`.
- **Full unit suite green at 427 tests** (was 408; +19 new). `make check` clean (ruff + mypy + pytest).

#### Documentation
- **New [ADR-016 — Multi-cloud deployment strategy](docs/adr/016-multi-cloud-deployment-strategy.md)** records the three-layer topology (per-cloud IaC / portable Helm chart / portable `pg_dump --where=tenant_id` data layer), pins Bicep-on-Azure-first with Terraform-elsewhere, locks in the `tagpulse.storage.BlobStore` abstraction shape, and parameterizes the MQTT broker module so EMQX cutover stays a config flip. Status: Proposed (flips to Accepted on first cloud deploy).
- **Sprint 22 plan added to [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)** — 7 phases (A config hardening, B container/migration pipeline, C Azure Bicep + `azd`, D portable data layer, E observability, F AWS/GCP skeletons, G docs) closing all 12 cloud-readiness gaps from the pre-deploy review. Phase A complete; B–G remain `[planned]`.

### Sprint 21 — Subject-Scoped Telemetry: UI & Deprecation Sunset (backend)

#### Smoke / DX
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py --with-subject-telemetry`** ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py)). New flag opts the demo tenant into subject-scoped telemetry by adding `lot` and `stock_item` to `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds` via `PATCH /tenant/config`, then probes `GET /telemetry-models/_smoke_probe_device_type` and asserts the **Sprint 21 cutover to `410 Gone`** in the same run. Folded into `--full`. Without this opt-in, `simulate_devices.py --cold-chain` writes lot/stock_item readings that the cache layer skips and the Sprint 20 `lot.cold_chain_breach` rule never fires. Quickstart + user-guide updated to reference the shortcut.

#### Fixed
- **Migration 031 cagg-on-RLS-hypertable failure** ([migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py](migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py)). TimescaleDB rejects `CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW … WITH (timescaledb.continuous)` against a hypertable that has row security enabled (`cannot create continuous aggregate on hypertable with row security`). Migration 030 enabled RLS on `telemetry_readings`, so the cagg DDL in 031 failed on first apply. Surfaced when the dev DB at `029` was advanced past 030 — `python scripts/smoke_setup.py` then 500'd on `GET /tenant/config` because the partial 031 had already added `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds` (the `telemetry_subject_kinds` column shows up in the SQLAlchemy model but the cagg failure rolled the rest back). Fix: bracket the cagg DDL with `DISABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` / `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` inside the existing `autocommit_block`. Cagg queries in [src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py) already filter on `tenant_id` in the WHERE clause, so the caggs themselves do not need a separate RLS policy. Operators that hit the failure mid-migration before the fix should `ALTER TABLE tenants DROP COLUMN IF EXISTS telemetry_subject_kinds;` and re-run `alembic upgrade head`.

#### Removed (Sprint 18 deprecation sunset — closes ADR-015 §6)
- **`device_telemetry` SQL view + `telemetry_readings_legacy_device` hypertable dropped** ([migrations/versions/032_drop_legacy_device_telemetry.py](migrations/versions/032_drop_legacy_device_telemetry.py)). Migration also drops the `tenant_isolation_device_telemetry` RLS policy and the `ix_device_telemetry_lookup` Sprint 14 index. Pre-flight: `pg_stat_user_tables.idx_scan = 0` on the legacy index for the slowest tenant's full retention window, `grep -rn 'device_telemetry' src/` clean of code references (only docstring history remains), and no Grafana / external SQL clients pointing at the view. Downgrade re-creates the empty hypertable + RLS + view shells but **does not restore data** — documented as irreversible at the row level; rollback is restore-from-backup.
- **`TimescaleTelemetryRepository` removed** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)). Sprint 14's device-shaped surface (`insert_reading` / `query` / `quarantine` / `list_quarantine`) is now hosted directly on `TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository` alongside the subject-aware surface (`insert` / `query_by_subject` / `latest_per_metric` / `aggregate`). Single class, two clearly-headered method groups; callers (`TelemetryService`, `MqttSubscriber`, FastAPI dependency) swap the repository class without API changes. Protocol `TelemetryRepository` removed from [src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py); `TelemetryReadingsRepository` extended with the device-shaped method declarations.
- **`DeviceTelemetryModel` removed** ([src/tagpulse/models/database.py](src/tagpulse/models/database.py)). The Sprint 18-deprecated SQLAlchemy ORM mapping over the back-compat view is gone; `TelemetryReadingModel` is now the single in-memory model for telemetry rows.
- **`GET /telemetry-models/{device_type}` 301 redirect → `410 Gone`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py)). The Sprint 19 redirect to `/telemetry-models/device/{device_type}` was the documented one-window fallback; a 410 (kept on the route as `deprecated=True` so it still renders in the OpenAPI doc) carries the migration message and the target URL so legacy clients fail loudly with a fix-it-now hint instead of silently following the redirect into a deprecated code path that no longer exists.

#### Added (Sprint 19 carry-overs — closes ADR-015 §5)
- **`tagpulse.core.ttl_cache.TTLCache`** ([src/tagpulse/core/ttl_cache.py](src/tagpulse/core/ttl_cache.py)). Generic `TTLCache[K, V]` with `__slots__`, `time.monotonic` clock, FIFO eviction at `maxsize`, configurable `ttl_seconds`. Lazy expiry on `get` (no background sweeper). Used by both Sprint 21 telemetry caches; isolated for unit-testing the eviction / expiry semantics without standing up the application.
- **`tagpulse.core.telemetry_caches`** ([src/tagpulse/core/telemetry_caches.py](src/tagpulse/core/telemetry_caches.py)) hosts two module-level singletons:
  - `SUBJECT_KINDS_CACHE: TTLCache[UUID, tuple[str, ...]]` — replaces the unbounded `_TELEMETRY_SUBJECT_KINDS` dict in `IngestionService`. 30 s TTL, `maxsize=1024`. `invalidate_subject_kinds(tenant_id)` helper drops a single tenant's entry.
  - `LATEST_TELEMETRY_CACHE: TTLCache[tuple[UUID, str, UUID], list[LatestTelemetryEntry]]` — coalesces the `latest_per_metric` lookup on `GET /assets/{id}` and `GET /lots/{id}`. 30 s TTL, `maxsize=4096` (≈ 4 K assets/lots actively viewed concurrently per worker).
- **`AssetService.get_asset` and `InventoryService.get_lot` are cache-aware** ([src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py](src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py), [src/tagpulse/api/services/inventory_service.py](src/tagpulse/api/services/inventory_service.py)). The `with_latest_telemetry=True` path now reads `SUBJECT_KINDS_CACHE` for the per-tenant opt-in list and `LATEST_TELEMETRY_CACHE` for the per-subject `latest_per_metric` result; both repos are still consulted on miss. Cache-skip when the subject kind is not in the tenant's opt-in list — never store empty placeholders that would block a future opt-in flip.
- **`PATCH /tenant/config` invalidates `SUBJECT_KINDS_CACHE` for the writing tenant** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py)). The change-detected branch on `telemetry_subject_kinds` calls `invalidate_subject_kinds(user.tenant_id)` so the writing worker sees the new opt-in immediately; sibling workers converge within one TTL (≤ 30 s). ADR-015 §5 alternative (Redis pub/sub) was reconsidered and rejected — the wrong outcome on a flip is "operator waits up to 30 s", not data loss.

#### Tests
- **13 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_sprint21_caches.py](tests/unit/test_sprint21_caches.py): `TTLCache` get/set/expire (with `monkeypatch` on the clock attribute) / FIFO eviction at `maxsize` / `invalidate` / `clear` / argument validation; `invalidate_subject_kinds` drops only the target tenant; `AssetService.get_asset` returns the cached `latest_telemetry` on the second call (single readings repo + tenant repo round-trip); `LATEST_TELEMETRY_CACHE.invalidate` forces a re-fetch; opt-out tenants never populate the cache.
- **Sprint 19 test fixture updated** ([tests/unit/test_sprint19_subject_telemetry.py](tests/unit/test_sprint19_subject_telemetry.py)): autouse `_clear_caches` now imports `SUBJECT_KINDS_CACHE` from the new module and clears it (was clearing the deleted `_TELEMETRY_SUBJECT_KINDS`); the `…_legacy_path_redirects` test renamed to `…_legacy_path_returns_410` and asserts `r.status_code == 410` plus the migration hint in `detail`.
- **Full unit suite green at 408 tests** (was 395; +13 new). `make check` clean (ruff + mypy + pytest).

### Sprint 20 — Subject-Scoped Telemetry: Rules & Templates

#### Audit fix (Sprint 18/19/20 cross-sprint review)
- **Device-scoped writes now also publish `Topic.TELEMETRY_RECORDED`** ([src/tagpulse/api/services/telemetry_service.py](src/tagpulse/api/services/telemetry_service.py)). Initial Sprint 20 implementation only published from the three new paths (subject fan-out, HTTP `/ingest`, MQTT subject topic) — the legacy `TelemetryService.ingest_reading` and `ingest_location` paths still wrote `subject_kind='device'` rows to `telemetry_readings` (Sprint 18 routing) but emitted no event. ADR-015 §1 permits `subject_kind='device'` in `telemetry.threshold` rules, so the schema accepted the rule but no event ever matched — a silent contract gap. New `_publish_telemetry_recorded` helper publishes after every accepted write (best-effort; failure does not roll back the row). [tests/unit/test_sprint20_telemetry_rules.py::test_telemetry_service_publishes_telemetry_recorded_for_device](tests/unit/test_sprint20_telemetry_rules.py) is the regression. ADR-015 §2 updated to list four producers (was three).

#### Added
- **`Topic.TELEMETRY_RECORDED` event** ([src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py](src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py)) — published after every `telemetry_readings` row commit by all three producers: `IngestionService._mirror_tag_borne_sensors` ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py), `source="tag"`), `POST /telemetry/readings/ingest` ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry.py), `source="external"`), and `MqttSubscriber._handle_subject_telemetry` ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py), `source="external"`). The MQTT path collects `(row, metric_name, metric_value, unit)` tuples during the transaction and emits events in a second pass after `session.commit()` so subscribers can re-read the row through a fresh session.
- **`telemetry.threshold` rule condition type** ([src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py](src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py)) — new `TelemetryThresholdCondition` Pydantic model with fields `subject_kind` (regex-validated against `device|asset|lot|stock_item|zone`), `metric_name`, `operator` (`gt|lt|gte|lte|eq`), `value`, optional `subject_id` (UUID-as-string for per-instance pinning), and `cooldown_s` (default 300). `_RULE_CONDITION_PATTERN` extended to accept `telemetry.threshold`.
- **`RuleEvaluator.on_telemetry_recorded`** ([src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py](src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py)) — looks up active rules with `condition_type='telemetry.threshold'` for the event's tenant, runs the new module-level `_eval_telemetry_threshold(config, payload)` matcher (subject-kind gate → metric-name gate → optional pinned subject-id → numeric op vs. value), then applies a per-(tenant, rule, subject) cooldown via the shared `_RULE_COOLDOWN_UNTIL` table before creating a `severity="warning"` alert and publishing `Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED`. Subscribed in [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) next to the existing evaluator subscriptions.
- **Rule template registry** ([src/tagpulse/rules/templates.py](src/tagpulse/rules/templates.py)) — new `RuleTemplate` dataclass with two seed templates: `lot.cold_chain_breach` (subject_kind=lot, metric=temperature_c, op=gt, value=8.0, cooldown=900s) and `asset.high_temperature` (subject_kind=asset, metric=temperature_c, op=gt, value=60.0, cooldown=600s). Each template's `to_dict()` payload is directly POST-able to `/rules`; `requires_subject_kind` is a UI hint (the backend does not gate on tenant opt-in — non-opted-in subjects simply never fire `TELEMETRY_RECORDED`).
- **`GET /rule-templates` and `GET /rule-templates/{template_key}`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py)) — admin/editor/viewer-readable listing and single-template lookup; `404` on unknown key.
- **`scripts/simulate_devices.py --cold-chain` flag** ([scripts/simulate_devices.py](scripts/simulate_devices.py)) — provisions a synthetic milk product, lot, and stock item up-front (idempotent GET-then-POST against `/products`, `/lots`, `/stock-items`), then publishes drifting `temperature_c` readings via `POST /telemetry/readings/ingest` every `--cold-chain-period` seconds (default 10s). Drift formula `4.0 + cycle * 0.05 + jitter(-0.2, 0.4)` crosses the default 8°C threshold within a few minutes — enough to validate `lot.cold_chain_breach` end-to-end.
- **20 unit tests** ([tests/unit/test_sprint20_telemetry_rules.py](tests/unit/test_sprint20_telemetry_rules.py)) covering the pure `_eval_telemetry_threshold` matcher (subject-kind, metric, pinned subject_id, every operator), the full `on_telemetry_recorded` path (fires on breach, skips below threshold, per-subject cooldown isolation, metric-name mismatch silently skipped), schema validation (rejects unknown subject_kind, accepts via `RuleCreate`), and the rule-template registry (built-in keys present, round-trip into `RuleCreate`).

#### Documentation
- **New [ADR-015 Subject-scoped telemetry rules & Sprint 18 deprecation sunset](docs/adr/015-telemetry-rules-and-deprecation.md)** — explains why a *new* `telemetry.threshold` condition type was preferred over extending `threshold` (different event source — `TELEMETRY_RECORDED` vs `TAG_READ_CREATED` — preserves the Sprint 14 contract byte-for-byte), documents the in-code `RuleTemplate` registry trade-off (handful of templates expected, no per-tenant ownership model needed yet), records the per-(tenant, rule, subject) cooldown reuse of `_RULE_COOLDOWN_UNTIL`, and pins the deprecation-sunset deferral to a documented retention-cycle gate.
- **New [docs/runbooks/subject-scoped-telemetry.md](docs/runbooks/subject-scoped-telemetry.md)** — operator runbook covering tenant opt-in, rule authoring (template + by-hand), end-to-end validation with the simulator, and the Sprint 18 → Sprint 21 deprecation sunset checklist (preconditions, inventory, executed migration, rollback dump).

#### Deferred to Sprint 21
- **UI items** (subject picker on telemetry timeline, `telemetry.threshold` rule builder, template gallery, alert detail context, opt-in toggle) — live in the separate `TagPulse-UI` repo.
- **Sprint 18 deprecation sunset** (drop `device_telemetry` view + `telemetry_readings_legacy_device` hypertable, remove `TimescaleTelemetryRepository` + `DeviceTelemetryModel` from `src/`, remove the `GET /telemetry-models/{device_type}` 301) — gated on the slowest tenant's `telemetry_retention_days` window cycling past the Sprint 18 cutover. Runbook precondition checks documented above.
- **Cross-process `_TELEMETRY_SUBJECT_KINDS` cache invalidation** and **30 s server-side `latest_telemetry` cache** — Sprint 19 carry-overs that did not block Sprint 20.

### Database
- **Sprint 19 implemented — multi-subject telemetry ingest activated.** Migration [031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py](migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py) adds `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '["device"]'` (per-tenant opt-in for which subject kinds the ingest pipeline may fan-out into) and creates two TimescaleDB continuous aggregates over `telemetry_readings`: `cagg_telemetry_1m` (1-minute buckets, refresh last 2h every 1m) and `cagg_telemetry_1h` (1-hour buckets, refresh last 31d every 15m). Both are keyed on `(tenant_id, subject_kind, subject_id, metric_name, bucket)` and expose `avg`/`min`/`max`/`count`. Cagg DDL runs inside `op.get_context().autocommit_block()` because Timescale's `add_continuous_aggregate_policy` cannot run in a transaction. `downgrade()` removes the policies, drops both caggs, and drops the column.

### Added
- **`IngestionService` subject fan-out** ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py)). `_mirror_tag_borne_sensors` now resolves each tag-read into a list of `(subject_kind, subject_id)` tuples — `device` from `read.device_id`, `asset` via cached `asset_tag_bindings.get_active_by_value`, `stock_item` via `stock_items.get_active_by_binding(kind="epc"/"tid")`, and `lot` derived from the resolved stock item — then writes one `telemetry_readings` row per (resolved subject × tag-borne metric) with `source="tag"`. Strict opt-in: the tenant must list the kind in `telemetry_subject_kinds` (process-local LRU cache `_TELEMETRY_SUBJECT_KINDS`, bounded). Unresolved subjects log `telemetry.subject_unresolved` at INFO and skip silently — never an error. The legacy `TelemetryService.ingest_reading` device-row path is preserved byte-for-byte so the Sprint 14 contract is unchanged.
- **HTTP endpoints for subject-scoped telemetry** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry.py)):
  - `GET /telemetry/readings?subject_kind=…&subject_id=…&metric_name=…&start=…&end=…&limit=…` — subject-scoped time-series query.
  - `GET /telemetry/aggregates?…&bucket_seconds=…` — bucketed avg/min/max/count, served from `cagg_telemetry_1m` for `bucket_seconds=60`, `cagg_telemetry_1h` for `3600`, and a live `time_bucket(make_interval(secs => :secs))` over the raw hypertable for arbitrary widths. Returns `400` when `end <= start`.
  - `POST /telemetry/readings/ingest` — admin/editor-only direct write of pre-resolved external observations (TMS GPS, BMS temperatures, etc). Subject + metric + value all come from the validated `TelemetryReadingsBatch` body.
- **`GET /lots/{lot_id}`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/inventory.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/inventory.py)) — single-lot read endpoint, registered before the existing PATCH route to avoid path shadowing.
- **`GET /telemetry-models/{subject_kind}/{key}`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py)) — subject-scoped model lookup. Validates `subject_kind ∈ {device, asset, lot, stock_item, zone}`. For `device`, `key` matches the legacy `device_type`; for non-device kinds, only `subject_kind` filters (at most one row per tenant, per Sprint 18 schema).
- **MQTT subject topic family** ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py)) — subscriber now also listens to `tenants/{tenant_id}/subjects/{subject_kind}/{subject_id}/telemetry`. Subject identity is taken from the topic path, not the body, so a misrouted publish cannot smuggle a different subject. Writes via `TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository.insert(source="external")`. Helper `_parse_subject_topic` validates the 6-segment shape, kind whitelist, and both UUIDs.
- **Embedded `latest_telemetry` on `GET /assets/{id}` and `GET /lots/{id}`** ([src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py](src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py), [src/tagpulse/api/services/inventory_service.py](src/tagpulse/api/services/inventory_service.py)). When the tenant has opted into the matching `subject_kind`, the response includes up to 5 latest readings (one per metric) via a single `DISTINCT ON (metric_name) … ORDER BY metric_name, timestamp DESC` query — one hypertable scan capped to N metrics, not N round-trips.
- **`TenantConfig.telemetry_subject_kinds`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/tenant_config.py)) — admin-managed list literal of `device | asset | lot | stock_item | zone`. PATCH is per-field optional with audit diff entries.
- **Subject-scoped Pydantic schemas** ([src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py)): `TelemetryReadingIngest`, `TelemetryReadingsBatch`, `TelemetryAggregateBucket`, `LatestTelemetryEntry`. `AssetResponse` and `LotResponse` gain `latest_telemetry: list[LatestTelemetryEntry] | None = None`.
- **`TelemetryReadingsRepository` Protocol** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py)) — typed contract covering `insert`, `query_by_subject`, `latest_per_metric`, and `aggregate`.
- **Migration round-trip CI harness** ([tests/integration/test_migration_round_trip.py](tests/integration/test_migration_round_trip.py), [Makefile](Makefile)) — Sprint 19 carry-over of the Sprint 18 audit gap. New `make migration-check` target runs `alembic upgrade head → downgrade -1 → upgrade head` against a real TimescaleDB; gated on `TAGPULSE_INTEGRATION_DB_URL` so `make test` (unit only) stays hermetic. Catches the regression class that bit Sprint 18 (silent missing-drop in downgrade).

### Changed
- **`GET /telemetry-models/{device_type}` returns `301` to `/telemetry-models/device/{device_type}`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/telemetry_models.py)). Provides one release of overlap; the legacy path is removed in Sprint 20.
- **`TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository.aggregate`** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)) — selects between the two cagg tables and the live `time_bucket` path purely on `bucket_seconds`. SQL is composed with fixed identifiers (no f-strings around table names) to satisfy `ruff S608`.
- **DI factory `get_telemetry_readings_repo`** ([src/tagpulse/api/dependencies.py](src/tagpulse/api/dependencies.py)) — threaded into `get_ingestion_service`, `get_asset_service`, and `get_inventory_service` so the routes, the ingest pipeline, and the MQTT subscriber all share the same Protocol-typed repository.

### Deprecated
- `GET /telemetry-models/{device_type}` — sunset Sprint 20.
- `device_telemetry` SQL view + `telemetry_readings_legacy_device` table — sunset Sprint 20 once consumers have migrated to `telemetry_readings`.

### Documentation
- **New [ADR-014 Multi-subject telemetry ingest & API](docs/adr/014-telemetry-multi-subject-ingest.md)** documenting tenant opt-in via `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds` (deviation from the spec's `tracking_modes` extension), the server-side subject resolution table, the new HTTP and MQTT surfaces, the cagg materialization strategy, the `latest_telemetry` embed pattern, and the migration round-trip CI harness — including alternatives considered (client-side fan-out, single-row JSONB design, per-subject hypertables) and the Sprint 20 follow-up list.

### Roadmap
- **Sprint 19 marked done in [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)** — *Subject-Scoped Telemetry: Multi-Subject Ingest & APIs*. All 11 planned items shipped, with three documented deviations: (1) opt-in lives in a dedicated `telemetry_subject_kinds` column instead of extending `tracking_modes`, (2) the ingest endpoint uses `/ingest` not `:ingest`, (3) the 30 s server-side cache for `latest_telemetry` is deferred to Sprint 20 (a single `DISTINCT ON` query is cheap enough at current scale).

## Previously Unreleased — Sprint 18

### Database
- **Sprint 18 implemented — subject-scoped telemetry schema.** Migration [030_subject_scoped_telemetry.py](migrations/versions/030_subject_scoped_telemetry.py) introduces the new `telemetry_readings` hypertable keyed on `(tenant_id, subject_kind, subject_id)`, renames `device_telemetry` → `telemetry_readings_legacy_device`, back-fills every legacy row with `subject_kind='device'` / `subject_id=device_id` / `source='device'`, and recreates `device_telemetry` as a read-only SQL view over `telemetry_readings WHERE subject_kind='device'` so Grafana dashboards and ad-hoc psql sessions keep working. `telemetry_models` gains a `subject_kind` column (default `'device'`) with a CHECK that enforces `device_type IS NOT NULL` only when `subject_kind='device'`; the old `UNIQUE(tenant_id, device_type)` is replaced by `UNIQUE(tenant_id, subject_kind, COALESCE(device_type,''))`. `telemetry_quarantine` gains nullable `subject_kind` / `subject_id` columns. `downgrade()` round-trips: it copies any post-upgrade `subject_kind='device'` rows back into the legacy table before dropping the new schema.

### Added
- **`TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository`** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)) — new subject-aware persistence surface for Sprint 19 multi-subject ingest and the Sprint 20 rules engine. Exposes `insert(subject_kind, subject_id, …)` and `query_by_subject(...)`. `TelemetryReadingModel` (new SQLAlchemy mapping for `telemetry_readings`) and `TelemetryReadingResponse` (new Pydantic schema) added alongside it.
- **`TelemetryModelCreate.subject_kind`** ([src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py)) — telemetry model definitions can now target any subject kind. `device_type` becomes optional and is required only for the `device` kind (enforced by both the Pydantic `model_validator` and the DB CHECK constraint). Existing Sprint 14 callers omit the new field and get the default `'device'`, so all 3 unit tests in `test_telemetry_model_schemas.py` pass unmodified.

### Changed
- **`TimescaleTelemetryRepository` re-routed through `telemetry_readings`** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)). The Sprint 14 device-scoped public API (`insert_reading` / `query` / `quarantine` / `list_quarantine`) is preserved unchanged; internally every method now writes to and reads from the new `telemetry_readings` table with `subject_kind='device'`. Marked `@deprecated:: Sprint 18` in the docstring — to be removed in Sprint 20 along with the back-compat view. `DeviceTelemetryModel` similarly marked deprecated; it now maps to the SQL view rather than a base table.

### Documentation
- **New [ADR-013 Subject-scoped telemetry](docs/adr/013-telemetry-subject-scoping.md)** documenting the rename-not-drop migration strategy, the SQL-view-as-back-compat decision, the repository split, and the rollout plan tying Sprints 18/19/20 together.

### Roadmap
- **Sprint 18 (planned) added to [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)** — *Subject-Scoped Telemetry: Schema & Back-Compat*. Read-only sprint introducing the `telemetry_readings` hypertable, renaming `device_telemetry` → `telemetry_readings_legacy_device` behind a back-compat view, back-filling rows, and extending `telemetry_models` + `telemetry_quarantine` with `subject_kind`. Zero behaviour change — every Sprint 14 telemetry test must pass unmodified. Follow-on **Sprints 19** (multi-subject ingest + APIs) and **20** (rules engine + UI: Asset Telemetry tab, Lot cold-chain card, Assets-list temperature column) added to the backlog.

### Documentation
- **New design doc [docs/design/subject-scoped-telemetry.md](docs/design/subject-scoped-telemetry.md)** — long-term plan to evolve `device_telemetry` into a subject-scoped `telemetry_readings` hypertable keyed on `(subject_kind, subject_id)` where `subject_kind ∈ {device, asset, lot, stock_item, zone}`. Covers the data model (with backwards-compatible view), server-side subject resolution from `asset_tag_bindings` + `tag_data_mappings`, rules-engine extension, UI surfaces (Asset Telemetry tab, Lot cold-chain card), 3-sprint rollout plan, storage/perf analysis, and 4 alternatives considered. Motivating use case: cold-chain milk pallets with on-tag temperature whose telemetry today is keyed to the *reader* instead of the *lot*.
- **Corrected binding-uniqueness rule in [docs/user-guide.md](docs/user-guide.md)**: previous text claimed "only one active binding per asset at a time" — the actual schema constraint (unique index `ix_asset_tag_bindings_active` on `(tenant_id, binding_value) WHERE unbound_at IS NULL`) allows an asset to hold multiple active bindings simultaneously (e.g. EPC + TID, or a redundant backup tag). Uniqueness is enforced per `binding_value` per tenant, not per asset.
- **New "Where is the tag?" section in [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md)** answering a frequent new-contributor question: TagPulse intentionally has no first-class `Tag` entity — a tag is a *value* (EPC/TID/device-emitted string) resolved through three independent layers (`tag_reads.tag_id` event ledger, `asset_tag_bindings.binding_value` for asset attachment, `stock_items.epc` + `tag_data_mappings` for inventory decode). Includes the rationale (ingest throughput, context-dependence, rebindability), a "three questions" lookup table (current asset / product+lot / location history / manifest containment), and a sidebar-page → underlying-entities map for the UI.

### Added
- **Assets list page now shows live `Location` + `Last seen` columns** ([TagPulse-UI/src/pages/assets/AssetList.tsx](file:///home/velen/ws/TagPulse-UI/src/pages/assets/AssetList.tsx)). Previously the page had only `Name / Type / External Ref / Status / Updated`, where `Updated` was the asset row's `updated_at` (registration time) — so a brand-new tenant saw `5/4 8:18 PM` forever even while the simulator pushed thousands of reads. Now:
  - New backend endpoint `GET /assets/current-locations` exposes the existing `asset_current_location` view in bulk (`AssetService.list_current_locations` was already there but had no route). Wired *before* `/{asset_id}` so FastAPI doesn't shadow it. ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py))
  - New hook `useAssetsCurrentLocations` polls the bulk feed every 5 s; `useAssets` itself now polls every 15 s so binding-derived columns stay fresh too. ([TagPulse-UI/src/hooks/useAssets.ts](file:///home/velen/ws/TagPulse-UI/src/hooks/useAssets.ts))
  - Table now renders `Location` (lat,lng + source tag — `rfid` / `samsara` / `manual` / etc., per `latest_position_source`) and `Last seen` (relative time with absolute timestamp on hover). Renamed misleading `Updated` → `Registered` (it shows `created_at`). Sortable by Last seen.
  - One bulk request per refresh instead of N+1 per row, so the page stays cheap even with hundreds of assets.

### Changed
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py --regenerate-key` now rotates *all* role keys, not just the admin's.** Previously, `--regenerate-key` only touched `admin@example.com`; if you'd previously run `--full` (which provisions `editor@example.com` + `viewer@example.com`), you had to also pass `--with-roles` to rotate those, and the script silently skipped them otherwise. Now `_run` queries existing non-admin users in the tenant up front and includes them in the rotation/print loop unconditionally — so the single command `python scripts/smoke_setup.py --regenerate-key` reissues all three role API keys and prints all three. `--with-roles` still controls *creation* of the editor/viewer if they don't yet exist.

### Added
- **`virtual` zones now supported end-to-end.** The user guide had documented `virtual` as a third zone kind (admin-defined logical groupings — `Cold-chain`, `FDA-controlled`, `Critical assets`, etc.) but the API rejected it: `ZoneCreate.kind` was `Literal["reader_bound", "geofence"]` and `ck_zones_kind_payload` had no branch for it. Now wired through:
  - [migrations/versions/029_zones_virtual_kind.py](migrations/versions/029_zones_virtual_kind.py) relaxes the CHECK to allow `kind = 'virtual' AND fixed_reader_ids IS NULL AND polygon_geojson IS NULL`. Downgrade refuses if virtual rows exist (no silent data loss).
  - [src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py) `ZoneCreate.kind` Literal extended with `"virtual"`; the `model_validator` now rejects virtual zones that carry `fixed_reader_ids` or `polygon_geojson` (use the matching kind for those instead) so 422s come from the schema layer before hitting the DB CHECK.
  - Unit tests in [tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py](tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py) cover the happy path + both rejection cases.
  - **Recommended `Site.metadata` and `Zone.metadata` templates** documented in [docs/user-guide.md](docs/user-guide.md) (Sites & Zones section). Both fields existed in the schema since Sprint 15 but weren't surfaced anywhere.
  - **Recommended `Device.metadata` template** documented in [docs/user-guide.md](docs/user-guide.md) (Devices → Registering a New Device), aligned with GS1 EPCIS / CBV, OPC UA for Auto-ID (IEC 62541-100), W3C WoT Thing Description, Azure DTDL, and MQTT Sparkplug B. Includes an explicit "what does NOT belong here" callout pushing site/zone/lat/lon onto the Site and Zone entities to keep one source of truth for facility hierarchy.

### Fixed
- **Alert-name lookup helpers crashed when the session lookup raised** ([src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py](src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py)). The recently-added `_lookup_subject_name` and `_lookup_zone_name` helpers (which produce the human-readable alert messages) called `await session.execute(stmt)` without a `try/except`, so any session error propagated up and *suppressed the alert entirely*. The changelog entry for the original feature promised "fall back silently to the raw UUID on any miss" — now it actually does. Both helpers wrap the `execute` in `try/except Exception` and `logger.debug(..., exc_info=True)` on failure, falling back to the raw UUID. Side-effect: the 8 unit tests in `test_zone_rules_and_dwell.py`, `test_phase_e_inventory_rules.py`, and `test_geofence_pipeline.py` whose fake session classes only stubbed `commit()` now pass; they previously failed with `AttributeError: '_Session' object has no attribute 'execute'`. Cosmetic name lookups must never block the alert pipeline.
- **Occupants drawer was empty for geofence zones; reader-bound query referenced a non-existent column.** Two bugs in [src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py)'s `get_assets_in_zone`:
  - The single SQL hard-coded `z.kind = 'reader_bound'` in the join, so `GET /zones/{zone_id}/assets` against any geofence zone always returned `[]` even when assets were demonstrably inside the polygon (see Alerts page firing `Asset entered Bay Area West Block`).
  - The reader-bound branch joined on `tr.reader_id`, which doesn't exist on `tag_reads` (the column is `device_id`) — the query would have errored at runtime if anyone reached the reader-bound path.
  - Now branches on `zones.kind`. Reader-bound uses the corrected `tr.device_id` join. Geofence reads each asset's *current* position from the existing `asset_current_location` view (which already merges latest RFID + external per asset), bbox-prefilters in SQL, and finishes the point-in-polygon in Python with `tagpulse.geo.point_in_polygon` — the same helper the ingestion-time geofence eval uses, so the Occupants drawer and `Asset entered/exited` alerts can never disagree on "inside". Importantly the bbox filter is applied to the *latest* fix (not to the per-binding history), so once an asset crosses out of the polygon it disappears from the drawer on the next refresh instead of stale-pinning to its last inside-bbox read.
- **Geofence eval was skipped for fixed readers without a reader-bound zone** ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/service.py)). The point-in-polygon evaluation was previously placed *after* the reader-bound zone-change early returns, so for fixed devices that had no `zones.reader_id` row the early returns at `cache miss → seed and return` and `new_zone_id == prev_zone_id → return` would skip `_eval_geofence_for_subject` forever. Net effect: smoke-test setups with a geofence zone but no reader-bound zone never produced `zone.entered`/`zone.exited` alerts. Moved the geofence eval call before the reader-bound short-circuits so it runs on every GPS-bearing read.
- **Multi-user-per-tenant API key auth** ([src/tagpulse/core/user_auth.py](src/tagpulse/core/user_auth.py)). `get_current_user` was using `scalar_one_or_none()` on `api_key_prefix`, but every user in the same tenant shares the same 10-char prefix `tp_{slug:7}_`. Adding the second user (editor or viewer) caused all `/tenant/*` calls to return `500 MultipleResultsFound`. Now iterates candidates and verifies the full SHA-256 hash against each.
- **`MapPage` Rules-of-Hooks violation crashed the Map page** ([TagPulse-UI/src/pages/map/MapPage.tsx](file:///home/velen/ws/TagPulse-UI/src/pages/map/MapPage.tsx)). The `useMemo` for the colored teardrop `divIcon` was placed below the `if (lat == null) return null;` early return. On the first render `lat` was null → early return → `useMemo` never called; when location data arrived a tick later the hook count changed and React threw, blanking the page. Moved the hook above the early return.

### Added
- **Geofence eval force-enabled in dev environments.** Added `GEOFENCE_EVALUATION_ENABLED=true` to [docker-compose.yml](docker-compose.yml) (the `app` service) and to the `make run` recipe in [Makefile](Makefile) so the rollout flag (off by default in production until the bbox index is live, per [docs/design/geofencing-and-map.md](docs/design/geofencing-and-map.md) §10) is on locally. Without this, the smoke-test's `zone.entered` / `zone.exited` rules never fire and the Alerts page stays empty.
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py --full` — fixture provisioning expanded.** Four new opt-in flags populate every sidebar page with non-empty data and exercise role-based access:
  - `--with-zones`: creates one site (`Bay Area HQ`) and one geofence zone (`Bay Area West Block`, polygon covering the western half of the smoke-test walk box). If `Sim-Reader-*` devices already exist, also creates one reader-bound zone anchored to `Sim-Reader-01`.
  - `--with-telemetry-model`: defines the `rfid_reader` telemetry model (`temperature`, `humidity`, `battery_pct`) so the Telemetry page renders charts as the simulator pushes sensor_data.
  - `--with-rules`: creates a `threshold` rule on temperature (>30 C) and (when a geofence zone exists) `zone.entered` + `zone.exited` notification rules. Wandering simulated assets cross the polygon every few minutes, so the Alerts page populates within ~1 min of starting `simulate_devices.py --with-gps`.
  - `--with-roles`: creates `editor@example.com` (role `editor`) and `viewer@example.com` (role `viewer`) alongside the default admin, each with their own API key, so the UI's role gating and the API's 403 enforcement (Sprint 12) can be exercised end-to-end.
  - `--full`: shortcut for all four.
  - All idempotent: re-runs reuse fixtures by name and don't duplicate.
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py` — one-shot smoke-test bootstrap.** Idempotently brings a fresh local instance from "just-migrated" to "ready to push data and watch the Map" in a single command: upserts the demo tenant, upserts the admin user and (re)issues an API key, enables `asset` tracking via `PATCH /tenant/config`, and creates N assets bound to `TAG0001`…`TAG000N` so the Map populates as soon as `simulate_devices.py --with-gps` starts. Prints a copy-pasteable `export TAGPULSE_API_KEY=…` block plus the next-step command. Replaces ~5 minutes of manual psql + curl steps documented previously. Reads `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` (default `postgresql://tagpulse:secret@localhost:5432/tagpulse`) for the bootstrap DB writes.

### Changed
- **Alert messages now include human-readable subject + zone names** ([src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py](src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py)). `zone.entered` / `zone.exited` and `stock.unexpected_in_zone` alerts previously read e.g. `asset 0623a26d-… exited zone 8fc65810-…`, forcing operators to cross-reference UUIDs against the Assets and Zones pages. Now they read e.g. `asset 'Sim-Pallet-03' (bd814c23-…) entered zone 'Bay Area West Block' (8fc65810-…)` — name first for scanability, UUID kept in parentheses for unambiguous lookup. Added `_lookup_subject_name` (resolves `asset` subjects against `assets.name`) and `_lookup_zone_name` (resolves against `zones.name`) helpers; both are tenant-scoped and fall back silently to the raw UUID on any miss.
- **GPS simulator — vehicle motion + spread + smoothness** (`scripts/simulate_devices.py --with-gps`):
  - New `--motion {random,vehicle}` flag. `random` (default) is wide-angle wander (forklift idling); `vehicle` is mostly-straight runs with occasional 90° turns (delivery van / route).
  - Per-tag deterministic *home points* spread on a circle around the SF anchor, so 5 simulated assets stay visually distinct instead of collapsing to one cluster.
  - Round-robin tag selection per device (was `random.choice`) so every bound asset receives a steady cadence of reads — eliminates the visible "jumps" between sparse reads.
  - Step size bumped 1.5 m → 5 m and tether-boundary behavior changed from hard 180° reflection to gentle 30°/step steer toward home — motion is now visible at city zoom and the marker no longer flicks back sharply.
  - Constraint: `--tags N` was added so the random tag pool can match the bound-asset count (otherwise ~90% of reads fall on unbound tags and the Map appears under-populated).
- **UI — live Map markers**:
  - `useAssetCurrentLocation` was missing `refetchInterval`; markers fetched once at mount and never updated. Now polls every 5 s with a 4 s `staleTime`. ([TagPulse-UI/src/hooks/useAssets.ts](file:///home/velen/ws/TagPulse-UI/src/hooks/useAssets.ts))
  - Replaced the default Leaflet blue pin with a per-asset color-coded teardrop `divIcon` cycling through the existing 6-color `PATH_COLORS` palette so multiple assets in the same area stay visually distinct. ([TagPulse-UI/src/pages/map/MapPage.tsx](file:///home/velen/ws/TagPulse-UI/src/pages/map/MapPage.tsx))
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py` — auto-heal binding collisions.** When an earlier smoke run left a `TAGxxxx` bound to a different (now-stale) asset, the script previously failed with `409 binding_value 'TAG0001' is already actively bound`. It now finds the holder, unbinds it, and rebinds to the correct `Sim-Pallet-NN` automatically.
- **GPS simulator anchor moved Seattle → San Francisco** (`scripts/simulate_devices.py --with-gps`). New random-walk anchor: `37.7749, -122.4194` (~110 m radius). Per-product feedback that Bay Area is more iconic for demos.
- **Docs — smoke-test workflow rewrite**: [docs/quickstart.md](docs/quickstart.md) §6b now leads with the new two-script smoke test (`smoke_setup.py` + `simulate_devices.py --with-gps`), demoting the manual UI/curl asset-and-binding steps. All Seattle coordinates updated to San Francisco. Added "Create Asset button missing" to the troubleshooting table (root cause: tracking_modes not enabled — fixed by re-running `smoke_setup.py`).
- **Docs — live-map walkthrough**: expanded `6b. Asset Tracking Smoke Test → Option B` in [docs/quickstart.md](docs/quickstart.md) into a 6-step walkthrough (start `--with-gps` simulator, bind synthetic tags to assets via UI **and** API one-shot loop, watch markers in Seattle anchor block, replay via time slider / Path tab, draw a geofence + zone-entered rule, API verification + troubleshooting table). Clarified in Option A that reader-bound zones also produce map markers (snapped to reader positions). Calls out the common gotcha that `--with-gps` alone produces tag reads but no markers until tags are bound to assets.
- **Simulator scripts now accept Bearer API keys** — `scripts/simulate_devices.py`, `scripts/simulate_assets.py`, `scripts/simulate_inventory.py`, and `scripts/load_test.py` gained a `--api-key` option (falls back to `$TAGPULSE_API_KEY`). Required since Sprint 12 made `POST /device-registry`, `POST /assets`, `POST /products`, etc. editor-or-admin only — a bare `X-Tenant-ID` header now authenticates as viewer and got a `403 Requires role: admin, editor` response from the simulators. Scripts print a `WARNING` when no key is configured. Documented in [docs/quickstart.md](docs/quickstart.md) §6/6b/6c/Load Testing option tables.
- **Docs — asset-tracking smoke test**: added new section `6b. Asset Tracking Smoke Test` to [docs/quickstart.md](docs/quickstart.md) covering the three position sources (`rfid` reader-bound, `gps` embedded via `simulate_devices.py --with-gps`, and `external` via `POST /assets/{id}/external-position`), plus `simulate_assets.py` flag reference. Added a cross-link callout under Step 7 of [docs/user-guide.md](docs/user-guide.md). Documented `--with-gps` in the device-simulator options table.
- **Docs — inventory-tracking smoke test**: added new section `6c. Inventory Tracking Smoke Test` to [docs/quickstart.md](docs/quickstart.md) covering `simulate_inventory.py` (catalog seed, near-expiry lots, `lot_code` tag-data mapping, SGTIN-96 stream), with UI/API verification steps and a sample `stock.expiring_within` rule to exercise alerting. Added a matching callout under Step 7 of [docs/user-guide.md](docs/user-guide.md).
- **Docs audit refresh** — brought reference docs in line with shipped Sprint 14–17b state:
  - `docs/data-models.md`: rewrote the Migrations table to cover 016–028 with concrete descriptions; stripped 82 stale `(planned, Sprint X)` markers from table cells, section headers and migration footers; added missing tables (`external_locations`, `tag_data_mappings`, `subject_current_zone`); added `parent_stock_item_id` row to `stock_items`; refreshed RLS table; added migration footers for `tenants` (017/023/026), `devices` (017/025/026) and `zones` (017/026).
  - `docs/architecture.md`: expanded Storage table from 5 to 19 tables; added Geofencing & Map and Device Identity component sections; refreshed Admin UI capabilities; added ADR-011 / ADR-012 to the Key Decisions table; refreshed project-structure tree to include `services/`, `geo/`, `rfid/`, `workers/`.
  - `docs/quickstart.md`: replaced "Bearer tokens from Sprint 12" with a pointer to the Bearer-API-key bootstrap step.
